1001 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Futrell v. Wagner


CA No. A47302


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


96 Ore. App. 27; 771 P.2d 292; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 383


November 16, 1988, Argued and submitted  
April 5, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Futrell's Reconsideration and Wagner's Reconsideration Denied May 12, 1989. Both Petitions for Review Denied June 27, 1989 (308 Or 158).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Clackamas County. William W. Wells, Senior Judge. No. 85-1-280.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff vendors brought a declaratory judgment action, seeking a declaration that they owned the vendors' interest under a land sale contract. The Circuit Court, Clackamas County (Oregon), entered a judgment in favor of defendant sureties. The vendors appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the vendors owned a vendors' interest in a land contract, which they assigned to a creditor as security for a guarantee on a corporate loan. Later a third party loaned the creditor and the corporation a sum, which the creditor secured by assigning his assignee's interest in the land contract. The sureties guaranteed that second loan. When the creditor and the corporation defaulted on the second loan, the creditor, the corporation, and the sureties were all sued. The sureties settled the lawsuit and obtained an assignment of the note on the second loan and of the third party's right, title, and interest in the land contract. The court concluded that the sureties were not the owners of the vendors' interest in the land contract because the third party had obtained nothing by the creditor's assignment of his interest in the land contract. The court noted that the creditor had only a security interest in the land contract and did not assign the underlying debt to the third party. However, the court was unable to determine who the true owner of the interest was as between the vendors and the creditor because the creditor was not a party to the lawsuit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of the sureties and remanded the matter with instructions to dismiss unless the creditor was joined as a party within a time limit to be set by the trial court. The court said that if the creditor was joined and asserted that he owned the vendors' interest, the rights as between the creditor and the vendors had to be litigated.

 

1002 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Mid-County Future Alternatives Committee v. Portland


CA No. A48513


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


95 Ore. App. 556; 770 P.2d 604; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 251


December 16, 1988, Argued and submitted  
March 8, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 28, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Katherine H. O'Neil, Judge pro tempore. No. A8711-06867.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory judgment action, plaintiffs, a citizen and a committee, challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which held that 1987 Or. Laws ch. 818, §3, which addressed city boundary changes, was constitutional in favor of defendant cities.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought a declaratory judgment action against the cities to challenge the constitutionality of 1987 Or. Laws, ch. 818, § 3, which provided that territory annexed to a city or district by a minor boundary change approved by a boundary commission's final order shall be in the annexing city or district by operation of this 1987 Act commencing upon the effective date of the boundary commission's final order. The trial court held that the statute was constitutional, and plaintiffs appealed. The court affirmed because § 3 provided that the annexations to which it related were effective by operation of the 1987 Act, and it also stated that its provisions applied notwithstanding any other provisions of Or. Rev. Stat. ch. 199. Thus, the legislature made it clear that 1987 Or. Laws. Ch. 818, § 3 was an independent source of validity for the annexations that it covered. In addition, statutory provisions affecting city boundaries were consistent with Or. Const. Art. XI, M 2 with regard to the cities because their charters did not describe their boundaries.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the statute was constitutional.

 

1003 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bateman


CA Nos. A47683 (Control), A47684 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


95 Ore. App. 456; 771 P.2d 314; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 261


September 30, 1988, Argued and submitted; November 2, 1988, Resubmitted In Banc  
March 8, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 26, 1989. Petition for Review Denied August 1, 1989 (308 Or 197).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Dorothy M. Baker, Judge. Nos. C85-08-33209, C85-10-34220.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the revocation of his probation by the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which had imposed conditions on defendant's probation, including a requirement that he post the notice "Dangerous Sex Offender" on his residence and any car he drove. An earlier appeal of the conditions themselves had been dismissed as moot when the probation was revoked.


OVERVIEW: The State first argued that the revocation of probation was not a judgment of conviction or any other appealable event under any statute granting appeals to criminal defendants. The court disagreed, noting that although Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.550(4), which authorized revocation of a probation previously granted, did not describe such an action as either an order or a judgment, it "smelled, looked, and quacked" like a judgment and therefore was subject to appellate review. But the court refused to review the conditions of probation to which defendant objected, holding that its scope of review was limited by Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.050, because defendant pleaded guilty, to whether the sentence imposed was cruel or unusual. Defendant did not challenge the length of the incarceration, contend that it exceeded the term specified for the crimes, or contend that it was unconstitutionally cruel and unusual. The court concluded that it was obligated to affirm the judgment. It rejected, as contrary to the import of § 138.050, defendant's argument that because revocation for violation of an unlawful condition of probation was invalid, any sentence was excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revocation of the probation.

 

1004 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crocker


CA No. A46952


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


95 Ore. App. 260; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 202


May 27, 1988, Argued and submitted; December 7, 1988, Resubmitted In Banc  
February 22, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Withdrawn by Order March 15 (95 Or App 581) and Reissued April 12, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Coos County. Richard L. Barron, Judge. Nos. 87-CR-1724, 87-CR-1725.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to rape in the second degree. The Circuit Court, Coos County (Oregon), suspended sentence and placed him on probation for five years, subject to conditions. On appeal, defendant claimed that a condition prohibiting him from being in a private home where children under the age of 18 were present was overbroad.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the court could only consider whether the sentence exceeded the maximum allowed by law or was unconstitutionally cruel and unusual and that, because defendant made neither of those contentions, there was nothing for the court to consider. The court found that a more fundamental issue was whether it could consider any part of the judgment or whether it could consider defendant's contention, unrestricted by the limitations imposed by Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.050. The court held: (1) where defendant pled guilty, Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.050 controlled; (2) a judgment of probation was not a sentence, let alone one that was contended to exceed the maximum allowable by law or to be unconstitutionally cruel and unusual; and (3) where defendant pled guilty and was granted probation, he could not appeal from the judgment of conviction where the trial court suspended his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's appeal.

 

1005 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Porter


CA No. A47698


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


95 Ore. App. 373; 768 P.2d 940; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 206


December 2, 1988, Argued and submitted  
February 22, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 21, 1989. Petition for Review Denied May 16, 1989 (308 Or 33).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Douglas County. Robert C. Millikan, Judge. No. M87-1906.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Oregon sought review of a decision of the District Court, Douglas County (Oregon), which sustained the demurrer of defendant. Defendant had been charged with the failure to perform the duties of a driver pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 811.700(1)(c).


OVERVIEW: The trial court allowed the demurrer on the ground that Or. Rev. Stat. § 811.700(1)(c) was unconstitutionally vague. The State appealed from the judgment on the demurrer pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 135.660. The court disagreed with the decision of the trial court and determined that defendant's demurrer should have been overruled. The requirement under Or. Rev. Stat. § 811.700(1)(c) that a person take "reasonable steps" to notify the person in charge of damaged property of the fact that it had been damaged articulated what was required sufficiently. It was left to the finder of fact to determine only whether the steps taken to provide the information to the owner or person in charge met that standard. Thus, the court found that Or. Rev. Stat. § 811.700(1)(c) was a constitutionally valid statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision.

 

1006 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Sealey v. Hicks


CA No. A47084


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


95 Ore. App. 182; 768 P.2d 428; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 146; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P12,104


September 23, 1988, Argued and submitted  
February 8, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 24, 1989. Petition for Review Allowed May 2, 1989 (307 Or 719).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. Nancy W. Campbell, Judge pro tempore. No. 86-0869C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff minor, by and through his guardian ad litem, and plaintiff parents filed a negligence action against defendant car distributor and others. The Circuit Court, Washington County (Oregon), entered summary judgment in favor of the distributor on the ground that the claim was time-barred by Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.905. The minor and his parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The minor and his parents filed suit against the car distributor for injuries suffered by the minor when the car in which he was riding as a passenger overturned. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of the distributor on the ground that the claim was time-barred by Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.905. The minor and his parents appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court rejected the contention that Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.905 violated the privileges and immunities provisions of Or. Const. art. I, § 20. According to the court, the minor and his parents did not show unequal treatment to them as individuals or as a class. The court further rejected the contention that the negligence claim asserted by the minor and his parents was timely because it was governed by either Or. Rev. Stat. § 12.110, the two-year statute of limitation, or Or. Rev. Stat. § 12.115, the general statute of repose, both of which ran from the date of injury. According to the court, the claim against the distributor clearly fell within the definition of a product liability action set forth in Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.905.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which entered summary judgment in favor of the car distributor in the negligence action filed by the minor and his parents.

 

1007 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Salem v. Wolf


CA No. A46107


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


94 Ore. App. 654; 766 P.2d 1051; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 5


October 19, 1988, Argued and submitted  
January 11, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Marion County. John B. Wilson, Judge. No. 87D-101400.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the District Court, Marion County (Oregon) that convicted him of resisting a peace officer in violation of Salem, Or. Rev. Code § 95.430(a). The trial court denied his motion to dismiss the accusatory instrument.


OVERVIEW: The lower court convicted defendant of resisting a peace officer in violation of a municipal code. The lower court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the accusatory instrument. The court affirmed the conviction. It found no merit in defendant's claim that the municipal code was unconstitutionally overbroad. The court found that the municipal code, Salem, Or., Rev. Code § 95.430(a) did not reach behavior protected under the search and seizure and free speech provisions of the Oregon and United States Constitutions. The court found the municipal code permitted resistance to an arrest made with excessive force. None of defendant's examples of how the municipal code prohibited free speech fit the definition of "resist" as used in the section so both of his constitutional challenges failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1008 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Portland v. Lodi


CA Nos. A47872 (Control), A48372 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


94 Ore. App. 735; 767 P.2d 108; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 23


November 14, 1988, Argued and submitted  
January 11, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 21, 1989. Petition for Review Allowed May 31, 1989 (308 Or 79).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Multnomah County. Frank Bearden, Judge. DA Nos. 360332, 363890.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged with carrying concealed weapons in violation of City of Portland, Or., Code § 14.32.100. The complaints alleged that they were carrying blades longer than three and one-half inches. Defendants demurred, and the District Court, Multnomah County (Oregon) dismissed the complaints. The City appealed from the pretrial judgments dismissing the complaints, and the appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that City of Portland, Or., Code § 14.32.100 was in conflict with Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.240, which prohibited the carrying of concealed weapons, and was thereby preempted. In affirming, the court held that § 166.240 only prohibited carrying certain types of concealed knives. Excluded from that list were pocketknives, regardless of the length of the blade. The statutory policy was to broadly preserve the right to bear arms, while narrowly limiting the right to carry knives. City of Portland, Or., Code § 14.32.100 made it unlawful for any legally unauthorized person to carry a pocketknife with a blade longer than three and one-half inches. Thus City of Portland, Or., Code § 14.32.100 prohibited an act that Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.240 permitted: the carrying of any concealed knife that had a blade longer than three and one-half inches. City of Portland, Or., Code § 14.32.100 and Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.240 were not compatible. Thus, City of Portland, Or., Code § 14.32.100 was preempted, as a city ordinance could not prohibit an act permitted by a state statute or permit an act that was prohibited by a state statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the pretrial judgments that dismissed the City's complaints against defendants for carrying concealed weapons.

 

1009 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Associated Oregon Veterans v. Department of Veterans' Affairs


CA No. A47761


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


94 Ore. App. 526; 766 P.2d 1043; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 2225


October 3, 1988, Argued and submitted  
December 21, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 28, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Duane R. Ertsgaard, Judge. No. 86C-12404.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff borrowers appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which awarded attorney fees to defendant Oregon Department of Veterans' Affairs (DVA) after it had granted DVA summary judgment. The borrowers had sought a determination of their rights under their farm and home loan agreements with DVA.


OVERVIEW: The borrowers alleged six claims. Three were based on contracts with DVA which provided for an award of reasonable attorney fees to the prevailing party in litigation. The borrowers contended that, because DVA denied that their claims arose from the contracts and then "straddled" the issue by conditional language in the prayer, it failed to meet the requirement that it set out the facts or statute upon which it was relying for the award. The court disagreed and affirmed the award. DVA's pleading adequately asserted the contractual basis of its right to recover attorney fees and gave the borrowers notice that it was prepared to assert a claim on that ground. The pleadings met the requirements of Or. R. Civ. P. 68C. The court held that the trial court considered the appropriate factors in determining the fee. It considered the hourly fee billed as relevant but not determinative. The evidence supported the conclusion that the hours spent in defending the action were not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Oregon State Police Officers Asso. v. State


CA No. A46148


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


94 Ore. App. 478; 766 P.2d 408; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 2235


November 18, 1988, Argued and submitted  
December 21, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 24, 1989. Petition for Review Allowed April 4, 1989 (307 Or 611).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Irving M. Steinbock, Judge. No. A8508-05041.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed on appeal and on cross-appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a state, the state police department, and the superintendent of the state police (government), sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which entered a judgment in favor of plaintiff union in the union's complaint challenging the constitutionality of a state statute that prohibited the political activities of police officers.


OVERVIEW: The union filed a complaint on behalf of the police officers that challenged the validity of Or. Rev. Stat. § 181.400(2). Section 181.400(2) prohibited any member of the state police from being active or participating in any political contest. The trial court granted a judgment for the union and awarded attorney fees to the union under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The government argued that the complaint had not presented a justiciable controversy because no there were no complaints of specific activities being restricted. The court held that the complaint had little if anything to do with the potential discipline or risk of discipline. The court concluded that § 181.400(2) facially violated Or. Const. art. I, § 8, so the trial court's decision in favor of the union was correct. The court rejected the government's challenge of the trial court's grant of attorney fees to the union.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which entered a judgment in favor of the union in the union's complaint challenging the constitutionality of a state statute that restricted the political activities of police officers.

Landsing Property Corp. v. Portland Fire Code Bd. of Appeals

March 4, 1988, Argued and submitted

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owner appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which affirmed respondent fire agency's determination upholding an order to place a fire sprinkler system in the owner's building.


OVERVIEW: The owner argued that the order requiring a fire sprinkler system was erroneous. On review, the court affirmed the order. In reaching its conclusion, the court held that its scope of review was limited to whether the fire marshal's order was an abuse of discretion. The court then held that the marshal acted within his discretion in issuing the order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1012 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Jungen v. State


CA No. A45994


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


94 Ore. App. 101; 764 P.2d 938; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 2075


September 28, 1988, Argued and submitted  
November 23, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 24, 1989. Petition for Review Denied April 18, 1989 (307 Or 658).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Douglas County. Joan G. Seitz, Judge. No. L86-2634.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, wife of decedent and insurer, appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Douglas County (Oregon), which granted defendant State's motion to dismiss the wife's wrongful death claim on the ground that it was immune from liability under Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.265(3)(a). The decedent's employer's workers' compensation carrier paid benefits to the wife and the insurer sought reimbursement of those benefits.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was killed when the tractor he was driving overturned on a state highway. Plaintiffs argued that Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.265(3)(a), which stated that every public body was immune from liability for any claim for injury to or death of any person covered by any workers' compensation law, was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the State. The court stated that the opportunity to sue the State was a privilege which § 30.265(3)(a) denied to persons who had recovered workers' compensation benefits. It discriminated against a true class and, therefore, was subject to constitutional scrutiny. The distinction drawn between persons receiving workers' compensation benefits and those not receiving benefits was established by workers' compensation laws and existed independently of § 30.265(3)(a). That distinction was not based on immutable personal characteristics. Accordingly, plaintiffs had to show that § 30.265(3)(a) was not rationally related to a legitimate state purpose, which they could not do. The court concluded that there was a rational basis for retaining governmental immunity as to those persons receiving workers' compensation benefits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1013 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Luttrell


CA No. A45162


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


93 Ore. App. 772; 764 P.2d 554; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 1767


May 31, 1988, Argued and submitted  
November 9, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Deschutes County. John M. Copenhaver, Judge. No. 85-CR-0299-JC.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Circuit Court, Deschutes County (Oregon), which convicted him of sodomy and sexual abuse, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.405(1)(b), of a six-month old child for whom he was providing day care.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that there was no evidence to support his convictions, the State failed to prove actual sexual penetration, the trial court erred in admitting polygraph evidence. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the State introduced sufficient evidence from which a rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of the crimes beyond a reasonable doubt. Further, under § 163.405(1)(b), defendant's conduct was deemed "deviate sexual intercourse," and the plain language of the statutes demonstrated that sexual penetration was not an element of sodomy. As to the admission of polygraph evidence, defendant mistakenly relied on a case that was decided several months after he was convicted, and the case did not have a retroactive effect. Moreover, the evidence was received without objection pursuant to a stipulation of the parties; thus, the question was not preserved for appeal. The court declined to consider it as an error of law because case law established a rule of evidence, not a rule of criminal procedure that was mandated by either the state or federal constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for sodomy and sexual abuse of a child.

 

1014 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Portland v. Ayers


CA No. A40979


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


93 Ore. App. 731; 764 P.2d 556; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 1768


April 1, 1987, Argued and submitted; June 1, 1988, Resubmitted In Banc  
November 9, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 4, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Multnomah County. Thomas Moultrie, Judge. No. 304441-8508.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the District Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which convicted him of violating a city code, Portland, Or., City Code § 14.24.160, by operating a sound reproducing device on a public right-of-way so as to be plainly audible 50 feet or more from the device.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction resulted from his use of a portable loudspeaker to amplify anti-abortion statements. Defendant assigned error to the overruling of his demurrer to the complaint, through which he asserted that the code provision violated the speech provisions of the state and federal constitutions, Or. Const. art. I, § 20 and the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. Because defendant did not attempt to use certain exception procedures, he could not complain on equal protection or equal privileges and immunities grounds regarding those procedures. Defendant's arguments on the constitutional free speech provisions appeared to be that the city's ordinance "prohibited" speech. However, the ordinance did not regulate speech or the content of speech, it regulated amplified noise. The court found that the ordinance did not violate Or. Const. art. I. § 8, as defendant urged. Finally, the court found that the ordinance did not violate the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

1016 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. McKenzie


CA No. A44952


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


92 Ore. App. 647; 759 P.2d 1123; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 1486


June 29, 1988, Argued and submitted  
August 24, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 14, 1988. Petition for Review Allowed November 16, 1988 (307 Or 145).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. James R. Ellis, Judge. No. C87-02-30673.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which convicted him of the crime of escape in the second degree, a violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.155. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion for a judgment of acquittal and in failing to properly instruct the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant escaped from custody when he was mistakenly released by an officer who believed that he was another detainee, who was scheduled to be released upon bail. Defendant was indicted for escape. His attorney moved for an acquittal on the ground that his offense did not constitute an escape as provided in Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.155. Defendant was convicted as charged, and he appealed. The court affirmed, finding that defendant's behaviour in allowing the officer to believe that he was the person who was allowed bail constituted escape under the statute, and the trial court properly instructed the jury that it was the arbiter of the facts and that it was the judge's function to decide the questions of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1017 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Reiman v. Eugene Education Asso.


CA No. A45910


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


92 Ore. App. 504; 759 P.2d 295; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 1423


June 27, 1988, Argued and submitted  
August 17, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. George J. Woodrich, Judge. No. 16-87-03570.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed as moot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), in favor of respondents, school district and education association, in an action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief to stop a teachers' strike.


OVERVIEW: The parents sought an injunction barring the education association from striking, requiring the union and the school district to submit their labor dispute to final and binding arbitration. They also sought a declaration that a certain state statute was unconstitutional. The labor dispute and strike ended before a final judgment was entered. Approximately six months after the strike had ended, the parents caused a final judgment to be entered and then filed their notice of appeal. On appeal, the court found that because the strike about which the parents complained had ended before the final judgment was entered, it was clear that the requests for injunctive relief were moot and that the request for an order mandating binding arbitration of the underlying labor dispute was also moot. The parents did not amend their complaint after the strike had ended to allege any continuing injury.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the parent's appeal as moot.

 

1018 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Federal Deposit Ins. Corp. v. Burdell


CA No. A43052


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


92 Ore. App. 389; 759 P.2d 282; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 1314


September 14, 1987, Argued and submitted  
August 10, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied September 30, 1988. Petition for Review Allowed November 1, 1988 (307 Or 101).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Maurice K. Merten, Judge. No. 16-86-04163.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant homeowner sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), that granted plaintiff corporate receiver's motion for summary judgment in the action for the judicial foreclosure of a trust deed and a deficiency judgment against the homeowners. The homeowners contended that the receiver was not entitled to a deficiency judgment, because the trust deed was given to secure the purchase price of the property.


OVERVIEW: The receiver filed an action for the judicial foreclosure of a trust deed and a deficiency judgment against the homeowners. The receiver subsequently filed a motion for summary judgment, which was granted by the circuit court. On appeal, the homeowner contended that the receiver was not entitled to a deficiency judgment, because the trust deed was given to secure the purchase price of the property. The court appealed the judgment, holding that the homeowners' trust deed was a commercial trust deed at the time of foreclosure, as defined in former Or. Rev. Stat. § 86.770(4), and former Or. Rev. Stat. § 86.770(3) permitted it to obtain a deficiency judgment, regardless of the anti-deficiency provisions for purchase money mortgages. Further, the court held that although a trust deed was deemed to be a mortgage on real property, Or. Rev. Stat. § 86.715, conflict when the beneficiary judicially foreclosed a purchase money commercial trust deed. Thus, the court concluded that the application of Or. Rev. Stat. § 88.075 (1985) to the homeowners' trust deed did not alter their obligations and was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment that was granted in favor of the receiver in the action that the receiver brought against the homeowners for the judicial foreclosure of a trust deed and a deficiency judgment.

 

1019 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Marcoules v. Oregon Liquor Control Com.


CA No. A42127


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


91 Ore. App. 573; 756 P.2d 661; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 1146


January 25, 1988, Argued and submitted  
June 22, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Judicial Review from Oregon Liquor Control Commission. Nos. 86-ES-001, 86-V-036.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant license holders challenged a final order of the Oregon Liquor Control Commission (Oregon), which suspended their retail malt beverage license for 120 days and upheld the emergency suspension of the license. They contended that the notice of the emergency suspension did not comply with ORS 183.430(2) and that there was not a sufficient showing of disorderly premises under OAR 845-06-045.


OVERVIEW: The license holders were notified by mail of an emergency suspension and a proposed cancellation of their license. They requested a hearing and the hearing examiner recommend a suspension, but not a cancellation. They alleged that the notice was fatally deficient because it did not comply with the statutory requirements and their due process rights were therefore violated. The hearing examiner had found that the notice may not have been adequate for the suspension because it did not include the violation of Oregon Liquor Control Commission rules that formed the substantive basis for suspension. However, the basis was the same as that for the cancellation notice, which had been received by the license holders, thereby curing any defect. On appeal, the court held that ORS 183.430(2) provided a basis for the Commission to suspend their license in order to protect the public health and safety. Because various types of ongoing disorderly conduct had been cited in the cancellation notice, and the licensees had been represented by counsel who vigorously cross examined witnesses, they had not been prejudiced by any deficiency in the suspension notice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the Commission.

State v. Buck


CA No. A43225


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


92 Ore. App. 130; 757 P.2d 861; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 1162


March 31, 1988, Argued and submitted  
June 13, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied September 9, 1988. Petition for Review Denied October 18, 1988 (307 Or 77).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. F. Gordon Cottrell, Judge. No. 10-86-03599.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), which convicted defendant of incest in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.525.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.525 was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad and denied him equal protection. Defendant was indicted for having engaged in sexual intercourse with his stepdaughter, who was over 18 years of age at the time. On appeal, the court held that a stepchild was a descendant for the purposes of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.525, whether or not the child had reached the age of majority. The court held that descendant was defined in such a way that a person could tell whether the relationship with another would render the person liable to the statute's penalties if they engaged in sexual intercourse. The court found that § 163.525 was not overbroad and did not violate defendant's federal right to privacy. The court held that the statute did not deny defendant equal protection under the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of the circuit court.

 

1021 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Helander


CA No. A46497


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


92 Ore. App. 108; 758 P.2d 359; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 1165


May 31, 1988, Argued and submitted  
June 13, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Clackamas County. Richard Barron, Judge pro tempore. No. 87-11581.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the District Court, Clackamas County (Oregon) for failing to perform the duties of a driver involved in an accident in which property was damaged.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was allegedly involved in a "hit and run" accident. The complaint against defendant named a different street upon which the alleged accident occurred from that named in the citation against defendant. The State put on proof that conformed to the complaint, not the citation. A judgment of acquittal was entered because of the difference between the proof and the accusatory instrument. After charges were refiled, defendant pled the defense of res judicata. His motion to dismiss on double jeopardy grounds was denied and he appealed contending that Or. Rev. Stat. § 131.535(1). The court found that the issue of guilt or innocence was not resolved in the former trial and that the State was not permitted to produce evidence at the second trial that it did not at the first. Thus, the prohibition against double jeopardy was not violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.

 

1022 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pyritz


CA No. A44954


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


90 Ore. App. 601; 752 P.2d 1310; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 452


February 24, 1988, Argued and submitted  
April 20, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Lane County. Kip W. Leonard, Judge. No. B70-470.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a judgment from District Court, Lane County (Oregon), which sustained defendant's demurrer to a charge that he violated Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.222, which prohibited frequenting a place where controlled substances were used.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.222(1) was too vague under the Oregon Constitution. The court reversed the judgment, finding that § 167.222(1) as a whole, nor any word in it, gave a judge or jury unbridled discretion to decide what conduct was criminal because each word was defined or definable with a reasonable degree of certainty. Accordingly, § 167.222(1) was not impermissibly vague under the Oregon Constitution. Defendant also contended that § 167.222(1) was overbroad because it reached conduct protected by Or. Const. art. I, §§ 8, 9, 20, 21, 26. The court rejected this contention, finding that Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.222(1) did not reach conduct that was protected under the Oregon Constitution. Further, the court rejected defendant's contention that § 167.222(1) was void for vagueness under the United States Constitution for the same reasons it rejected respondent's vagueness arguments under the Oregon Constitution. Finally, although § 167.222(1) clearly applied to constitutionally proscribable conduct, defendant failed to show that § 167.222(1) as applied to him was unconstitutionally overbroad and that the infringement of his rights was substantial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment that sustained defendant's demurrer to a charge that he violated a statute, which prohibited frequenting a place where controlled substances were used.

Jackson County v. Jackson Education Service Dist.


CA No. A42801


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


90 Ore. App. 299; 752 P.2d 1224; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 271

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Jackson County. L. A. Merryman, Judge. No. 85-4169-J-1.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school taxing districts sought review of a judgment entered by the Circuit Court, Jackson County (Oregon), which found in favor of respondent county in its declaratory judgment action seeking a return of interest that it had paid to the districts pursuant to a settlement agreement.


OVERVIEW: In a prior case, the tax court held that under Or. Rev. Stat. § 294.080(3), interest earned on unsegregated county tax accounts belonged to the several taxing districts within the counties for whom the funds had been designated. As a result of the decision of the tax court, the county entered a stipulation with the districts for payment of the interest. The legislature subsequently passed 1985 Or. Laws ch. 162, §§ 12, 13, which limited the liability of the counties to interest that accrued after a certain date. The county brought this action to recover the interest paid to the districts that had accrued before that date. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment in favor of the county because the trial court properly determined that §§ 12, 13 were constitutional. The districts did not have a vested right to the funds, and the legislature had the authority to enact the laws. Furthermore, the trial court and not the tax court had jurisdiction to consider the validity of §§ 12, 13. The trial court also did not abuse its discretion in denying the districts' motion to file a second amended answer because the districts' proposed allegations did not constitute colorable claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the county.

Miller Brands, Inc. v. Oregon Liquor Control Com.


CA No. A41773


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


90 Ore. App. 266; 752 P.2d 320; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 354


December 16, 1987, Argued and submitted  
April 6, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Charles S. Crookham, Judge. No. A8505-02765.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with instructions to dismiss complaint as moot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Oregon Liquor Control Commission (OLCC) and a corporation, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which entered a judgment declaring Or. Rev. Stat. § 473.030(7) (repealed 1988) unconstitutional and dismissed a claim. After the legislature repealed § 473.030(7), OLCC requested that the court remand the case with instructions to dismiss it. Plaintiff opposed the motion.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff had also sought to have the OLCC enjoined from allowing tax credits pursuant to § 473.030(7) and required to collect amounts equal to past credits from the taxpayers that had received them. After the trial court granted partial summary judgment in plaintiff's favor on the constitutionality of § 473.030(7), plaintiff voluntarily dismissed the other claim and moved for the entry of final judgment. In remanding the cause with instructions to dismiss the complaint as moot, the court found that neither § 473.030(7) nor the issue of whether it was constitutional existed. The constitutionality of § 473.030(7) was the only controversy which remained in the case, after plaintiff withdrew its claim for other relief, and the constitutional issue was the only issue on which the trial court made a substantive ruling. Plaintiff's argument that the trial court's declaration that § 473.030(7) was unconstitutional implicitly carried with it some or all of the other relief that plaintiff sought explicitly in its complaint and explicitly decided to forego later in the proceedings was unavailing.


OUTCOME: The court allowed OLCC's motion. The cause was remanded with instructions to dismiss the complaint as moot.

State v. Caughey


CA No. A43473


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


89 Ore. App. 605; 750 P.2d 511; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 234


November 25, 1987, Argued and submitted  
February 24, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 22, 1988. Petition for Review Denied May 24, 1988 (305 Or 672).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Josephine County. Gerald Neufeld, Judge. No. 86-CR-358.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court, Josephine County (Oregon), which imposed a sentence following defendant's guilty plea to kidnapping in the first degree pursuant to the dangerous offender statute, ORS 161.725.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to kidnapping in the first degree, a Class A felony. The trial court found that defendant suffered from a severe personality disorder. It further found that on the basis of past criminal activity, he had a propensity toward criminal conduct and that he was a dangerous offender. Based on such finding, the trial court sentenced him to 30 years imprisonment, with a minimum of 15 years pursuant to the dangerous offender statute, ORS 161.725. On appeal, defendant argued that the imposition of an enhanced sentence punished the "status" of suffering from a severe personality disorder and thereby violated the prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment contained in Article I, section 16, and the Eighth Amendment. In affirming, the court noted that ORS 161.725 did not punish a person for having a severe personality disorder; rather, it merely reflected the legislative recognition that a person who had a severe personality disorder that caused him to commit dangerous crimes was less amenable to rehabilitation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1026 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Damofle


CA Nos. A43818 (Control), A43841 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


89 Ore. App. 620; 750 P.2d 518; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 239


September 14, 1987, Argued and submitted  
February 24, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Damofle's Reconsideration and Quintana's Reconsideration Denied April 22, 1988. Both Petitions for Review Denied May 17, 1988 (305 Or 671).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Lincoln County. Robert J. Huckleberry, Judge. Nos. CR86-03127, CR86-03303.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged a judgment from the District Court, Lincoln County (Oregon), which convicted defendants of criminal mistreatment in the second degree, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.200(1). The trial court also denied defendants' motions for acquittal, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 136.445.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were the parents of three children. The family lived in a room constructed of plastic and wood inside a barn that was cold, wet, and had an overwhelming stench. The family used a coffee can as a toilet, which was full of urine and easily accessible to the children. In addition, the home contained a gasoline container with matches within easy reach of the children. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly convicted defendants of failing to provide adequate "physical care" for their children. As a result, the court rejected defendants' contention that, without actual physical harm, they could not have been held liable under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.200(1). Instead, the court held that no physical injury was required because the statute was intended to protect dependent persons from mistreatment other than physical violence and that such a construction did not violate Or. Const. art. I, § 20, or the Fourteenth Amendment, as defendants had alleged. Furthermore, the court held that the statute was not impermissible vague and that the statute provided fair notice. Accordingly, the court held that there was ample evidence to support the convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendants of criminal mistreatment in the second degree.

State ex rel. Juvenile Dep't v. Stevens


CA No. A43264


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


89 Ore. App. 467; 749 P.2d 613; 1988 Ore. App. LEXIS 122


November 16, 1987, Argued and submitted  
February 10, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Kristena A. LaMar, Judge. No. 88080.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile appealed from an order of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which found him to be within the jurisdiction of the juvenile court pursuant to ORS 419.476(1)(a) (Oregon) because he committed an act, which, if committed by an adult, would have constituted a crime. Appellant's motion to suppress evidence seized from his person after his arrest for a curfew violation was denied.


OVERVIEW: The State had filed a petition alleging that appellant was within the juvenile court's jurisdiction. Appellant was in a bowling alley after the hour of curfew according to an ordinance of Multnomah County, Oregon. A police officer approached appellant and arrested him for a curfew violation. In a search incident to the arrest, the officer found a cloth pouch, some baggies, and cash. Appellant gave the officer permission to look in the pouch, which contained methamphetamine. Affirming, the court found no error. Under ORS 419.760, the police could take a minor into custody for violation of a curfew ordinance. The minor had to be taken into custody according to the procedures in ORS 419.569. The court concluded that the only way to interpret the statutes meaningfully was to construe ORS 419.760 to be read to grant authority to take a child into custody for a curfew violation, as long as it was done within the procedures set out in ORS 419.569. The officer had authority to arrest appellant for a curfew violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

OVERVIEW: Defendant was a cable-logging operator and contended that Or. Admin. Rogers v. Saylor


CA No. A35289


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


88 Ore. App. 480; 746 P.2d 718; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 5210


May 16, 1986, Argued and submitted; October 7, 1987, Resubmitted In Banc  
December 9, 1987, Filed; Petition for Review allowed February 23, 1988


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 5, 1988. Petition for Review Allowed February 23, 1988 (305 Or 273).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Charles S. Crookham, Judge. No. A8409 05447.



DISPOSITION: Striking of attorney fees allegations reversed; judgment otherwise affirmed and remanded for proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party appealed a certification of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County, (Oregon), which dismissed his claim alleging punitive damages, compensatory damages in excess of the limits of Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.270, and attorney fees in connection with his 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action against defendants, Multnomah County, City of Gresham and individual police officers, for the police officers' alleged physical and verbal assault on him.


OVERVIEW: The injured party asserted a § 1983 violation against defendants for an alleged physical attack on him by the police officers and sought punitive damages, compensatory damages of $ 110,000, and attorney fees. Defendants made a motion to strike the injured party's allegations of damages which the trial court granted on the ground that the injured party's remedy was subject to Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.270, which limited the liability of public bodies and their employees acting within the scope of their employment to $ 100,000 per claimant, prohibited the award of punitive damages, and was silent with respect to attorney fees. The injured party appealed. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court found that the injured party could not recover punitive damages or compensatory damages in excess of the limits of § 30.270 because 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 did not provide a basis for concluding that Congress intended § 1983 to preempt the Oregon statutory direction. The court held that § 1988 expressly provided for attorney fee awards in § 1983 actions and, although there was no basis for an award of fees under Oregon law, the express language of § 1988 was preemptive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's certification of the dismissal of the injured party's claim for punitive damages and for compensatory damages in excess of statutory limits. The court reversed and remanded the trial court's certification of the dismissal of the injured party's claim for attorney fees.

 

1031 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Woodley


CA No. A41196


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


88 Ore. App. 493; 746 P.2d 227; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 5224


April 27, 1987, Argued and submitted  
December 9, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 12, 1988. Petition for Review Allowed April 5, 1988 (305 Or 467).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Klamath County. Donald A. W. Piper, Judge. No. 86-173-CR.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Klamath County (Oregon), which convicted him for attempted sexual abuse in the second degree under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.415.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was employed as a high school girls' basketball coach. While traveling by bus to a game, he allegedly touched a team member on "the thigh area and between her breasts." Defendant's motion for an acquittal at the close of the State's case was denied. The court considered whether the indictment sufficiently alleged the crime of sexual abuse in the second degree. If the indictment was insufficient to charge the offense that it purported to state, then it was insufficient to support a trial. Subjecting another person to nonconsensual sexual contact constituted the crime of sexual abuse in the second degree, Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.415. Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.305(6) prohibited any touching of the sexual or other intimate parts of a person. The court interpreted the meaning of "sexual or other intimate parts" and held that there was no basis in the language of the statute or in the legislative history on which to conclude that a human "thigh area" or the area "between female breasts" were "intimate parts." The court could not permit the legislative intent to be determined by the trier of fact. Thus, the indictment failed to allege a crime.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1032 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Pooler v. Motor Vehicles Div.


CA No. A41560


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


88 Ore. App. 475; 746 P.2d 716; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 5183


September 30, 1987, Argued and submitted  
December 2, 1987, Filed; Petition for Review allowed February 23, 1988


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied January 29, 1988. Petition for Review Allowed February 23, 1988 (305 Or 273).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Klamath County. Theodore D. Abram, Judge. No. 85-547-CV.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Motor Vehicles Division (MVD) challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Klamath County (Oregon) reversing an order suspending respondent driver's license.


OVERVIEW: Around 2:40 a.m., the driver approached a DUII roadblock and made a legal U-turn before reaching it. An officer, assigned to stop vehicles that appeared to be avoiding the roadblock, stopped the driver, noticed an odor of alcohol, and asked him to perform field sobriety tests. The driver was arrested after he took a breath test which disclosed a blood alcohol content of 0.15 percent. The trial court reversed his subsequent license suspension by the MVD on the ground that there was not a valid stop and that the exclusionary rule barred all evidence admitted as a result of the illegal stop. The court held that when the legislature used the term "arrest" in former ORS 482.541 and former ORS 487.805, it meant a valid arrest. Accordingly, the police could not administer a breath test, and the MVD could not suspend driving privileges based on a breath test result, unless the driver was first validly arrested. The fact that the driver made a legal U-turn and was slow to stop in response to the officer's flashing lights did not constitute a reasonable suspicion that the driver had committed a crime or a traffic violation. Thus, the stop and subsequent arrest were not valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents appealed a decision from the Circuit Court, Coos County (Oregon), which found that defendants, the administrators of state agencies involved in the care of children committed to secure custody by the juvenile court, could charge them for the support of their children under Or. OVERVIEW: The parents' children were found to be within the jurisdiction of the juvenile court under Or. Rev. School Dist. v. Wilsonville


CA No. A39158


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


87 Ore. App. 246; 742 P.2d 59; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 4520


February 11, 1987, Argued and submitted  
September 9, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 27, 1987. Petition for Review Denied December 22, 1987 (304 Or 548).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Clackamas County. Charles A. Sams, Judge. No. 84-12-165.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; assessment reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court, Clackamas County (Oregon), which voided a special road improvements assessment as to property owned by respondent school district. The court reviewed the decision pursuant to ORS 223.401, 34.040 (Oregon).


OVERVIEW: Part of the district's undeveloped property was included in a Local Improvement District (LID) formed for the improvement of a road over its objection. The city adopted the recommendations of a Board of Viewers for apportionment of the assessment and adopted an ordinance authorizing the city recorder to establish a lien docket. The trial court reversed the city's decision, holding that it had excluded property from the LID that was specifically benefitted by the improvement. On appeal, the court held that where the school district did not directly challenge its assessment, but argued that the cost of the improvement was not distributed widely enough, the court had to determine whether the trial court had jurisdiction. The court held that it did because the process was quasi-judicial. The court held that the decision to excluded the properties in question from the LID was not arbitrary because the city's decision was supported by substantial evidence. Benefit was a question of fact to be decided on a case by case basis. The trial court also misapplied Wilsonville, Oregon Ordinance 70, § 6. Finally, procedural deficiencies did not void the assessment when it was not unfair.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and reinstated the assessment.

 

1036 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


C.I.S. Northwest, Inc. v. Berjac of Portland, Inc.


CA No. A38096


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


87 Ore. App. 233; 742 P.2d 618; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 4630


October 6, 1986, Argued and submitted  
September 9, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Allowed by Opinion December 30, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Charles S. Crookham, Judge. No. A8501-00356.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurance broker challenged a ruling from the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which dismissed the broker's action against defendant insurance premium financing company to recover money that the broker had paid to the company pursuant to the company's demand under Or. Rev. Stat. § 746. 515.


OVERVIEW: An agency asked the broker to locate insurance companies that would provide insurance for the agency's clients. When the policies were issued, the broker asked the company to finance the premiums on some of the policies, which the company agreed to do. When the agency lost its license, the broker paid an amount equal to the unearned premiums to the company because the broker believed that Or. Rev. Stat. § 746.515 required the broker to take such action. The broker then brought the instant action, and the circuit court dismissed the complaint for failure to state a claim. The broker appealed, and the court reversed and remanded the judgment. The court held that the amended complaint alleged facts which, if true, showed that the company, as promisor, could satisfy an actual or asserted duty of the insureds, as promisee, to the broker, as beneficiary, by performance of the promise. Or. Rev. Stat. § 746.515 did not require an insurer to "return" unearned premiums if no premiums had been paid to it or its agent. The return of money necessarily implied that it had been received. Nothing in Or. Rev. Stat. § 746.515 created an obligation that the broker collect premiums for the company.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's dismissal of the broker's complaint against the company and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

Moen v. Washington County


CA Nos. A35949 (Control), A36066 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


86 Ore. App. 639; 740 P.2d 802; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 4163


May 28, 1986, Argued and submitted  
August 5, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. Delbert B. Mayer, Judge. (82-0519C); Gregory E. Milnes, Judge. (19-850 and 19-851).



DISPOSITION: Appeal in cases nos. 19-850 and 19-851 dismissed; judgment in case no. 82-0519C affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In actions against respondents, a county, court officials, the State of Oregon, and others, appellant citizen sought review of the decisions of the Circuit Court, Washington County (Oregon) in three cases; in two cases, the citizen challenged the trial court's denial of her motion for the return of funds deposited as bail to secure her son's appearance in criminal proceedings. The trial court dismissed a third action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: In the first two cases, the citizen challenged the trial court's denial of her requests for the return of funds posted as bail for her son. The son was convicted in the first case, and the second action against him was dismissed. The trial court then ordered the security exonerated under Or. Rev. Stat. § 135.265(2), and the funds were sent to the son's attorney. The citizen then filed her motions for the return of the funds, which were denied on the ground that she had no standing to object to the exoneration order. The trial court's orders in the first two cases were rendered in 1981, and the citizen obtained an order in 1985, which reiterated the trial court's decisions in 1981, and designated the orders as final judgment orders. The citizen's action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 was dismissed on the ground of judicial immunity and that she could not use a § 1983 action as a collateral attack upon the bail refund proceedings. The court dismissed the citizen's appeals in the first two cases as untimely, as the trial court's orders of 1981 were final judgments, and affirmed the trial court's judgment as to the § 1983 action.


OUTCOME: The citizen's appeal was dismissed in the first two cases, and the trial court's judgment in the third case was affirmed.

 

1038 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Cascade Fireworks, Inc. v. State


CA No. A40335


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


86 Ore. App. 355; 738 P.2d 1013; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 4014


February 25, 1987, Argued and submitted  
July 8, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Richard D. Barber, Judge. No. 85-2350.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wholesaler of fireworks sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Marion County (Oregon), which upheld the constitutionality of statutes regulating the sale of fireworks in favor of defendant, the State of Oregon. The wholesaler brought the declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of the statutes.


OVERVIEW: The wholesaler brought the declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of statutes regulating the sale of fireworks. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of the statutes. On review, the court affirmed and held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 480.156 did not violate the Commerce Clause. A wholesaler's reasonable belief that a permit was valid would provide a defense to a prosecution for violation of the statute and, thus, the application of the statute could have only incidental effects on interstate commence. Further, the statute advanced a legitimate local public interest in the safety of the citizens of the State. Oregon's interest in the safety of its citizens clearly outweighed any incidental impact on interstate commerce. Or. Rev. Stat. § 480.156 was not unconstitutionally vague because the wording was sufficiently specific to inform a person of what conduct was prohibited. It was clear that a wholesale sale of fireworks could not be made to a non-Oregon resident unless the purchaser had a permit, if a permit was required by the laws of the non-resident's state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment upholding the constitutionality of Oregon's statutes regulating the sale of fireworks.

State v. Moen


CA No. A39495


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


86 Ore. App. 87; 738 P.2d 228; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 3984


March 31, 1987, Argued and submitted  
June 24, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Val D. Sloper, Judge. No. 86-C-20504.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which found defendant guilty of contempt of court for failure to obey a duly served subpoena.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found defendant guilty of contempt of court for failure to obey a duly served subpoena. Defendant contended on appeal that the trial court's authority to punish him for contempt was, under the facts, limited to a fine not exceeding $ 100. The court stated that Or. Rev. Stat. § 33.020(1) limited the punishment for nondisruptive contempt to a $ 100 fine, unless the court found an actual prejudicial effect, specifically focused on the concrete situation in the particular proceeding. The prejudice contemplated by § 33.020(1) had to be directly related to the proceeding for which the defendant had been held in contempt. The court held that it could not say that the loss of defendant's testimony actually prejudiced the state. The statute required a finding of actual prejudice. Further, the court held that the legislature had the authority to limit the court's power to punish for contempt where the court was a creature of the legislature and not constitutionally established. The court held that § 33.020(1) was constitutional as applied to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded for resentencing.

State v. Lissy


CA No. A35041


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


85 Ore. App. 484; 737 P.2d 617; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 3770


August 28, 1986, Argued and submitted  
May 27, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 17, 1987. Petition for Review Allowed August 24, 1987 (304 Or 55).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. William A. Beckett, Judge. No. 10-84-08136.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of aggravated murder. He appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), assigning as error the trial court's denial of his motions to suppress certain recorded conversations between him and others and the recorded statement of a co-conspirator, and to suppress the co-conspirator's statements as violative of the Confrontation Clauses of U.S. Const. amend. VI and Or. Const. art. I, § 11.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's wife was strangled to death. A witness consented to making telephone calls to defendant that were recorded by the police in which she blackmailed defendant into paying for her silence. A witness who had arranged the meeting between defendant and the co-conspirator consented to the police recording her telephone calls with defendant in which the murder and the co-conspirator's payment were discussed. She recorded a conversation with the co-conspirator by a concealed microphone in which they discussed meeting with defendant and the murder. The court held that the telephone conversations were admissible under Or Rev. Stat. § 133.724. The police were not prohibited from recording a telephone conversation without a court order, as the witnesses consented. The co-conspirator's recorded statement was admissible without corroborating evidence under Or. Evid. Code 804(3)(c) as a statement against interest. Though the co-conspirator was unavailable, defendant's confrontation rights under Or. Const. art. I, § 11 and U.S. Const. amend. VI were not violated. There was an adequate indicia of reliability, as the statement fell within Or. Evid. Code 804(3)(c).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of aggravated murder.

Libertarian Party of Oregon v. Roberts


CA No. A40378


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


85 Ore. App. 450; 737 P.2d 137; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 3762


March 18, 1987, Argued and submitted  
May 20, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 10, 1987. Petition for Review Allowed August 24, 1987 (304 Or 55).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Robert B. McConville, Judge. No. 151821.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a minor political party and related individuals, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which was entered in favor of defendants, the Oregon Secretary of State and the Oregon Director of Elections and Public Records Division. Plaintiffs had filed a declaratory judgment action, contending that Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 248.008, 249.732 violated the First Amendment and portions of the Oregon Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs contended that Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 248.008 and 249.732 violated the First Amendment, various provisions of the Oregon Constitution pertaining to political, expression, and association rights, and the right to equal privileges and immunities assured by Or. Const. art. I, § 20. Their principal argument was that the five percent requirement for petitions under both of the challenged statutes set an unduly high threshold for placement on the ballot. Therefore, according to plaintiffs, the requirement ran afoul of the criteria that the United States Supreme Court and other courts had established for ballot qualification. Affirming, the court held that the United States Supreme Court had already upheld a Georgia statute that set a five percent petition requirement for independent or minor party candidates to qualify for the general election ballot, and Oregon statutes pertaining to ballot access were no more restrictive than the Georgia statutes previously considered by the United States Supreme Court. The court also found nothing that suggested that the analysis in the First Amendment cases was not equally appropriate in connection with the Oregon Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Grimes


CA No. A41687


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


85 Ore. App. 159; 735 P.2d 1277; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 3502


February 27, 1987, Argued and submitted  
April 22, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 26, 1987. Petition for Review Denied August 24, 1987 (304 Or 56).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Multnomah County. William J. Keys, Judge. No. 321775.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the District Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which entered judgment convicting him of unlawfully and knowingly offering and agreeing to pay a fee to engage in sexual conduct, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.007(1)(b). Defendant asserted that § 167.007(1)(b) violated Or. Const. art. I, § 8 because it punished protected speech.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.007(1)(b) by unlawfully and knowingly offering and agreeing to pay a fee to engage in sexual conduct. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court rejected defendant's argument that § 167.007(1)(b) was unconstitutional. The court held that Or. Const. art. I, § 8 foreclosed the enactment of any law directed to the substance of any subject of communication unless the scope of the restraint was wholly confined within some well-established pre-1859 historical exception. The court found that although Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.007(1) punished speech, it fit within an historical exception to the constitutional prohibition because the speech it prohibited was identical to that penalized by statutory solicitation and conspiracy provisions as well as pre-1859 common law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1043 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Guthrie


CA No. A40623


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


85 Ore. App. 164; 735 P.2d 1279; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 3508


December 11, 1986, Argued and submitted  
April 22, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 12, 1987. Petition for Review Allowed by Opinion August 24, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Multnomah County. Thomas L. Moultrie, Judge. No. M673968.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Multnomah County (Oregon), which convicted him of operating a motor vehicle without a proper permit in violation of ORS § 767.105. Defendant challenged the trial court's denial of his motion for judgment of acquittal.


OVERVIEW: The parties stipulated that a police officer observed defendant drive a dump truck, on a public highway, loaded with gravel and pulling a trailer with an asphalt spreader. The officer noted that the truck had expired tags and did not have a proper permit, as required by ORS § 767.105. After he was stopped, defendant unsuccessfully searched the truck for a permit and explained that the truck belonged to his father, for whom he worked. The officer testified that defendant did not dispute that he needed a proper permit. Defendant contended that he was entitled to an acquittal because the State failed to present evidence that he had intended to drive the truck without the proper permit. On appeal, the court reasoned that pursuant to ORS § 161.105 if a criminal offense constituted a violation rather than a crime, no culpable mental state was required, unless stated in ORS § 767.105. The court held that in designating the offense a violation rather than a crime, ORS § 767.105 clearly indicated a legislative intent to dispense with any culpable mental state requirement. Accordingly, a culpable mental state was not an element of the offense, and defendant's conviction was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1044 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Haase v. Eugene


CA No. A38327


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


85 Ore. App. 107; 735 P.2d 1258; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 3533


February 2, 1987, Argued and submitted  
April 22, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Gregory G. Foote, Judge. No. 16-83-03002.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff assault victim sought review of an order from the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant city in the assault victim's action under the Oregon Tort Claims Act (OTCA) and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 alleging that the city's police officers assaulted and beat him.


OVERVIEW: The assault victim brought an action against the city under the OTCA, alleging that the city's police officers assaulted and beat him. The court construed the complaint as also raising claims under § 1983 and for common law assault and battery. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the city without stating its reasons on the record. On appeal the court reversed, holding that: (1) the trial court erred in awarding the city summary judgment on the OTCA claim because Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.265(1) made public bodies liable for violations of that provision by their officers, employees, and agents acting within the scope of their employment or duties; thus, the city's liability existed whether or not the officers acted pursuant to a "custom or usage," and evidence on that point had no relevance to a § 1983 claim brought under the OTCA and (2) the trial court erred in awarding the city summary judgment on the § 1983 and common law assault and battery claims because the court could not determine as a matter of law that the officers were acting outside the scope of their employment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the city in the assault victim's action alleging the city was liable under the OTCA, § 1983, and common law assault and battery and remanded the case for further proceedings.

Hunter v. State


CA Nos. A37983 (Control), A37984 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


84 Ore. App. 698; 735 P.2d 1225; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 3386


November 20, 1986, Argued and submitted  
April 15, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 2, 1987. Petition for Review Allowed August 24, 1987 (304 Or 55).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Deschutes County. Walter I. Edmonds, Jr., Judge. Nos. 38367, 38667.



DISPOSITION: Judgment in each case reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, petitioners appealed judgments from the Circuit Court, Deschutes County (Oregon) that denied their petitions for post-conviction relief from convictions for driving under the influence of intoxicants (DUII), in violation of a city ordinance, which, pursuant to former Or. Rev. Stat. § 487.015, proscribed exactly the same conduct and provided the same penalties as the state DUII statute, former Or. Rev. Stat. § 487.540.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners claimed that Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.510(1) was unconstitutional under Or. Const. art. I, § 20, and the federal constitution, because it allowed post-conviction remedies to persons convicted of violating the state DUII statute but denied those remedies to persons who, like petitioners, although guilty of the same conduct, were convicted under a municipal ordinance. The court agreed with petitioners that, when the legislature granted a "privilege" to some, Or. Const. art. I, § 20 required that the privilege be available "upon the same terms" to any citizen or class of citizens. The interest in the availability of a procedure by which to vindicate constitutional violations outweighed any state justification for the deprivation of that interest. The court ruled that the language in Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.510(1), "the laws of this state," included convictions for violations of municipal ordinances when an ordinance was required by statute to be essentially the same as a state statute that prohibited the same conduct and provided the same penalties. To the extent that that they held to the contrary, the court overruled three prior decisions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgments that denied the petitions for post-conviction relief that were filed by petitioners.

State v. Stone


CA No. A40635
