PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. James R. Hargreaves, Judge. No. 10-86-03367.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Lane County (Oregon) that convicted him of coercion. Defendant contended that Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.275(1)(a) was overbroad.


OVERVIEW: The police responded to defendant's residence because of a family disturbance. Three police officers attempted to arrest defendant, but he threatened to injure his infant son whom he was holding, and the officers left the scene without making an arrest. Upon review, the court construed the § 163.275(1)(a) narrowly to eliminate possible applications that would render it unconstitutionally overbroad. The court concluded that the fear instilled in the other person had to be objectively reasonable, the physical injury that was feared had to be objectively reasonable, and the person to whom the injury was threatened had to be a specific person. The court found that defendant's conduct came squarely within its narrow construction of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for coercion.

State v. Crooks


CA No. A35935


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


84 Ore. App. 440; 734 P.2d 374; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 3213


May 23, 1986, Argued and submitted  
March 25, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Deschutes County. Walter I. Edmonds, Jr., Judge. No. 38053.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court, Deschutes County (Oregon) convicting defendant of selling an unregistered security in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 59.055, and ordering defendant to pay restitution to the purchasers.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was engaged in the business of buying and selling real estate security instruments. Although defendant had previously applied for registration of a certain security, registration was not actually granted at the time defendant sold the security to purchasers. Defendant's conviction for selling an unregistered security and a restitution award to the purchasers were affirmed. The term commercial paper in the securities law included only unsecured short term negotiable debt instruments issued by commercial entities. Whether the security fell within the class of exempt securities was a fact peculiarly within the personal knowledge of defendant. It was not unreasonable to require defendant to present proof of the exemption. The security in this case was not exempt. Three prerequisites for a restitution award were met: defendant engaged in criminal activity, purchasers suffered pecuniary damages, and a causal relationship between the two existed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed because it was not unreasonable to require defendant to prove that the securities were exempt, the securities were not exempt, and the three prerequisites for a restitution award to purchasers were met.

 

1049 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mitchell


CA No. A37813


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


84 Ore. App. 452; 734 P.2d 379; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 3214


July 28, 1986, Argued and submitted  
March 25, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 12, 1987. Petition for Review Denied June 30, 1987 (303 Or 590).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Gregory G. Foote, Judge. No. 10-85-01355.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed; sentence vacated; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), which convicted him of assault in the second degree pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.175.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended that he was entitled to a jury determination of facts that the court used to impose an enhanced sentence under Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.725 of the Dangerous Offender Act. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, but reversed and remanded as to his sentence. The court held that the initial predicate for the court to invoke the dangerous offender statute and proceed to determine if defendant was in fact a dangerous offender was the type of crime for which defendant was being sentenced. It had to be either a Class A felony or any lesser felony that seriously endangered the life or safety of another under Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.725(2). The lower court could determine as a matter of law whether the crime for which defendant was convicted was a felony and whether it was a Class A or a lesser felony. However, the lower court could not determine as a matter of law whether the felonious act seriously endangered another. The statute was unconstitutional insofar as it made the lower court the factfinder as to whether the crime seriously endangered the life or safety of another.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's conviction, but vacated the sentence and remanded for resentencing.

 

1050 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Freudenthaler


CA No. A38270


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


84 Ore. App. 531; 734 P.2d 894; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 3218



March 25, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 1, 1987. Petition for Review Denied May 27, 1987 (303 Or 455).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Jackson County. Mitchell A. Karaman, Judge. No. 85-2404C2. Submitted on respondent's motion to dismiss filed July 16, 1986.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court, Jackson County (Oregon), which entered defendant's guilty plea on a charge of robbery and did not allow defendant to withdraw the plea. The State filed a motion to dismiss, in which it argued that the court lacked jurisdiction to consider the merits of defendant's appeal, because Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.050 limited the appeal of a guilty plea to a review of the sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to a robbery charge and then appealed on the merits. He argued that the circuit court erred in accepting his guilty plea and should have allowed him to withdraw it. The State's argued that the court lacked jurisdiction under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.050 to consider the merits of defendant's appeal. The statute provided that a defendant who had pled guilty could appeal only the severity of his sentence. The court compared Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.050 with Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.040, which gave the court general appellate jurisdiction over convictions from district or circuit courts. Defendant argued that Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.050 created impermissible distinctions under the state and federal constitutions between those who pled guilty and those convicted in a trial. The court held that, in light of an analogous civil case, the distinction was not unconstitutional, particularly because a defendant could chose whether to put himself in the less advantageous appellate category. The court found that defendant's sentence was not unduly harsh and held that it lacked the power to consider defendant's other arguments. The court granted the State's motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's appeal of his guilty plea in the robbery case.

 

1051 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ferre


CA No. A38884


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


84 Ore. App. 459; 734 P.2d 888; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 3225


August 28, 1986, Argued and submitted  
March 25, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Coos County. Richard L. Barron, Judge. No. 85-2172.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to and was convicted of burglary in the second degree and placed on five years of probation. Arguing that a condition of probation that he not enter Coos County except for court appearances upon written court authorization was unconstitutionally cruel or excessive, defendant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court, Coos County (Oregon), which modified a condition of his probation.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was under an order restraining him from having any contact with his wife, he drove two and one-half hours to her home with a weapon and assaulted her and struggled with her boyfriend. For this incident, defendant was charged with three counts of burglary in the first degree, one count of assault in the fourth degree, and one count of harassment, from which his appeal stemmed. The court reversed the judgment. The court noted that an excessive or unusual punishment was one that was unrelated to the offense or that went beyond that necessary to accomplish the purpose of the punishment. The court found that, although precluding defendant from entering Coos County without permission promoted the purpose of protecting the victims in this case, it was broader than necessary to accomplish that purpose. The geographical restriction was unnecessarily broad, as defendant was not shown to pose a threat to anyone outside of his wife's area. The trial court could draw a more limited geographical area. If the area was sufficiently limited, the court could properly require defendant to obtain permission, on a showing of justification, to enter that area.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court, modifying a condition of defendant's probation that he not enter Coos County except for court appearances upon written court authorization. The court remanded the action for a greater geographical restriction.

State v. Langevin


CA No. A36402


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


84 Ore. App. 376; 733 P.2d 1383; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 3206


December 16, 1986, Submitted on remand  
March 18, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 15, 1987. Petition for Review Allowed June 23, 1987 (303 Or 534).


PRIOR HISTORY: On remand from the Oregon Supreme Court, State v. Langevin, 302 Or 298, 728 P2d 530 (1986). Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Rodney W. Miller, Judge. No. 146,798.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which, after remand, again convicted him of criminally negligent homicide.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress samples of blood taken from him, while he was unconscious in the hospital, and evidence derived from tests performed with the blood samples. At issue was whether the police had authority to take defendant's blood without a warrant, and whether they had authority to test it for its alcohol content without a warrant. Defendant was the driver in a one-car accident, in which his passenger was killed. The court was satisfied that the officers had probable cause to believe that defendant had been drinking alcohol and that alcohol was a factor in causing the accident. When the police directed that blood be taken at the hospital, defendant was under "actual or constructive restraint" so as to be under arrest for purposes of ORS 133.005(1). Because defendant was under arrest when his blood was drawn, the taking of blood samples while he was unconscious did not violate either the federal or state constitution. The vials of blood did not belong to defendant; thus, no search was involved in opening the vials and there was no additional seizure of the blood in testing its blood alcohol content.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

 

1053 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Juvenile Dep't of Benton County v. Strickland


CA No. A37958


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


84 Ore. App. 272; 733 P.2d 932; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 3120


September 10, 1986, Argued and submitted  
March 11, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Benton County. Frank D. Knight, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant child sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Benton County (Oregon), which, in a proceeding where the circuit court was sitting as a juvenile court, denied the child's motion to remand three citations charging traffic offenses from the municipal court to the juvenile court.


OVERVIEW: In 1972, a circuit court, sitting as a juvenile court pursuant to former Or. Rev. Stat. § 419.533(3), ordered all cases involving traffic offenses to be remanded to municipal court. In 1985, a 15-year-old was cited for traffic offenses. Pursuant to the "blanket" remand order, he was cited into municipal court. A circuit court denied the child's motion that the citations be remanded to juvenile court. The motion was denied and the court, on appeal, affirmed, ruling first that the case was not moot because it turned on whether the blanket remand order was valid as to a child who was then 15. While the child argued that statutory language limited blanket remand orders to traffic cases involving children 16 and over, the court disagreed. Given the statute's legislative history, the court found no legislative intention that the blanket remand language was subject to an age limit. Finally, the statute did not unconstitutionally discriminate against children under 16, because allowing prosecution of juveniles in adult courts for traffic offenses was a rational alternative to glutting juvenile courts with offenders who would not profit from rehabilitative efforts of the juvenile system.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court order denying the child's motion to remand three citations charging traffic offenses from the municipal court to the circuit court, which was sitting as a juvenile court.

 

1054 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Day


CA No. A39279


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


84 Ore. App. 291; 733 P.2d 937; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 3134


September 11, 1986, Argued and submitted  
March 11, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 24, 1987. Petition for Review Denied June 16, 1987 (303 Or 535).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Douglas County. Robert H. Anderson, Judge. No. M84-1158.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of conviction from the District Court, Douglas County (Oregon) for driving while her driver's license was suspended.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's driver's license was suspended under Or. Rev. Stat. § 482.593(1), because she was 17 years old and violated Or. Rev. Stat. § 471.430, which prohibited persons under 21 from possessing alcohol. Thereafter, she was convicted for driving while suspended. She appealed, arguing that the statute under which her driver's license was suspended violated the Oregon Constitution. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. Contrary to defendant's assertion, the group to whom the privilege of driving was denied was not a suspect class because it was not based upon an immutable personal characteristic that could be suspected of reflecting prejudice or stereotyped prejudgment. Further, the law bore a rational relationship to the State's legitimate interest in deterring drug and alcohol possession and use among young people and the promotion of highway safety. The court also found that the interest in possessing a driver's license was outweighed by the State's goals of promoting highway safety and deterring drug and alcohol use. Finally, the court found that the loss of driving privileges was not a disproportionate penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1055 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. McDonnell


CA No. 38776


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


84 Ore. App. 278; 733 P.2d 935; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 3182


September 30, 1986, Argued and submitted  
March 11, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 24, 1987. Petition for Review Denied May 27, 1987 (303 Or 455).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Douglas County. Ronald Poole, Judge. No. J85-0004.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Douglas County (Oregon) set aside an indictment charging defendant with aggravated murder. The offense was committed after defendant had escaped from a state penal and correctional facility. The indictment was set aside on the ground that the statute under which defendant was charged, Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.095(2)(f), was unconstitutional because it imposed an unconstitutional sentence. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that § 163.095(2)(f) violated Or. Const. art. I, § 20, the privileges and immunities provision, because there was no rational basis for imposing a more severe penalty for a murder committed by an individual on escape status than the penalty imposed on an individual who was in the process of escaping. The trial court also held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.095(2)(f) violated U.S. Const. amend VIII because being an escapee was not an aggravating circumstance which genuinely narrowed the class of persons eligible for the death penalty or reasonably justified the imposition of a more severe sentence on defendant compared to others found guilty of murder. The court stated that § 163.095(2)(f) did not impose any penalty but merely defined a crime. The court also stated that (1) the sentencing statute, Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.105(1), provided for the arguably unconstitutional sentence only after a conviction of aggravated murder, and defendant had not yet been convicted of any crime, much less aggravated murder; and (2) defendant could be sentenced for the lesser-included offense of murder. Thus, it was error to set aside the indictment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

State v. King


CA No. A34353


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON

Related proceeding at King v. Bd. of Parole & Post-Prison Supervision, 283 Ore. App. 689, 2017 Ore. App. LEXIS 182 (2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Clackamas County. Dale Jacobs, Judge. No. 82-247.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Clackamas County, after he was convicted of aggravated murder under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.095.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated murder after he allegedly hired a man to kill the victim. Defendant appealed asserting numerous procedural, evidentiary, and constitutional errors. The court affirmed. The court found the State's indictment met the requirements of the Oregon statute. The court further found that defendant had been mentally competent to stand trial and was mentally competent at the time Washington transferred defendant to Oregon authorities. Defendant also raised the issue of double jeopardy after his first trial ended abruptly in a mistrial. The court held that defendant was not entitled to a jury hearing on whether double jeopardy barred his second trial. The court found that the witness' highly prejudicial answer which caused the mistrial was not expected by the prosecution, and thus, the State neither intended nor was indifferent to the mistrial. Finally, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of aggravated murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

 

1057 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cornell


CA Nos. A38557 (Control), A39036 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


83 Ore. App. 559; 732 P.2d 922; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 2901


October 27, 1986, Argued and submitted  
February 11, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 24, 1987. Petition for Review Allowed May 27, 1987 (303 Or 454).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. Alan C. Bonebrake, Judge. Nos. 85-1106, 85-1107.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, the State appealed the judgments of the Circuit Court, Washington County (Oregon), which dismissed charges of aggravated murder against each defendant after it found Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.095(1)(e), which elevated murder to aggravated murder when it was committed during torture, to be unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were each charged with one count of aggravated murder in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.095(1)(e), and two counts of felony murder in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.115(1)(b), all related to the killing of the same victim. Both defendants moved for dismissal of the aggravated murder counts, and in substantially identical pretrial orders the trial court granted the motions, holding that Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.095(1)(e) was unconstitutionally vague under Or. Const. art. I, § 20 and § 21, The statute elevated murder to aggravated murder when it is committed in the course of torture. The legislature had not provided a statutory definition of torture, and the trial court reasoned that, in the absence of a definition, courts and juries were powerless to define and apply the term to the facts of a given case. The State appealed. The court affirmed because an allegation of murder by torture under the statute could not have been submitted constitutionally to a jury because a jury would have been allowed impermissibly to determine a defendant's guilt in an ad hoc manner, unregulated by legislative standards.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the aggravated murder counts against defendants and held the statute to be unconstitutional.

 

1058 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Salem v. Jungblut


CA No. A39094


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


83 Ore. App. 540; 732 P.2d 919; 1987 Ore. App. LEXIS 2934


September 16, 1986, Argued and submitted  
February 11, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Richard D. Barber, Judge. No. 151,391.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in a municipal court under Salem, Or., Rev. Code (SRC) 100.330, which was enacted on June 14, 1982, prohibiting DUII. Defendant appealed his conviction to the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon) and moved to dismiss the charge, contending that SRC 100.330 was invalid. The motion was denied, and defendant was convicted again of the offense after a trial de novo in the circuit court. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: SRC 100.330, the local ordinance under which defendant was tried and convicted, adopted by reference several State statutes prohibiting DUII and other vehicle-related crimes, one of those being former Or. Rev. Stat. § 487.540 which prohibited driving with a blood alcohol content (BAC) of .10 percent or higher. In October 1983, the State legislature repealed § 487.540 and immediately reenacted the same law with a prohibition against driving with a BAC of .08 percent or higher. In January 1984, defendant was arrested and cited for DUII in violation of the local ordinance. Defendant's BAC was .20 percent. In July 1984, the local ordinance was amended to conform to the .08 percent limit of amended § 487.540. Defendant contended that the amendment of § 487.540 rendered the local ordinance pursuant to which he was convicted invalid because the ordinance no longer incorporated existing State law. The court, limiting the appeal to issues concerning the constitutionality of the local ordinance, dismissed the appeal. The court found that the ordinance was not unconstitutional because the city which adopted it had not attempted to adopt future amendments to § 487.540.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

1060 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Heuker


CA No. A38544


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


83 Ore. App. 180; 730 P.2d 1258; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 4407


June 27, 1986, Argued and submitted  
December 31, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Multnomah County. Joseph F. Ceniceros, Judge. No. K02390.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Oregon appealed the judgment of the District Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which sustained defendant's demurrer and dismissed the charge against him for the unlawful possession of steelhead trout. The charge was dismissed on the ground that the unlawful possession of steelhead did not constitute an offense.


OVERVIEW: The State alleged that defendant violated Or. Admin. R. 635-06-230. Defendant argued that the mere possession of steelhead was not prohibited by Or. Rev. Stat. § 509.031. The State claimed that § 509.031 authorized the Oregon Fish and Wildlife Commission to promulgate the regulation. Defendant argued that the Commission exceeded the scope of its delegated rulemaking authority. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred in sustaining the demurrer. Because the violation of any regulation promulgated by the Commission in carrying out § 509.031(1) was a Class A misdemeanor under Or. Rev. Stat. § 506.991(1), the Commission did not exceed the scope of its delegated authority when it declared that violating the prohibition set forth in Or. Admin. R. 635-06-230 constituted an unlawful act. If the State did not prove that defendant possessed the steelhead for purposes other than to deliver it to the State, it would not prove a violation. Additionally, the court found no unlawful delegation of legislative power.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded.

State v. Okeke

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the District Court, Multnomah County (Oregon) that convicted her of carrying a concealed weapon in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.240.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the trial court's denial of her pretrial motion to suppress evidence, arguing that the search of her purse and seizure of a pistol from it by an employe of a detoxification center violated her right against unreasonable searches and seizures under Or. Const. art. I, § 9. In reversing, the court held that the search was state action because the center had authority over defendant similar to what the police would have had if the police had searched her purse. Because the search was unnecessary and, therefore, unreasonable, the trial court erred in denying the motion to suppress.

1062 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Huntley


CA Nos. A36731 (Control), A36732, A36733 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


82 Ore. App. 350; 728 P.2d 868; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 4104


May 21, 1986, Argued and submitted  
November 12, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 19, 1986; Petition for Review Denied February 3, 1987
Reconsideration Denied December 19, 1986. Petition for Review Denied February 3, 1987 (302 Or 594).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Duane R. Ertsgaard, Judge. Nos. 151,748, 151,749, 151,750.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Marion County Circuit Court (Oregon), which convicted him of providing a false statement under the election laws in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 260.715(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a candidate for state representative and, in the course of his campaigns, he signed and submitted a form to the secretary of state for publication in a voters' pamphlet that contained a statement that he had two associate degrees. The parties stipulated that defendant had not received any degree. Defendant argued that his false statements were not "required under the election laws" and did not fall within § 260.715(1). The court upheld the conviction. When defendant chose to file the candidate's statement, its substance was circumscribed by law, and the statements regarding his educational background were "required under the election laws." Defendant's statement included a provision that he certified the information about his occupation, educational and occupational background, and prior governmental experience as true. Although it was not a sworn statement, it was certified as true. The statement required by § 251.085 was one of fact, and defendant's educational background was a verifiable fact that was not open to dispute or debate. Defendant falsified those facts, was trying to mislead the voting public, and would have undermined the electoral process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Sekne v. Portland


CA No. A36443


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


81 Ore. App. 630; 726 P.2d 959; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 3946


April 16, 1986, Argued and submitted  
October 15, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 19, 1986. Petition for Review Denied February 18, 1987 (302 Or 615).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Robert P. Jones, Judge. No. A8504-02530.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; and remanded for proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiffs, tavern owner and nude dancer, and held that Portland, Or. City Code §§ 14.36.010 and 14.36.020 were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought an action challenging the two city ordinance that prohibited nude dancing in establishments that served alcohol. The lower court held that the ordinances were unconstitutional, and the court affirmed as to the nude dancing. The court found that the ordinances were not repealed or superseded by Or. Rev. Stat. § 471.045 because it did not forbid or permit nude dancing and was therefore not directed at the ordinances in question. The court determined that nudity alone did not take dancing out of the realm of expression protected by Or. Const. art. I, § 8 and therefore, Portland, Or., City Code § 14.36.010 extended into areas of constitutionally protected expression. The court held that the portions of the ordinance, which prohibited nude dancing, were overbroad and invalid, but could be severed from the remainder of the ordinance. The court stated that the lower court erroneously found the other portions of the ordinance invalid. The court held that as § 14.36.020 did not prohibit nude dancing, its validity was not at issue in this matter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that the prohibition against nude dancing was unconstitutional, but reversed as to the remaining sections of the ordinance.

 

1064 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vasey


Nos. B67-654, CA A38369


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


80 Ore. App. 765; 723 P.2d 1068; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 3281


Argued and Submitted June 16, 1986  
August 20, 1986, Filed. Reversed and Remanded August 20, 1986. Petition for Review Denied November 20, 1986


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Lane County, Winfrid K. Liepe, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from an order of the District Court, Lane County (Oregon), which sustained defendant's demurrer to an indictment against him under ORS 166.470 (Oregon). Defendant was charged with the sale or transfer of a concealable firearm between nonlicensed persons when the purchaser was not personally known to him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the "not personally known" component of the statute was unconstitutionally vague, in violation of Or. Const. art. I, § 20. Reversing, the court determined that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague in describing the prohibited conduct. The court noted that a vague statute failed to adequately apprise the public of what conduct was proscribed. A judicial interpretation could save a statute that was attacked as vague, but only if the construction maintained a reasonable fidelity to the legislature's words and apparent intent. The court concluded that, in the context of the statute, the words "not personally known to the vendor" could be interpreted to uphold the statute and give it meaning. The requirement had two aspects for a nonlicensed vendor. The vendor had to know the purchaser's identity and the vendor had to know the purchaser to the extent that he could reasonably believe that the purchaser was not within a class of persons prohibited from owning or possessing a concealable firearm. The words of the statute, in context, were not vague but conveyed a clear meaning that something that which judges and juries were capable of applying.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded.

Payless Drug Stores Northwest, Inc. v. Brown


Nos. 83-1-1014; CA A30985


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


80 Ore. App. 255; 722 P.2d 31; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 3050


Submitted on Remand November 5, 1985  
July 2, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 3, petition for Review Denied October 28, 1986


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Umatilla County.

Richard J. Courson, Judge.

Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand, defendants, parents of an unemancipated teenage daughter, sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Umatilla County (Oregon), which denied their motion for summary judgment in an action brought by plaintiff retailer to recover damages for shoplifting, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.875(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendants appealed a judgment entered against them in an action filed by the retailer to recover damages resulting from the arrest of defendants' daughter for shoplifting. The jury returned a verdict for the retailer, and defendants filed a motion for summary judgment alleging that the shoplifting statute, Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.875(2), was unconstitutional. The trial court denied the motion, and on appeal the court refused to review the denial. On further appeal, the case was remanded for consideration on the assignment of error. Affirming the trial court's denial, the court held that the statute did not deny parents the right to choose how to teach their children or bar them from making decisions concerning them, but encouraged parents to teach lawful behavior. The court further held that the standard of review was not strict scrutiny, but whether the statute advanced a legitimate state purpose and whether the means chosen were rationally related to achieving that purpose. The court concluded that the deterrence of juvenile shoplifting was a legitimate state purpose and that the imposition of vicarious liability on parents was rationally related to that purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendants' motion for summary judgment, in the retailer's action to recover damages for shoplifting.

1067 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Buchanan v. Wood


CA No. A32883


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


79 Ore. App. 722; 720 P.2d 1285; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 2882


May 24, 1985, Argued and submitted  
June 4, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted May 24, 1985; Reconsideration Denied August 1, Petition for Review Denied October 21, 1986
Reconsideration Denied August 1, 1986. Petition for Review Denied October 21, 1986 (302 Or 158).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Stephen B. Herrell, Judge. No. A8306-04179.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed on appeal; reversed on cross-appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which declared that the Court Reorganization Act, 1981 Or. Laws 3, preempted a Multmomah County Home Rule charter provision for election of a district court clerk and that defendant was not entitled to a salary for the position. Plaintiffs cross-appealed from the award of attorney fees to defendant for trial and for appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was elected by the county as district court clerk and a salary for the position was approved. As assistant to the district court administrator, defendant was paid a salary by the state as well. The lower court found that the Court Reorganization Act abolished the county office of district court clerk and defendant was not entitled to a salary for that office. Defendant asserted that the Act did not preempt the charter amendment, which created the office of district court clerk. Defendant conceded that under the Act the state took over the duties that had been assigned to him as district court clerk, but argued that the county should have assigned to him other duties that the state did not take over. The court found that the state's preemption of the duties of district court clerk did preempt the office and nullified it. Also, the state's preemption of all of the functions of the office of district court clerk did not impinge on the county's freedom to choose its own political form. Defendant was not entitled to a salary for holding a non-existent office. The court agreed that the lower court erred when it awarded attorney fees to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that defendant was not entitled to a salary for the position in question. The court reversed the award of attorney fees to defendant for trial and for appeal.

Kay v. David Douglas School Dist.


CA No. A32742


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


79 Ore. App. 384; 719 P.2d 875; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 2856


April 19, 1985, Argued and submitted  
May 21, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted April 19, 1985; Reconsideration Denied August 8, 1986
Reconsideration Denied August 8, 1986. Petition for Review Allowed November 12, 1986 (302 Or 194).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Robert P. Jones, Judge. No. A8404-02438.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school district officials sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which entered a judgment enjoining the school officials from sponsoring, permitting, or encouraging the inclusion of formal prayer at a high school graduation.


OVERVIEW: Some graduating high school students urged the school board to not include a vocal prayer at their high school graduation. The majority of students approved of the use of the vocal prayer at the graduation. The school district paid public funds for the use of an auditorium for the graduation. The school board adopted a resolution directing the superintendent and principal to include the prayer at the graduation. The objecting students filed suit, and the trial court issued an injunction prohibiting the school district from sponsoring, permitting or encouraging the inclusion of formal prayer at the graduation. The court affirmed, holding that the effect of the prayer was to create the impression that government was sponsoring or endorsing religion. The Oregon constitution forbade the majority of a population from compelling a graduation ceremony to be opened with a vocal, public prayer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of an injunction against the school district.

 

1069 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bennett


CA No. A34494


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


79 Ore. App. 267; 719 P.2d 38; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 2795


July 24, 1985, Argued and submitted  
May 14, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted July 24, 1985; Reconsideration Denied July 11, 1986; Petition for Review Denied September 3, 1986
Reconsideration Denied July 11, 1986. Petition for Review Denied September 3, 1986 (301 Or 667).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Klamath County. Donald A. W. Piper, Judge. No. 84-207.



DISPOSITION: Conviction for burglary in first degree reversed; minimum sentence for use of firearm in committing felony vacated; remanded for entry of conviction for burglary in second degree and for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court, Klamath County (Oregon), which convicted him for burglary in the first degree, theft in the first degree and possession of a firearm in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.270.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for burglary in the first degree, theft in the first degree and possession of a firearm in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.270. On appeal, defendant argued that he was improperly convicted of first degree burglary by virtue of his having used a screwdriver to gain entry to a gun shop, under Or. Rev. Stat. § 164.235(2); and that the circuit court erred in imposing a minimum sentence pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.610. The court reversed and held that the circuit court erred in convicting defendant of burglary in the first degree on the basis of his use of a screwdriver to gain entry to the gun shop. Defendant was convicted under an unconstitutionally vague statute, which defined a burglar's tool to include an item "commonly used for committing or facilitating a forcible entry." The court held that the circuit court erred in imposing a minimum sentence, pursuant to § 161.610, for using or threatening to use a firearm in the commission of a felony. There was no evidence that defendant or his accomplice loaded any of the guns stolen from the gun shop or used them in any way other than as proceeds in the burglary of the gun shop.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment convicting defendant for burglary in first degree, vacated the minimum sentence for use of firearm in committing felony, and remanded for entry of conviction for burglary in second degree and for resentencing.

 

1070 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Danielson


No. A34472


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


79 Ore. App. 278; 719 P.2d 44; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 2813


October 22, 1985, Argued and submitted  
May 14, 1986 Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted October 22, 1985; Reconsideration Denied July 11, Petition for Review Denied July 29, 1986
Reconsideration Denied July 11, 1986. Petition for Review Denied July 29, 1986 (301 Or 445).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Maurice K. Merten, Judge. No. 10-84-03506.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), which sustained defendant's demurrer to an indictment for aggravated murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.103 was unconstitutional because it allowed the State to present evidence of a prior homicide conviction, unless defendant stipulated to it. The trial court sustained defendant's demurrer to an indictment for aggravated murder. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for trial. The court held that the legislature could include a prior conviction for homicide as an element of aggravated murder. Permitting the introduction of a prior homicide conviction in the guilt determination phase of an aggravated murder trial did not violate Or. Const. art. I, § 11 or § 12. There was no merit in defendant's argument that Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.103 compelled an accused to incriminate himself through a stipulation. Proof of the prior conviction was usually a mere formality. A defendant was not required to stipulate it, and if he chose not to, the State was required to prove the conviction beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded for trial.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer sought judicial review of the decision from the Workers' Compensation Board (Oregon), which awarded respondent claimant permanent total disability. The employer argued that Or. Rev. Stat. § 656.278 unconstitutionally delegated legislative authority to the Board.


OVERVIEW: The claimant sought own motion relief, and the Board awarded the claimant permanent total disability benefits. The employer appealed, arguing that Or. Rev. However, the court reversed the decision to award benefits because the Board failed to give the employer the 20 days required by Or. Admin. R. 438-12-005 to state its own position after the claimant had requested own motion relief.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision to award the claimant benefits and remanded the cause for further consideration.

State v. Redwine


CA No. A35146


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


79 Ore. App. 25; 717 P.2d 1239; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 2687


October 22, 1985, Argued and submitted  
April 23, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted October 22, 1985; Reconsideration Denied June 6, Petition for Review Allowed July 15, 1986
Reconsideration Denied June 6, 1986. Petition for Review Allowed July 15, 1986 (301 Or 338).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Josephine County. Loyd O'Neal, Judge Pro Tempore. No. 84-400-C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court, Josephine County (Oregon), which convicted him for kidnapping in the first degree, robbery in the first degree, and assault in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for kidnapping in the first degree, robbery in the first degree, and assault in the first degree. On appeal, defendant contended that his testimony was improperly limited by the circuit court because he had failed to provide a notice of alibi pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 135.455. The court affirmed and held that although the circuit court erred in sustaining the State's objection to and striking defendant's testimony to establish that he did not participate in the crimes charged, the error was harmless because the excluded testimony would not likely have changed the outcome. Section 135.455 did not bar a defendant from denying his participation in a crime charged for failure to give a notice of alibi. However, there was substantial and convincing evidence of guilt. The victim, who was acquainted with defendant, testified in detail about defendant's presence at the crime scene and his participation in the crimes charged. Other witnesses also placed defendant at the crime scene.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment convicting defendant for kidnapping in the first degree, robbery in the first degree, and assault in the first degree.

 

1074 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Troute v. Aero Mayflower Transit Co.


CA No. A34614


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


78 Ore. App. 564; 718 P.2d 745; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 2669


June 28, 1985, Argued and submitted  
April 16, 1986, Filed; Argued and submitted June 28, 1985


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Lane County. Winfrid K. Liepe, Judge. No. 84-90098.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant carrier sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Lane County (Oregon), which awarded attorney fees pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 20.080 to plaintiff shipper in an action to recover damages for goods lost in transit. The carrier did not seek review of the trial court's award of damages.


OVERVIEW: The complaint included a claim for attorney fees under Or. Rev. Stat. § 20.080, which, at the time when the an action was brought, provided for reasonable attorney fees in an action for damages for injury or wrong to the person or property, or both, of another where the amount pleaded was $ 3,000 or less. The carrier sought review of a judgment of the of only the attorney fees award, contending that liability for lost goods was governed by the Interstate Commerce Act. The carrier claimed that the Interstate Commerce Act preempted Or. Rev. Stat. § 20.080 and that, therefore, attorney fees were not recoverable. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which awarded attorney fees to the shipper. The court held that the Interstate Commerce Act did not prohibit the recovery of attorney fees under Or. Rev. Stat. § 20.080. The state law was within the state's inherent powers and did not conflict with the Interstate Commerce Act or infringe its policy. In addition, there was no clear evidence of a congressional intent to preempt state law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which awarded attorney fees to the shipper in an action to recover damages for goods lost in transit.

State v. Hoehne

State v. Henry


CA No. A26439


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


78 Ore. App. 392; 717 P.2d 189; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 2626


January 20, 1984, Argued and submitted; December 4, 1985, Resubmitted In Banc  
April 9, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted January 20, 1984; resubmitted in banc December 4, 1985; Reconsideration Denied July 11, petition for reivew allowed September 3, 1986
Reconsideration Denied July 11, 1986. Petition for Review Allowed September 3, 1986 (301 Or 666).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Deschutes County. John M. Copenhaver, Judge. Nos. 31300, 31301.



DISPOSITION: In case no. 31300, conviction reversed; in case no. 31301, conviction reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court, Deschutes County (Oregon), which convicted him of dissemination of obscene material pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.087(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of dissemination of obscene material. He demurred to the indictment on the ground that the facts stated did not constitute an offense because § 167.087 was unconstitutional. He stipulated that he sold the magazines in question. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that because § 167.087 was used by judges, juries, and potential defendants to assess the criminality of particular conduct, its definitions were not sufficiently precise to determine whether particular sexually explicit material was legally obscene. It was not acceptable, as a matter of state constitutional law, that the precise course of the line dividing obscene expression from protected expression be uncertain and that a person who chose to disseminate sexually explicit materials had to bear the risk of that uncertainty. The constitutional right to communicate freely on "any subject whatever" guaranteed by Or. Const. art. I, § 8, required more than the statute provided by way of guidance. A person who traded in sexually explicit materials could not discern that his wares were legally obscene under the statute, and a trial judge was left with no legal standard to apply.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which had convicted defendant of dissemination of obscene material.

 

1077 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Farley


CA No. A35584


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


78 Ore. App. 102; 714 P.2d 1079; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 2508


November 27, 1985, Argued and submitted  
February 26, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted November 27, 1985; Reconsideration Denied March 28, petition for review allowed May 28, 1986
Reconsideration Denied March 28, 1986. Petition for Review Allowed May 28, 1986 (301 Or 165).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Josephine County. Gerald E. Neufeld, Judge. No. 84-1870-C.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Circuit Court, Josephine County (Oregon) with feloniously driving while suspended under former Or. Rev. Stat. § 487.560, repealed by 1983 Or. Laws ch. 338, § 978. The trial court dismissed the indictment on the ground that defendant's guilty plea to driving under the influence of intoxicants, based on the same criminal episode, barred prosecution of the driving while suspended charge. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court found that prosecution of defendant on the charge of driving while suspended was not barred by his guilty plea to driving under the influence of intoxicants (DUI). The two charges were "based on the same criminal episode" as that term was used in Or. Rev. Stat. § 131.515(2). However, the indictment on the driving while suspended charge was filed before he pleaded guilty to the DUI charge. Therefore, the indictment was not later than 30 days after the entry of the guilty plea. Or. Rev. Stat. § 131.525(2) provided that defendant's guilty plea did not bar this prosecution. The statute allowed defendant to move to vacate the previous plea and judgment within 30 days of his arraignment on the driving while suspended charge. He did not do so. The omission of no contest pleas from Or. Rev. Stat. § 131.525(2) may have been due to legislative oversight; however, defendant could not base a privileges and immunities attack on the putative different double jeopardy effect of two pleas when it was his choice and not the government's that determined which results followed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's dismissal of defendant's indictment on a charge of driving while suspended and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

1078 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Schoeneman v. Meyer


CA No. A34300


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


78 Ore. App. 89; 715 P.2d 100; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 2547


October 24, 1985, Argued and submitted  
February 26, 1986 Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted October 24, 1985; Reconsideration Denied April 11, petition for review denied May 20, 1986
Reconsideration Denied April 11, 1986. Petition for Review Denied May 20, 1986 (301 Or 165).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Linn County. Frank D. Knight and Wendell H. Tompkins, Judges. No. 83-1191.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed a decision from the Circuit Court, Linn County (Oregon), which granted the motions for summary judgment filed by one landlocked neighbor and a second neighbor in the landowners' action for declaratory and injunctive relief. The landowners sought to enjoin the defendants from expanding or using a way of necessity established pursuant to former Or. Rev. Stat. § 376.105 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Years before this litigation commenced, the state declared a statutory way of necessity over three adjoining farms pursuant to former Or. Rev. Stat. § 376.105 et seq. One farm was landlocked and could only be reached by the way of necessity, a gateway. The owner of one of the farms filed an action for declaratory and injunctive relief against his two neighbors. He sought to enjoin the landlocked neighbor from expanding its use of the gateway and to enjoin the other neighbor from using the gateway at all. The circuit court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court explained why the landowner was not entitled to relief as a matter of law. A statutory way of necessity was open to the public for anyone who wanted to use it. This included public roads or gateways used as access to residences and farms. The landlocked neighbor was clearly entitled to expand its use to serve additional residences on his property. The other neighbor was entitled to use the gateway not only as a member of the public but as an abutting property owner. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's decision to grant defendants' motions for summary in the landowner's action to enjoin them from use of a way of necessity.

 

1079 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Oregon Education Asso. v. Paulus


CA No. A35391


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


78 Ore. App. 32; 714 P.2d 1060; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 2651


January 13, 1986, Argued and submitted  
February 26, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted January 13, 1986; Reconsideration Denied April 11, Petition for Review Allowed April 29, 1986
Reconsideration Denied April 11, 1986. Petition for Review Allowed April 29, 1986 (301 Or 76).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Richard D. Barber, Judge. No. 152580.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, union and affiliated individuals, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which granted the motions to dismiss of defendants, Secretary of State of Oregon, Attorney General of Oregon, and chief practitioners. The action concerned an initiative petition and challenged official actions under Or. Rev. Stat. § 183.484, and the Secretary's actions under Or. Rev. Stat. § 246.910.


OVERVIEW: The action sought to prohibit the processing and circulation of an initiative petition in favor of submitting a constitutional amendment to voters at a general election. The initiative petition concerned pay levels and pensions of public employees. Plaintiffs argued that the initiative petition violated the requirement under Or. Const. art. IV, § 1(2)(d), that such petitions could only concern one subject. The trial court held that pre-election review by courts to determine if the requirement was met was impermissible. The court affirmed the judgment. The legislature's use of "proposed" in § 1(2)(d), and its failure to change "act" into "bill" in Or. Const. art. IV, § 20, upon amendment, showed its intent regarding when judicial intervention was permissible. Given courts' holdings before the amendment of Or. Const. art. IV, § 1(2)(d), (4)(b), that single subject review was not available before elections, it was unlikely that "proposed" in Or. Const. art. IV, § 1(2)(d), was intended to change the prior holdings in a non-overt manner. The court found a preference against courts intervening in legislative processes or interfering with voters' abilities on referendum proposals.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that granted the motions to dismiss of the Secretary, the Attorney General, and the chief practitioners.

Molodyh v. Truck Ins. Exchange


CA No. A33853


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


77 Ore. App. 619; 714 P.2d 257; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 2480


June 26, 1985, Argued and submitted  
February 12, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 9, 1986. Petition for Review Allowed July 1, 1986 (301 Or 320).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Rodney W. Miller, Judge. No. 149,522.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which granted defendant insurers summary judgment on the insured's action to seek a jury determination concerning the value of his loss under a fire insurance policy.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff's property was damaged by a fire. His insurance policy contained an arbitration provision as required by Or. Rev. Stat. § 743.648 which provided for an appraisal hearing to determine the amount of loss sustained by an insured. An appraisal hearing was held and plaintiff brought an action on the policy to have a jury determine the loss. The trial court granted summary judgment to the insurers and held that the statutorily required arbitration provision was binding on both parties. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court found that the economic necessity to insure all valuable structures against fire did not provide the insured with any other realistic alternative than to accept the insurer's policy that contained the statutorily mandated arbitration provision. The court held that the contract was one of adhesion to which the insured was not a voluntary party and that § 743.648 was unconstitutional because it deprived the insured of his constitutional right to a jury under Or. Const. art. I, § 17.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's summary judgment in favor of the insurers and held that the insured did not waive his right to have the value of his loss determined by a jury.

 

1081 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Seattle-First Nat'l Bank v. Umatilla County


CA No. A33950


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


77 Ore. App. 283; 713 P.2d 33; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 2919


May 16, 1985, Argued and submitted; December 4, 1985, Resubmitted In Banc  
January 22, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted May 16, 1985, at Pendleton, Oregon; resubmitted in banc December 4, 1985; Reconsideration Denied March 7, petition for Review Denied March 25, 1986
Reconsideration Denied March 7, 1986. Petition for Review Denied March 25, 1986 (300 Or 704).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Umatilla County. J. F. Olsen, Judge. No. 84-5-477.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mortgagee appealed from the order of the Circuit Court, Umatilla County (Oregon), which dismissed its complaint to challenge the validity of a tax foreclosure conducted by defendant county for failure to state a claim for relief pursuant to Or. R. Civ. P. 21A(8). The trial court held that newspaper publication of a foreclosure action under former Or. Rev. Stat. § 312.040(1) satisfied Fourteenth Amendment due process requirements.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagee did not have actual notice of the foreclosure until after the one-year redemption period expired. The statute formerly provided that newspaper publication of notice of foreclosure four times was sufficient to put all persons claiming an interest in the property on notice. A recent amendment, not applicable to the case, required mailed notice to record lienholders. On appeal, the court held that the Fourteenth Amendment required the state to provide notice reasonably calculated, under all the circumstances, to apprise interested parties of the pendency of an action that affected a property interest, and afford them an opportunity to present their objections. The court held that the statute was constitutional as applied to a landowner because it supplemented at least three years of written notices of delinquency as well as a notice of the right of redemption. The court reversed and held that newspaper publication alone, without mailed or served notice, violated due process as to the holder of a recorded mortgage, notwithstanding the right of the mortgagee to make a request for mailed notice, because the state had an affirmative duty to provide sufficient notice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court that had held that the mortgagee did not state a claim for relief. The court remanded the case.

State v. Mattila


CA No. A34261


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


77 Ore. App. 219; 712 P.2d 832; 1986 Ore. App. LEXIS 2326


June 19, 1985, Argued and submitted  
January 8, 1986 filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and Submitted June 19, 1985; Reconsideration Denied March 28, petition for Review Denied April 29, 1986
Reconsideration Denied March 28, 1986. Petition for Review Denied April 29, 1986 (301 Or 77).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Washington County. Michael McElligott, Judge. M No. 56583-B.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the trial court (Oregon) for obstructing governmental or judicial administration, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.235.


OVERVIEW: When deputies arrived at defendant's residence to serve eviction papers, the door was blocked. Defendant did not make any attempt to remove the crutch blocking the door so that the deputies could enter the house but, instead, stood at the front window shouting at them. At one point, defendant asked his mother if they could shoot the deputies. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that: (1) Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.235 was constitutional; (2) whether evidence of defendant's behavior in keeping the door wedged shut was sufficient to constitute physical interference within the meaning of the statute was a question for the jury; (3) the evidence supported a finding that the deputies were placed in fear by defendant's words and actions; (4) the trial court did not err in admitting a carbine found in defendant's bedroom after the deputies entered the house because it was relevant to the issue of defendant's intent to intimidate them and the need for the evidence was substantial given that it was the only physical evidence the State had of defendant's intent to shoot the deputies; and (5) the trial court did not err in instructing the jury on "intimidation."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1083 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Samuel v. Board of Chiropractic Examiners


CA No. A25531


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


77 Ore. App. 53; 712 P.2d 132; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 4348


February 1, 1985, Argued and submitted  
December 26, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted February 1, 1985; Reconsideration Denied February 14, petition for Review Denied April 1, 1986
Reconsideration Denied February 14, 1986. Petition for Review Denied April 1, 1986 (300 Or 704).


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review from Board of Chiropractic Examiners.



DISPOSITION: Remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant chiropractor sought review of a decision from the Board of Chiropractic Examiners (Oregon), which suspended his chiropractic license for four years and permanently revoked his right to perform minor surgery. The Board found that the chiropractor had performed major surgery, a vasectomy, in violation of the chiropractic licensing statutes.


OVERVIEW: The chiropractor performed a vasectomy on one of his patients. The Board of Chiropractic Examiners learned of the surgery and notified the chiropractor that it intended to revoke his license on the ground that chiropractors were not authorized to perform vasectomies under Oregon law. At the hearing, the chiropractor did not deny performing the vasectomy, but argued that a vasectomy was "minor surgery" under Or. Rev. Stat. § 684.010(4). The Board disagreed. It found that a vasectomy was not "minor surgery" and that, therefore, it was prohibited "major surgery." The chiropractor's first assignment raised the issue of whether the Board was required to promulgate rules defining "major surgery" and further defining "minor surgery" before applying those statutory terms. On appeal, the court affirmed the finding of the Board holding that while the question of what was "minor surgery" was a question of law for the courts, they Board had not erred in determining that the vasectomy was "major surgery." The court held further that the appearance of impropriety concerning extra record discussions required a redetermination of the appropriate sanction to impose.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the decision of the Board of Chiropractic Examiners for a reconsideration of the appropriate sanction.

 

1084 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Hogue v. Olympic Bank


CA No. A33411


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


76 Ore. App. 17; 708 P.2d 605; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 3950


May 3, 1985, Argued and submitted  
October 30, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted May 3, 1985; Reconsideration Denied January 17, 1986; Petition for review denied February 11, 1986
Reconsideration Denied January 17, 1986. Petition for Review Denied February 11, 1986 (300 Or 545).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Kathleen B. Nachtigal, Judge. No. A1999.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions to reinstate adoption decree.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant natural father's personal representative sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 109.381 could not be applied to validate an adoption decree void for lack of consent or notice and which entered a judgment for respondents, a natural mother's personal representative and a daughter, in an action to vacate a decree of adoption.


OVERVIEW: The mother gave birth to an illegitimate daughter. The mother's father adopted the child. The mother neither consented to the adoption nor received notice of the adoption proceedings. In 1947, the child's adopted mother told the mother about the adoption. The mother filed an action to vacate the adoption decree in 1984. The mother died after filing the action. The trial court entered a judgment for the mother's personal representative and the child. On appeal, the court held that the adoption decree was void when it was entered because the adoption court had no jurisdiction to enter it without consent from or notice to the mother. However, if the legislature had power to bar challenges to tax foreclosure decrees void for want of jurisdiction, it could perceive no reason why it could not do so with respect to adoption decrees. Section 109.381 reflected a legislative purpose to lend finality to adoption decrees, even those arising out of proceedings suffering from jurisdiction defects. The mother had one year from the 1959 enactment of § 109.381 to challenge the decree. That was a reasonable time period. Thus, her attack on the adoption decree was barred by § 109.381.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision. The case was remanded with instructions to reinstate the adoption decree.

 

1085 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Portland v. Gatewood


CA No. A34366


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


76 Ore. App. 74; 708 P.2d 615; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 3958


May 6, 1985, Argued and submitted  
October 30, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted May 6, 1985; Reconsideration Denied December 20, 1985; Petition for review denied January 14, 1986
Reconsideration Denied December 20, 1985. Petition for Review Denied January 14, 1986 (300 Or 477).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Multnomah County. Frank L. Bearden, Judge. DA No. 279144.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a judgment from District Court of Multnomah County (Oregon), which dismissed a charge of indecent exposure against defendant on the ground that Portland, Or., City Code § 14.24.060, under which he was charged, violated Or. Const. art. I, § 8, and the First and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The city challenged dismissal of the charge of indecent exposure against defendant, arguing that the trial court erred in granting defendant's demurrer and in holding the city's indecent exposure ordinance was overbroad. Defendant had argued that the ordinance was overbroad because some of the conduct it proscribed was protected speech. The trial court agreed. The trial court held that Portland, Or., City Code § 14.24.060 unconstitutionally outlawed the act of exposure itself, that is the nudity. The court disagreed and reversed the judgment, holding that a statute that reached constitutionally protected behavior only rarely when compared with legitimate applications of the law need not succumb to an overbreadth attack. The court held that such a statute could be interpreted as impliedly excluding the protected activity from coverage. The court held that Portland, Or., City Code § 14.24.060 was focused on the goal of regulating conduct determined to be injurious to the public health, safety, and morals by prohibiting public nudity or indecent exposure not intended as a protected symbolic or communicative act. The court remanded the case for trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissed the charge was reversed and the case was remanded for trial.

Cooper v. Eugene School Dist.


CA No. A31423

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted February 11, 1985; Reconsideration Denied January 17, both petition for review allowed February 25, 1986
Duncan's Reconsideration and Eugene School Dist.'s Reconsideration Denied January 17, 1986. Both Petitions for Review Allowed February 25, 1986 (300 Or 562).


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review from Superintendent of Public Instruction.



DISPOSITION: Order set aside.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant teacher sought judicial review, under Or. Rev. Stat. § 183.480(1), of an order of appellee state superintendent of public instruction, who revoked the teacher's certification because she wore religious dress while teaching in a public school.


OVERVIEW: A public school teacher wore religious dress while teaching, in conformity with her Sikh beliefs. The state superintendent of public instruction revoked the teacher's certification for violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 342.650. The teacher sought judicial review of the order of the superintendent, as provided for by Or. Rev. Stat. § 183.480(1). On review, the court concluded that the teacher did offend the school's religious neutrality and violate the statute by wearing religious dress while teaching. However, the court also considered whether revocation of the teacher's certification, as provided by Or. Rev. Stat. § 342.655, was an excessive penalty. The court noted that sanctions for behavior far more serious than wearing religious dress were not so severe. The court recognized the school's obligation not to lend its support to any religion, but found that § 342.655 was unconstitutional because less restrictive alternatives than revocation would achieve the school's purpose.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the order of the state superintendent of public instruction, who revoked the teacher's certification.

State v. Woodcock


CA No. A34352


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


75 Ore. App. 659; 706 P.2d 1012; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 3918


June 10, 1985, Argued and submitted  
October 9, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted June 10, 1985; Reconsideration Denied December 6, 1985; petition for review denied January 28, 1986
Reconsideration Denied December 6, 1985. Petition for Review Denied January 28, 1986 (300 Or 506).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Yamhill County. Wayne R. Harris, Judge. No. 42937.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction from the District Court, Yamhill County (Oregon) for furnishing obscene materials to minors, a Class A misdemeanor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold lapel buttons that contained obscenities. He was convicted of furnishing material containing obscenities to minors in violation of ORS § 167.065(1)(b). The court noted that the statute essentially prohibited furnishing minors with any printed matter containing obscenities no matter how incidental the objectionable language was in the context of the work as a whole. Defendant contended that the statute was therefore unconstitutionally overbroad. The court addressed the appeal to the Oregon Constitution and did not address defendant's U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV claims. The court held that because the statute did not address the significance of the words in the context of the work as a whole, it was unconstitutionally overbroad. The statute prohibited furnishing minors with any printed matter containing "dirty words" no matter how incidental the objectionable language was in the context of the work as a whole, and while constitutional protections were more limited in respect to minors than to adults, such a prohibition was unconstitutionally overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction.

Davis v. Vesely


CA No. A33191


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


75 Ore. App. 591; 707 P.2d 627; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 3923


June 14, 1985, Argued and submitted  
October 9, 1985, Filed; Argued and submitted June 14, 1985


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Philip T. Abraham, Judge. No. A8208-05257.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, challenged the judgment from Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which directed a verdict in favor of defendant attorney in plaintiffs' legal malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs had hired the attorney to bring an action for malpractice against another lawyer, but the attorney had allowed the statute of limitations for the claim to run. The attorney admitted his negligence but argued that plaintiffs could not have prevailed on the claim against the other lawyer, and thus, no damages were sustained. On appeal, plaintiffs argued that the trial court erred in granting the directed verdict. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the action for trial. The court held that the testimony of plaintiffs' expert witness and other evidence was sufficient to present a jury question as to whether the four elements of a legal malpractice claim were proven. The court noted that plaintiffs' expert witness testified that the other lawyer did not exercise the ordinary care and diligence used by lawyers in the community because he failed to prepare an agreement that would not have subjected plaintiffs to future liability, and because he failed to inform plaintiffs of their potential liability to the corporation's creditors.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the attorney was reversed, and the action was remanded.
