State v. Timmons


CA No. A35001


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


75 Ore. App. 678; 706 P.2d 1018; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 3932


August 9, 1985, Argued and submitted  
October 9, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted August 9, 1985; Reconsideration Denied November 8, 1985; Petition for review denied December 17, 1985
Reconsideration Denied November 8, 1985. Petition for Review Denied December 17, 1985 (300 Or 451).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Douglas County. Ronald Poole, Judge. No. J84-0451.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in a two-count indictment with unlawfully and knowingly refusing and neglecting to support his children. Defendant demurred on the ground that ORS 163.555(1) (Or.) was unconstitutionally vague. The Circuit Court, Douglas County (Oregon), overruled his demurrer. Defendant was found guilty of one count, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his conviction of violating ORS 163.555(1), contending that the phrase "without lawful excuse" in ORS 163.555(1) was unconstitutionally vague. The court disagreed. The phrase "without lawful excuse" did not confuse or mislead defendants to the slightest degree as to their duty to support their minor children. It was commonly understood that a "lawful excuse" referred to some condition, not of defendant's own making, which prevented defendant from being able to provide support. The state satisfied its burden by showing (1) there was a court mandate that defendant pay child support, (2) he had an ability to generate an income, and in fact had earned wages during the time period in question, and (3) he had made no payment in any amount towards his child support obligation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1091 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Self


CA No. A33130


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


75 Ore. App. 230; 706 P.2d 975; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 3835



September 18, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] On Appellant's Petition for Reconsideration June 19, 1985


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. William A. Beckett, Judge. No. 10-84-04453. On appellant's reconsideration filed June 19, 1985.



DISPOSITION: Petition for reconsideration granted; affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petitioned for reconsideration of an affirmance of a judgment from the Lane County Circuit Court (Oregon), which convicted defendant for solicitation to possess a controlled substance, cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.435 forbade only solicitation of Oregon crimes and his substantive crime was a California offense, the charging instrument failed to allege that delivery of cocaine was a crime in California, and § 161.435, if applicable to foreign crimes, was unconstitutional. The court granted the reconsideration but affirmed the conviction. One could be criminally liable in Oregon for soliciting the commission of a crime in another state, so long as that other state's offense had a counterpoint under Oregon law. Possession of cocaine was illegal in both Oregon and California. It was therefore permissible to charge defendant with the crime of soliciting possession of cocaine in California. This was not an unlawful delegation of legislative authority to another state because it expressed legitimate policy and contained sufficient procedural protections to guard against arbitrary application. Section 161.435 was not vague as to defendant because defendant did not need to speculate whether his conduct would be an offense in another jurisdiction. Matters of judicial notice, including the law of another state, need not be alleged in a charging instrument.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition for reconsideration and affirmed the conviction.

Kling v. Exxon Corp.


CA No. A33008


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


74 Ore. App. 399; 703 P.2d 1021; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 3483


February 25, 1985, Argued and submitted  
July 17, 1985, Filed; Argued and submitted February 25, 1985


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Multnomah County. Michael J. O'Brien, Judge Pro Tempore. No. 244379.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer sought review of a decision of the District Court, Multnomah County (Oregon) that entered a judgment in favor of plaintiff employee for past wages that were due immediately upon termination under Or. Rev. Stat. 652.140. The judgment also assessed defendant with a civil penalty under Or. Rev. Stat. 652.150 and awarded plaintiff attorney's fees under Or. Rev. Stat. 652.200(2).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee last worked for defendant employer on May 5th, but defendant agreed to pay plaintiff additional salary in lieu of notice of termination. Defendant made salary payments May 13th and May 27th, and paid vacation pay in July. The trial court found that plaintiff's termination date was May 5th, that defendant had violated Or. Rev. Stat. 652.140 by not paying plaintiff the agreed upon amounts on that date, and that defendant should be liable for a civil penalty under Or. Rev. Stat. 652.150 and attorney's fees under Or. Rev. Stat. 652.200(2). The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that defendant was not relieved of its obligation for immediate payment of wages as of the date of termination simply because the additional wages were voluntarily offered by defendant. The penalty was appropriate when defendant's actions were wilful when it knew that it was not making payments on plaintiff's termination date. The statutory provision for attorney's fees only to successful plaintiffs under Or. Rev. Stat. 652.200(2) was not unconstitutional when there was a valid legislative purpose for the distinction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that found that defendant employer was liable to plaintiff employee for not paying past wages upon the date of termination and was also liable for a civil penalty and attorney's fees. Defendant's liability was not relieved because the payments were negotiated as an agreement in lieu of termination. The statute allowing attorney's fees only for successful plaintiffs was not unconstitutional.

Trivoli v. Multnomah County Rural Fire Protection Dist. No. 10

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which dismissed his petition for writ of review and granted summary judgment to defendants, an employer, certain supervisors, and the Civil Service Commission, in the employee's action alleging that the employer had violated due process by terminating his employment without notice or a hearing.

State v. Armenta


CA No. A31395


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


74 Ore. App. 219; 702 P.2d 1113; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 3285


November 30, 1984, Argued and submitted  
July 3, 1985, Filed; Argued and submitted November 30, 1984


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Clarke C. Brown, Judge. No. 145,500.



DISPOSITION: Order excluding blood test results as to assault charge reversed; otherwise affirmed; remanded for trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a pretrial order by the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which suppressed evidence of the result of a blood alcohol test taken while defendant was in the hospital. Defendant was charged in the same indictment with driving under the influence of intoxicants (DUII), Or. Rev. Stat. § 487.540, and assault in the second degree, Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.175.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found in the driver's seat of a vehicle that had crossed the centerline and collided head-on with another vehicle, injuring its driver. The investigating officer smelled alcohol on defendant's breath and observed that he walked unsteadily. At his own request, defendant was taken to the hospital. A blood alcohol test was performed at the hospital. In reversing the order that excluded the blood test results as to the assault charge, affirming in all other matters, and remanding for trial, the court held that probable cause and exigent circumstances justified taking the blood sample without defendant's consent. The Implied Consent law did not govern the admissibility of otherwise competent, relevant evidence in prosecutions for offenses other than DUII. The taking of the blood sample was not an unconstitutional search and seizure. The assault charge and the DUII charge were not so intertwined that evidence inadmissible as to one had to necessarily be excluded as to the other. Defendant could have the two charges severed, with separate trials being held.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order excluding blood test results as to the assault charge. Otherwise, the court affirmed and remanded for trial.

Davidson v. Oregon Government Ethics Com.


CA No. A31304


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


74 Ore. App. 160; 702 P.2d 417; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 3289


December 14, 1984, Argued and submitted; April 4, 1985, Resubmitted In Banc  
June 26, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted December 14, 1984; resubmitted in banc April 4, 1985; Reconsideration Denied August 16, 1985, Review Allowed September 17, 1985
Reconsideration Denied August 16, 1985. Petition for Review Allowed September 17, 1985 (300 Or 64).


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review from Oregon Government Ethics Commission.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner actuary sought review of an order by respondent, the Oregon Government Ethics Commission, that determined that the actuary had violated Or. Rev. Stat. § 244.040(1) by using his official position to obtain financial gain.


OVERVIEW: The actuary was employed by the state accident insurance fund. The fund decided to buy a fleet of cars. The actuary purchased a car as an "add-on" to the fleet purchase. The car was ordered in the fund's name and the title was later transferred to the actuary, who saved approximately $ 1,300 in comparison to what the car would have cost to an average consumer. The commission found the actuary used his official position to obtain financial gain for himself. The actuary argued the statute applied to more narrow situations where a public official used the power or influence of his office to obtain financial gain and that the term "use" in § 244.040(1) meant only influence peddling. The court affirmed the commission's order and held that three other statutes effectively dealt with influence peddling and the term "use" in the statute at issue was intended to be a broad catch-all provision to cover many types of unethical behavior. The court gave the term its ordinary meaning and determined that the actuary used his position to purchase the car.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commission's order that found the actuary had violated the ethics law.

Rantru v. Unger


CA No. A31246


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


73 Ore. App. 680; 700 P.2d 272; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 3107


April 17, 1985, Argued and submitted  
May 22, 1985, Filed; Argued and submitted April 17, 1985


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. William S. McLennan, Judge. No. 137725.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a will contest, appellant contestant sought review of a judgment order of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon) that overruled his objections and admitted the will to probate in solemn form. The contestant's sole assignment of error was that the circuit court erred in denying his motion for a jury trial. Respondent representative of a decedent's estate filed a cross-appeal.


OVERVIEW: Before trial, the contestant timely moved for a jury trial, which the circuit court denied. From a subsequent judgment order overruling his objections and admitting the will to probate in solemn form, the contestant appealed. The contestant contended that the circuit court erred in denying him a jury trial. The contestant alleged that a legislative change of Or. Rev. Stat. § 113.055(4), which provided that in the event of a will contest, proof of any facts should be made in the same manner as in an action tried without a jury, violated Or. Const. art. VII, § 3, which preserved the right to jury trials in actions at law where the value in controversy exceeded $ 200. Affirming, the court held that the changes were procedural and not substantive. They were not intended to alter, and did not alter, substantive rights such as the right to trial by jury or the lack thereof. The court noted that the present case would not have been triable to a jury when the Or. Const. was enacted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment order on the appeal. Thus, the cross-appeal was moot.

 

1099 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Carlson v. AFSCME


CA No. A31372


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


73 Ore. App. 755; 700 P.2d 260; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 3117


December 18, 1984, Argued and submitted  
May 22, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted December 18, 1984; Review Denied August 23, ordered vacated December 18, petition for review denied November 26
AFSCME's Reconsideration and Carlson's Reconsideration Denied August 23, 1985. Both Petitions for Review on Merits Denied November 26, 1985 (300 Or 332). Carlson's Reconsideration on Order Awarding Attorney Fees Allowed, Order Vacated December 18, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review from the Employment Relations Board. No. C-166-81.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; and remanded for proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent unions sought judicial review of the decision of the Employment Relations Board (ERB) (Oregon), which found that the unions had committed an unfair labor practice by spending a portion of complainant employees' fair share dues for unauthorized purposes. The employees sought review of the ERB's decision holding that fair-share dues could be used to defray costs for services rendered by the unions.


OVERVIEW: The employees were non-union employees who benefited from the unions' collective bargaining. The unions charged the employees fair share dues to pay support the unions' collective bargaining activities. The employees filed a complaint under the Public Employee Collective Bargaining Act, Or. Rev. Stat. § 243.650 et seq., challenging the imposition of fair share dues. The court affirmed the ERB's decision holding that the unions had committed an unfair labor practice by spending a portion of the employees' fair share dues for unauthorized purposes. Unions could use fair share dues to support some legitimate political involvement and had some latitude in determining the best means of promoting the legitimate negotiations and contract administration objectives of the bargaining unit. If a union knew in advance that a portion of fair share dues would be used for purposes not germane to or supportive of collective bargaining negotiations and contract administration, it had to reduce the fair share dues pro-rata In advance. The employees were entitled to interest at the statutory rate for any amount of fair share dues that the ERB concluded on remand was used unlawfully.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ERB's decision holding that the unions had committed an unfair labor practice by spending a portion of the employees' fair share dues for unauthorized purposes. The court reversed the ERB's decision that fair-share dues could be used to defray costs for purposes not germane to collective bargaining negotiation.

 

1100 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Romig


CA No. A32379


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


73 Ore. App. 780; 700 P.2d 293; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 3120


December 20, 1984, Argued and submitted  
May 22, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted December 20, 1984; Reconsideration Denied July 19, petition for review denied August 20, 1985
Reconsideration Denied July 19, 1985. Petition for Review Denied August 20, 1985 (299 Or 663).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Douglas R. Spencer, Judge. No. 10-83-05673.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Lane County (Oregon), which convicted him under the Oregon Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organization Act (RICO), Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 166.715 to 166.735. Defendant also was convicted of fraudulently obtaining a signature, under Or. Rev. Stat. § 165.042, and obtaining execution of documents by deception, under Or. Rev. Stat. § 165.102.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for violation of RICO, and for the separate offenses of fraudulently obtaining a signature and obtaining execution of documents by deception. Defendant demurred to the indictment but the demurrer was overruled, and defendant was tried on stipulated facts and convicted on all counts. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that there was no constitutional privilege fraudulently to misrepresent facts in order to obtain another's property, signature to a written instrument or execution of a written instrument affecting a pecuniary interest. All of defendant's hypotheticals involved such misrepresentations. Or. Rev. Stat. § 165.042 and Or. Rev. Stat. § 165.102 were not overbroad and were constitutional under Or. Const. art. I, § 8. Although RICO was complicated because of its many definitions and cross-references to other crimes, it was not indefinite or vague. The court held that the indictment was sufficient under Or. Rev. Stat. § 132.550(7) and Or. Rev. Stat. § 135.630(6).


OUTCOME: The order of the lower court convicting defendant was affirmed.

 

1101 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Roberts v. Gray's Crane & Rigging, Inc.


CA No. A31447


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


73 Ore. App. 29; 697 P.2d 985; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 2714


December 7, 1984, Argued and submitted  
April 3, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted December 7, 1984; Reconsideration Denied May 10, petition for Review Denied Junly 9, 1985 (299 or 443)
Reconsideration Denied May 10, 1985. Petition for Review Denied July 9, 1985 (299 Or 443).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Charles S. Crookham, Judge. No. A8206 03882.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Third-party plaintiff lessor appealed an order of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which dismissed its third-party complaint seeking enforcement of indemnity agreements in a lease against fourth-party defendant lessee in connection with a wrongful death action brought by plaintiff personal representative against the lessor.


OVERVIEW: A general contractor subcontracted with the lessee to construct a new roof on a stadium. The lessee leased a crane from the lessor. The lease agreements provided that the lessee would indemnify the lessor for all claims for death or injury to persons, including the lessee's employes, arising out of the lessee's use of the crane. One of the lessee's employes was killed, and his personal representative brought an action against the lessor for negligence. The lessor asserted a claim against the lessee based on the indemnity provisions of the lease agreements. The trial court held that the indemnity agreements in the lease were void under Or. Rev. Stat. § 656.018. The court affirmed, holding that under Or. Rev. Stat. § 656.018(1)(c), the lessee's duty to provide workers' compensation coverage was its exclusive liability for injuries to its workers, and thus the indemnity agreement was void. The court further held that the statute did not unreasonably interfere with the right to contract guaranteed by Or. Const. art. I, § 20 or the Fourteenth Amendment, and did not deny the lessor's right to a remedy under Or. Const. art. I, § 10.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the lessor's third-party claim for indemnification against the lessee.

 

1102 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Payless Drug Stores Northwest, Inc. v. Brown


CA No. A30985


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


73 Ore. App. 90; 698 P.2d 45; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 2720


September 18, 1984, Argued and submitted  
April 3, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted September 18, 1984; Reconsideration Denied July 5, petition for review allowed August 8, 1985
Reconsideration Denied July 5, 1985. Petition for Review Allowed August 8, 1985 (299 Or 583).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Umatilla County. Richard J. Courson, Judge. No. 83-1-1014.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant parents, citing Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 30.875(2), 164.045, Or. Evid. Code 103, appealed a judgment of the District Court, Umatilla County (Oregon) in favor of plaintiff store owner in the store owner's action seeking to recover a statutory civil penalty and the value of merchandise shoplifted by the parents' daughter and on the parents' counterclaim for damages under the Unlawful Debt Collection Act, Or. Rev. Stat. § 646.639.


OVERVIEW: The parents contended on appeal that the trial court erred in granting the store owner's motion for a directed verdict on their counterclaim, in comments it made to the jury before voir dire, and in admitting evidence on statements made by the daughter to the store owner's security guard and on the store owner's overall expenses and costs due to shoplifting and actual damages. The court affirmed the judgment. The court observed that whether or not the daughter had shoplifted, there was no evidence from which the jury could find that there had been a "consumer transaction" between her and the store owner. The court determined that the trial court's comments to the jury were harmless. The court pointed out that while the trial court erred when it admitted the guard's testimony and report, the jury's conclusion from other testimony was inescapable that the daughter intended to and did shoplift and the admission of the report and testimony was therefore harmless. The court commented that evidence of the store owner's actual damages from the daughter's acts was clearly relevant and that if there was any error in admitting the other evidence, it was cured by an instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the store owner in its action against the parents for a civil penalty and on the counterclaim by the parents.

 

1103 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Ackerley Communications, Inc. v. Multnomah County


CA No. A34195


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


72 Ore. App. 617; 696 P.2d 1140; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 2677


January 21, 1985, Argued and submitted  
March 20, 1985, Filed; Argued and submitted January 21, 1985


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 10, 1985. Petition for Review Allowed June 18, 1985 (299 Or 313). Reconsideration on Attorney Fees Denied August 1, 1985. Petition for Review on Attorney Fees Denied August 27, 1985 (299 Or 732).


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review from Land Use Board of Appeals. Nos. 83-028, 83-034 & 83-051.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporation sought review of an order of the Land Use Board of Appeals (Oregon), which rejected its challenges to respondent county's ordinance, Multnomah County, Or., Ordinance 365 as amended by Ordinances 369 and 376.


OVERVIEW: The county enacted an ordinance that regulated outdoor advertising through billboards. The corporation made constitutional and other challenges to the ordinance on the basis that the county regulated only advertising that had "commercial" content and "noncommercial" outdoor advertising was completely exempt from regulation. The board rejected the challenges. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the content-based distinction in the way that different kinds of constitutionally equal speech were regulated could not be salvaged by the fact that the regulation restricted only the time, place, and manner of engaging in the expression that had been selected for regulation. The court held that the ordinance violated Or. Const. art. I, § 8 because it regulated one kind of speech and not another, based on the difference in their content. The court held that the county could have no constitutionally acceptable interest in regulating commercial and noncommercial expression differently because of the content. The court held that the ordinance also violated the equal privileges and immunities requirement of Or. Const. art. I, § 20.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the board's finding that the ordinance regulating billboards was constitutional.

 

1104 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Eckles v. Livermore


CA No. A28776


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


72 Ore. App. 650; 696 P.2d 1153; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 2678


September 17, 1984, Argued and submitted  
March 20, 1985, Filed; Argued and submitted September 17, 1984


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 10, 1985. Petition for Review Allowed June 4, 1985 (299 Or 251).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Edwin E. Allen, Judge. No. 16-83-00926.



DISPOSITION: Reversed on appeal; affirmed on cross-appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the directors of the State Accident Insurance Fund (SAIF) Corporation, appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon) that held that the legislation creating the SAIF Corporation, 1979 Or. Laws ch. 829, was unconstitutional, enjoined the directors from acting for a legally nonexistent entity, and awarded attorney fees to plaintiff insured employer. The insured employer filed a cross-appeal regarding relief not granted.


OVERVIEW: The insured employer argued that 1979 Or. Laws ch. 829 was a special law prohibited by Or. Const. art. XI, § 2. The trial court held that 1979 Or. Laws ch. 829 was unconstitutional. On review, the court reversed that conclusion, holding that ch. 829 did not violate Or. Const. art. XI, § 2. The court found that the SAIF Corporation was not a corporation in the ordinary sense of the word, even though it had some attributes generally considered necessary for corporate existence. The SAIF Corporation was neither a private corporation nor a corporation created for a municipal purpose. The court held that Or. Const. art. XI, § 2 did not prohibit the legislature from clothing a state instrumentality that it created with some corporate attributes when that entity was created for a statewide, not municipal, public purpose and was subject to public management and control. The SAIF Corporation was such an entity. It was given limited corporate attributes to enable it to carry out its function of transacting the workers' compensation insurance business formerly transacted by another entity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the holding that the legislation creating the SAIF Corporation was unconstitutional and the award of attorney fees to the insured employer. The court affirmed the issues on cross-appeal.

 

1105 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jalo


CA Nos. A28299 (Control), A28314, A28315, A28316, A28317, A28318, A28319, A28320 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


72 Ore. App. 479; 696 P.2d 14; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 2512


December 10, 1984, Argued and submitted  
March 6, 1985, Filed; Argued and submitted December 10, 1984


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 24, 1985. Petition for Review Denied July 2, 1985 (299 Or 443).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Clackamas County. Howard J. Blanding, Judge. Nos. 81-927, 81-928, 81-929, 81-930, 81-931, 81-933, 81-934, 82-2.



DISPOSITION: Judgment in No. A28318 reversed; other judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions from the Circuit Court, Clackamas County (Oregon) for six charges of rape in the third degree, ORS 163.355, one charge of sodomy in the third degree, ORS 163.385, and one charge of failure to appear in the first degree, ORS 162.205. Each of the charges were brought in separate indictments but were consolidated for trial. He contended that his convictions were not supported by sufficient evidence.


OVERVIEW: The charges stemmed from defendant's relationship with a 15-year old girl who lived with his family and his alleged attempts to start her in business as a prostitute. He challenged the admission of evidence of a similar relationship with another girl. The trial court allowed the evidence as relevant to a related charge for which he was not convicted and he had not requested a limiting charge. The court therefore held that there was no error. Defendant also claimed that ORS 163.355 was unconstitutional because he was not allowed to assert that he thought she was over age 16. He contended that there was no rational basis for not requiring him to have knowledge of the fact that she was under age 16, thereby subjecting defendant to strict liability. The court held that the legislature had reduced the penalties for intercourse with girls under age 14 by requiring knowledge of the victim's age, but retained at least some penalty by not requiring suck knowledge for intercourse with a girl under age 16. Therefore ORS 163.355 was not an equal protection violation, and the attachment of responsibility for a crime of which he ignorant of the facts was not a due process violation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed one of defendant's convictions for rape in the third degree, but affirmed his other convictions.

Barnett v. State


CA No. A32452


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


72 Ore. App. 585; 695 P.2d 991; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 2518


December 13, 1984, Submitted on record and briefs  
March 6, 1985, Filed; Submitted on record and briefs December 13, 1984


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. Gregory E. Milnes, Judge. No. 83-1326 C.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions to set aside plaintiff's conviction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought against defendant State, plaintiff, an individual who was convicted of a crime, brought a post-conviction proceeding and challenged a decision of the Circuit Court, Washington County (Oregon), which denied him relief from his conviction for carrying a blackjack.


OVERVIEW: The State confessed that ORS 166.510 was unconstitutional insofar as it prohibited the possession of a blackjack. The State also confessed that the trial court erred in holding otherwise. In reversing the decision, and remanding the cause, the court agreed with the State. As to plaintiff's contention that the trial court erred in refusing to award him a sum in restitution that he paid as part of his sentence and a sum in general damages, the relief that could be granted under ORS 138.520 was limited to matters similar to release, new trial, and modification of sentence. The court was aware of no statute that authorized a court in a post-conviction proceeding to award money damages or to require the State to repay to plaintiff the restitution that he paid for the benefit of a private party.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision and remanded the cause with instructions to set aside plaintiff's conviction.

State v. Eells

COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


72 Ore. App. 492; 696 P.2d 564; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 2520


April 25, 1984, Argued and submitted  
March 6, 1985, Filed; Argued and submitted April 25, 1984


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 19, 1985. Petition for Review Denied June 18, 1985 (299 Or 313).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Irving M. Steinbock, Judge. No. C83-01-30067.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which convicted him on two counts of possession of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found by a police officer in his vehicle, wherein defendant voluntarily stated that he had marijuana. After he was given Miranda warnings and placed under arrest, he told the officer that there were more drugs in his vehicle. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the statements, and the trial court denied the motion. The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that (1) defendant made no incriminating statements under police interrogation, and his statement regarding drug possession was voluntary, without prompting by the officer; (2) the decision to proceed without a post-indictment hearing was not improper because preventing unnecessary delay was a valid reason to skip the hearing; and (3) it was not unconstitutional for Oregon to adopt the Federal Controlled Substances Act, 21 U.S.C.S. §§ 811-812, but not its criteria because it was not arbitrary for Oregon to exclude, under Or. Rev. Stat. § 475.035, medical use as a factor in establishing drug classifications.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction of the trial court.

Korgan v. Oregon Liquor Control Com.


CA No. A28824


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


72 Ore. App. 31; 695 P.2d 81; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 2390


May 4, 1984, Argued and submitted  
February 6, 1985, Filed; Argued and submitted May 4, 1984


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 10, 1985. Petition for Review Denied July 9, 1985 (299 Or 443).


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review from Oregon Liquor Control Commission.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner licensee appealed from a decision of the Oregon Liquor Control Commission, which suspended the Dispenser Class A license of the licensee's business or, alternatively, imposed a fine of $ 1,755 in lieu of suspension for operating a lewd establishment in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 472.180(5).


OVERVIEW: The evidence presented before the Commission showed that male dancers had contact with female patrons in a sexually suggestive manner, including the touching of genitalia. The evidence also indicated that the licensee was aware of the conduct and had allowed minors to enter the establishment. The court rejected the licensee's contention that the word "lewd" in Or. Rev. Stat. § 472.180(5) was unconstitutionally vague. The Commission's interpretation of "lewd" as "lustful, indecent, lascivious, or lecherous" was consistent with the court's interpretation of the term in prior cases, and with the generally expressed legislative policy. The term indicated with sufficient specificity the proscribed conduct so that men of ordinary understanding could govern their activities, and, consequently it was not unconstitutionally vague. The court rejected the licensee's contention that the Commission erred in failing to consider adequately their defenses to the charges of allowing minors to enter and consume alcoholic beverages. It was not the court's role to reassess or reweigh facts about which there was an evidentiary dispute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Oslund


CA No. A28771


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


71 Ore. App. 701; 693 P.2d 1354; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 2376


May 25, 1984, Argued and submitted  
January 23, 1985, Filed; Argued and submitted May 25, 1984


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 8, 1985. Petition for Review Denied April 16, 1985 (299 Or 37).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. Gregory E. Milnes, Judge. No. 83-0123.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment entered in the Circuit Court, Washington County (Oregon), which convicted defendant of aggravated murder and sentenced defendant to life imprisonment with a 30-year minimum without possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued on appeal that the trial court had erred in failing to suppress certain tape-recorded statements because the application on which the order authorizing the interception had been based had failed to demonstrate the inadequacy of alternative investigative procedures as required by the wiretap statutes, ORS 133.724(1)(h), 133.724(3)(c) (Oregon). The court concluded that the application and supporting affidavits provided sufficient factual information from which the trial court could find that normal investigative procedures had been tried and had failed or reasonably appeared to be unlikely to succeed if tried. The court also determined that there was evidence, independent of defendant's admissions, that the murder had been for hire. It was enough if there was some proof, circumstantial or otherwise, from which a reasonable inference could be drawn that defendant had received money for the murder. As to the severity of defendant's sentence, Or. Const. art. I, § 15 did not prohibit the legislature from providing heavier minimum sentences for crimes such as murder for hire that could be considered more dangerous to the public.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of aggravated murder.

Sanders v. United States Nat'l Bank


CA No. A29126


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


71 Ore. App. 674; 694 P.2d 548; 1985 Ore. App. LEXIS 2384

January 23, 1985, Filed; Argued and submitted June 25; resubmitted in banc November 7, 1984


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 8, 1985. Petition for Review Denied April 2, 1985 (299 Or 31).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. William S. McLennan, Judge. No. 135825.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contestants appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Multnomah County (Oregon), which found that their father's will was not the product of an insane delusion and entered a judgment in favor of respondents, decedent's former wife and his grandchildren.


OVERVIEW: The decedent's son and daughter filed a will contest to their father's will based on grounds that the decedent lacked testamentary capacity; the will was the product of undue influence by his former wife, and the will was the product of an insane delusion. The contestants withdrew the first two grounds and submitted the case only on the grounds of the will being the product of an insane delusion. The trial court ruled against them and the contestants appealed. The court noted testimony from the attorney who prepared decedent's will that he discussed decedent's proposed will before it was executed and the decedent was very clear that he desired to disinherit his children because he did not like them and they did not like him, and also because they had already received part of his estate indirectly when their mother died.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court finding the decedent's will was not the product of an insane delusion.

State v. Jacobs


CA No. A29458


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


71 Ore. App. 560; 692 P.2d 1387; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 4688


June 25, 1984, Argued and submitted  
December 19, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted June 25, 1984


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Robert Redding, Judge. No. C82-09-37343.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which found that he had violated his probation and that imposed additional conditions on his continued probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was on probation after pleading guilty to burglary. During this probationary period, the probation officer searched defendant's residence and found a knife, a broken pool cue, drug paraphernalia, and some marijuana seeds. Defendant had also withdrawn from a course at school, without informing the officer. At his revocation hearing, the court ordered that defendant not reside in Troutdale, Oregon, and that he serve one year in county jail with school release privileges. Defense counsel objected to the provision restricting defendant from residing in Troutdale as unconstitutional. The court ordered counsel to present a more refined definition, but counsel did not submit one. Defendant appealed. The court reversed and remanded. The court held that the provision that he not reside in Troutdale was excessive, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. §138.050, in light of the offense. The court held that the restriction should have been more narrowly drawn, and could be modified to reasonably restrict his residency within Troutdale. The court affirmed the remainder of the order, finding that the imposition of jail time was supported by the various violations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that portion of the trial court judgment which ordered that defendant not reside anywhere in Troutdale, Oregon.

 

1114 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hilborn


CA No. A30898


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


71 Ore. App. 534; 692 P.2d 1383; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 4700


July 30, 1984, Argued and submitted  
December 19, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted July 30, 1984


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 15, 1985. Petition for Review Allowed March 19, 1985 (298 Or 822).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Coos County. Charles H. Reeves, Judge. MC No. 83-2164.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of conviction of the crime of driving under the influence of intoxicants entered against him in the District Court, Coos County (Oregon). Defendant challenged the trial judge's denial of his pretrial motion for change of judge and the refusal to grant a hearing on his motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that it was improper for the trial judge to rule on the motion. The trial judge's refusal to recuse himself was based on defendant's failure timely to file the motion, as required by ORS 14.260 (Oregon). Accordingly, if the motion was untimely the trial judge did not act improperly by ruling on defendant's motion. Defendant argued, in support of his first assignment, that his motion was in fact timely. The court on appeal did not find that defendant's motion was untimely filed. It was obvious that a defendant in a multi-judge district would have no reason to object to a particular judge until he knew which judge has been assigned to his case. ORS 14.260 specifically provided that the proper way to establish prejudice was to file a motion supported by affidavit that the judge before whom the cause, matter or proceeding was pending was prejudiced. In order to comply with that provision, a party must first know before whom the case was pending. The trial notice received by defendant did not indicate which judge would hear the case. The statutory time limits had not begun to run when the trial notice was sent and the denial of defendant's motion was erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court on appeal reversed the judgment. The court on appeal also remanded the cause for further proceedings not inconsistent with its opinion. The motion to suppress issue was not addressed because the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1115 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wood


CA Nos. A32257, A32258 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


71 Ore. App. 126; 691 P.2d 116; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 4426


September 28, 1984, Argued and submitted  
November 21, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted September 28, 1984


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. John C. Beatty, Jr., Judge. Nos. C83-06-33043, C83-06-33040.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which convicted defendants of the felony crime of buying and possessing food fish unlawfully caught during a closed season in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 509.011(2)(a), 506.991(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendants became the target of a police undercover investigation of purchases and sales of salmon caught out of season. An undercover police officer sold defendants illegally caught fish. Defendants contended that the trial court erred in denying to dismiss the indictments and admitting at trial rebuttable evidence that one of the defendants had bought illegal sturgeon roe on other occasions. The salmon sold to defendants were illegally caught. The court determined that defendants knew that the salmon were illegally caught when they bought them. The court found that the fact that the state may sell illegal fish to prevent loss or spoilage did not alter the character of the fish to make them "legally caught." The court concluded that defendants could not have benefited from the fact that the state had authority to sell fish under the circumstances described by Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 506.690(2), 635-02-030. The court further found that defendants failed to explain how the probative value of the rebuttal testimony was substantially outweighed by the danger of unfair prejudice or confusion. Thus, the court did not abuse its discretion in admitting the challenged testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' conviction of buying and possessing food fish unlawfully caught during a closed season.

 

1116 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Friedman v. Paulus


CA No. A33697


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


70 Ore. App. 612; 689 P.2d 1330; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 4324


October 30, 1984, Argued and submitted  
November 1, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted October 30, 1984


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 7, 1984. Petition for Review Denied March 6, 1985 (298 Or 773).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Duane R. Ertsgaard, Judge. No. 151880.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, political party and candidate, challenged the refusal of appellant Secretary of State to accept the party's nominating papers. The Circuit Court of Marion County (Oregon) ruled in favor of the party. The Secretary appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Secretary refused to accept papers nominating a candidate of the party in a 1984 general election for a state representative from a house district. The party's candidate in the 1982 election had not achieved five percent of the votes. The Secretary's basis for her refusal was that the party did not qualify as a "minor political party" under ORS 249.732. The trial court ruled in favor of the party. On appeal, the court reversed in favor of the Secretary. The court held that ORS 249.732 clearly contemplated that minor political party status required a candidate to achieve at least five percent of the votes cast in an electoral district in which the party previously offered a candidate. There was a necessary connection between the electoral district in which the party previously offered a candidate and the district where in presently sought a nomination.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Whitford


CA No. A30628


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


70 Ore. App. 456; 689 P.2d 1023; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 4298


September 26, 1984, Argued and submitted  
October 24, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted September 26, 1984


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Maurice K. Merten, Judge. No. 10-83-02624.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), convicted defendant of failure to appear in the first degree, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.205. Defendant had intentionally failed to appear at a sentencing hearing for which he was ordered, through his attorney, to appear. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed and held that defendant was precluded from challenging the constitutionality of the charging statute on vagueness grounds because his behavior was unquestionably within the prohibited conduct of the statute. Defendant was charged with intentionally failing to appear at a sentencing hearing after the trial court had ordered him to appear. Defendant, a person of ordinary intelligence, would have had no difficulty knowing that his conduct, if performed with the requisite intent, fell within the ambit of the statutory prohibition. The record was clear that defendant left the state voluntarily. Through correspondence, he indicated to the district attorney that he never intended to return. The court could not see how defendant had been victimized by any uncertainty in the statute. He did not contend that the trial court lacked authority. Thus, defendant could not challenge the constitutionality of § 162.205, as applied to him, on the ground of vagueness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for failure to appear in the first degree.

 

1118 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Marks v. Roseburg


CA No. A27195


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


65 Ore. App. 102; 670 P.2d 201; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 4865


March 23, 1984, Submitted on record and briefs  
October 12, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied January 13, 1984. Petition for Review Denied February 28, 1984 (296 Or 536).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Douglas County. Don H. Sanders, Judge. No. E80-1783.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded on appeal with instructions to enter judgment for plaintiffs. Affirmed on cross-appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, palmistry practitioners, appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court of Douglas County (Oregon), which upheld the constitutionality of City of Roseburg, Or., Municipal Code § 10.04.060 and enjoined the practitioners from engaging in the practice of palmistry for hire or profit in the city. Defendant city cross-appealed, alleging that the practitioners lacked standing.


OVERVIEW: City of Roseburg, Or., Municipal Code § 10.04.060 prohibited the practice of occult arts for hire or profit within the city. The practitioners, who intended to open a palmistry business inside the city limits, had to find a business location beyond the city limits. They argued that the ordinance violated the free speech guarantees of the U.S. Const. amend. I and Or. Const. art. I, § 8. The court dismissed the city's cross-appeal after determining that the practitioners had standing. Their rights were affected by the ordinance and they had a direct and substantial interest in the controversy. Reversing the judgment, the court held that the ordinance was overbroad and therefore unconstitutional. The ordinance sought to restrict the practitioners' ability to speak about palmistry. Such a restriction fell squarely within the prohibitions of Or. Const. art. I, § 8. The court did not reach the practitioners' First Amendment argument. The case was remanded so that a judgment could be entered for the practitioners.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter with instructions that the trial court enter a judgment for the practitioners.

State v. Gainer


CA No. A29805


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


70 Ore. App. 199; 689 P.2d 323; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 4187


February 22, 1984, Argued and submitted  
October 10, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted February 22, 1984


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Josephine County. Allan H. Coon, Judge. No. 82-2075-K.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court, Josephine County (Oregon) that convicted her of driving while under the influence of intoxicants, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 487.540(1)(a).


OVERVIEW: After defendant's car was stopped, the officer turned on a tape recorder, asked defendant several questions, and conducted several field sobriety tests. Although she performed several tests adequately, she was unable to recite the alphabet accurately. Upon further questioning, defendant stated that she had been drinking, that she had always had difficulty reciting the alphabet rhyme, and that the alcohol she had consumed affected her ability to recite the alphabet. Defendant was then arrested and a subsequent breath test indicated a blood-alcohol level above the limit prescribed by § 487.540(1)(a). On appeal, the court ruled that defendant's pre-Miranda, tape recorded statements properly were not suppressed because they were not the product of a custodial interrogation. Even if, under a then pending case on remand from the United States Supreme Court, she was subject to a custodial interrogation, the only suppressible statement was her admission that alcohol affected her recitation of the alphabet. Given the other evidence of guilt, the admission of that statement was harmless error, if any. Also, § 487.540(1)(a) was not unconstitutionally vague, the court ruled.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1120 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Saddler


CA No. A32344


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


70 Ore. App. 76; 688 P.2d 428; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 4085


August 3, 1984, Argued and submitted  
September 26, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted August 3, 1984


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Lane County. Winfrid K. Liepe, Judge. No. B64-863.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment and order of the District Court, Lane County (Oregon) requiring him to repay to the State of Oregon, as a condition of his probation, $ 100 as part of the cost of his court-appointed counsel, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.665.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of contributing to the sexual delinquency of a minor and ordered to repay part of the cost of his appointed counsel. He argued that Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.665, applicable only to convicted defendants, was unconstitutional because it incorporated a reference to Or. Rev. Stat. § 135.055(5). On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's determination. It held that the only portion of Or. Rev. Stat. § 135.055 held unconstitutional was subsection (6). Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.665 referred only to subsection (5), which simply set out the procedure by which appointed counsel should support a request for attorney fees. It had nothing to do with recoupment of those fees or other costs. The court found that when the pre-and post-1981 versions of Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.665 were compared, the only substantive change was the inclusion of costs include the compensation of counsel appointed pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 135.045, 135.050 and expenses approved under Or. Rev. Stat. § 135.055(5). All of the safeguards approved by the Oregon Supreme Court remained in the recoupment scheme in the current version of Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.665.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and order requiring defendant to repay part of the cost of his appointed counsel.

1122 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


AFSCME Council 75, Local 350 v. Clackamas County


CA No. A29038


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


69 Ore. App. 488; 687 P.2d 1102; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3911; 117 L.R.R.M. 2447


March 30, 1984, Argued and submitted  
August 29, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted March 30, 1984


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Judicial Review from Employment Relations Board. No. C-101-83.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner county appealed an order from the Employment Relations Board (ERB)(Oregon), which found that the county committed an unfair labor practice in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 243.672(1)(e) by refusing to bargain with respondent local regarding certain subjects covered by the county's civil service system. The civil service system was adopted by the voters pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 241.002(1).


OVERVIEW: The ERB ordered the county to desist from refusing to bargain over the union's proposals. The county argued that the subjects of the proposals, layoff, recall, discipline, discharge, and grievance procedures, were covered by the County Civil Service Act (CCS), Or. Rev. Stat. § 241.020 et seq., and so it was not required to bargain about them under the Public Employee Collective Bargaining Act (PECBA), Or. Rev. Stat. § 243.650 et seq. The court affirmed. There was an apparent conflict between PECBA and the CCS. PECBA required the county to bargain as to employment relations. The CCS authorized amendment of the system by methods including submission to the electorate. The county's authority regarding conditions of employment was subject to PECBA. To harmonize the laws as suggested by the county would defeat the purposes of PECBA. Moreover, the county failed to show how requiring bargaining about employment relations would thwart the purposes of the CCS. If a county civil service system adopted pursuant to the CCS covered employment relations under PECBA and about which a representative desired to bargain, Or. Rev. Stat. § 241.002(1) was inapplicable and the county had to bargain.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Holterman


CA No. A28038


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


69 Ore. App. 509; 687 P.2d 1097; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3919


April 25, 1984, Argued and submitted  
August 29, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted April 25, 1984


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 12, 1984. Petition for Review Denied November 6, 1984 (298 Or 172).
Review denied by State v. Holterman, 298 Ore. 172, 691 P.2d 481, 1984 Ore. LEXIS 1927 (1984)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Holterman v. Morrow, 81 Fed. Appx. 136, 2003 U.S. App. LEXIS 23168 (9th Cir. Or., 2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Holterman v. Nooth, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 62372 (D. Or., June 8, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Clackamas County. Winston L. Bradshaw, Judge. No. 82-716.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Clackamas County (Oregon), which convicted him of aggravated murder and attempted aggravated murder. He received a life sentence with a minimum of 20 years for the aggravated murder conviction and 20 years with a minimum of 10 years on the attempted aggravated murder conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of shooting one dealer and killing another in the course of robbing them at an illegal gambling establishment. The court held that there was probable arrest defendant. The police were entitled to rely on information about his nickname and activities generally known in the law enforcement community. The trial court did not err in concluding from the evidence that the dealer who was killed understood the questions an officer asked her and was able to employ his signaling system. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in excluding defendant's evidence showing that another person committed the crimes. Defendant's testimony only marginally tended to show that another person could have had a motive to commit the crimes. Any probative value was far outweighed by the potential of that testimony to mislead the jury. The 20-year minimum for aggravated murder did not violate Or. Const. art. I, § 15, the "Reformation Clause." The sentence was not so disproportionate to the offense as to shock the conscience of fair-minded persons.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for aggravated murder and attempted aggravated murder.

Chapman v. Perron


CA No. A30072


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


69 Ore. App. 445; 685 P.2d 492; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3858

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Hood River County. John Jelderks, Judge. No. 8973.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court, Hood River County (Oregon), which entered judgment in favor of defendant landowners and dismissed plaintiffs' petition for a statutory way of necessity over the land pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 376.150-376.200.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed a petition for a statutory way of necessity over the land. The court also determined that the landowners were entitled to an award of attorney fees under Or. Rev. Stat. § 376.175(2)(e).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of plaintiffs' petition for a statutory way of necessity.

State v. Earp


CA No. A25449


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


69 Ore. App. 365; 686 P.2d 437; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3870


November 23, 1983, Argued and submitted  
August 8, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted November 23, 1983


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied September 14, 1984. Petition for Review Denied December 4, 1984 (298 Or 334).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Clackamas County. Howard J. Blanding, Judge. No. 82-95.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Clackamas Court (Oregon), which convicted him of aggravated murder pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.095(1)(c), and sentenced him to a mandatory minimum of 30 years imprisonment pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.105(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in refusing to grant his motion for a preliminary hearing, in admitting evidence of his previous conviction for first degree murder, and in sentencing him to a minimum of 30 years imprisonment. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion for a preliminary hearing because the charging process was applied the same as it was in other counties. The court further found that defendant's prior conviction for first degree murder was properly admitted because the prior conviction was an element of the crime of aggravated murder under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.095(1)(c), the statute under which defendant was charged. The evidence of the prior crime was not only relevant, it was material to proof of the crime. Although the prejudicial impact on defendant of having the jurors know that he had previously committed first degree murder was strong, defendant could have avoided that problem by stipulating to the prior conviction pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.103. The court lastly held that the 30-year mandatory minimum sentence did not violate the proportionality requirement of Or. Const. art. I, § 16.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State ex rel. Fox v. Hicks


CA No. A28881


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


69 Ore. App. 348; 686 P.2d 431; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3872


February 15, 1984, Argued and submitted  
August 8, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted February 15, 1984


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Gordon Cottrell and Maurice K. Merten, Judges. No. 60-82-02507.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of paternity and resultant child support order reversed; remanded for ruling on defendant's motion and for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant putative father challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Lane County(Oregon), which, in plaintiff State of Oregon's paternity action instituted on behalf of relatrix mother, granted the State's motion for paternity under Or. Rev. Stat. § 109.252, determined that the putative father, who was indigent, was the father of the mother's child, and ruled that the putative father's motion for blood tests at the State's expense was moot.


OVERVIEW: In order to receive public assistance, the mother named the putative father as the father of her child. In the State's paternity action, the putative father denied paternity. He was represented by a legal aid attorney and, in deposition testimony, expressed his willingness to submit to blood group tests, but stated that he was unable to pay for the tests because he was indigent and unemployed.Thereafter, the parties signed a stipulation, which was signed by the trial court and which stated that the putative father agreed to submit to blood testing and that he recognized an obligation to pay for such testing. Trial was delayed so that the putative father was able to save money for the testing. About three months later, the State moved for determination of paternity without the blood tests and claimed that the putative father's inability to pay for the tests was equivalent to a refusal under § 109.252. The court held that summary determination of paternity against the putative father denied him due process of law. The court further noted that although he initially agreed to pay for the tests, he failed to comply with the agreement because he was indigent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of paternity and resultant child support order and remanded for a ruling on the putative father's motion for blood tests to determine paternity at the State's expense.

State v. Earls


CA No. A26656


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


69 Ore. App. 75; 683 P.2d 1387; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3618


August 24, 1983, Argued and submitted  
July 11, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted August 24, 1983


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied August 31, 1984. Petition for Review Denied September 18, 1984 (297 Or 824).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Gregory G. Foote, Judge. No. 10-82-04862.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), which convicted and sentenced him for robbery in the first degree under Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 144.110, 161.610. Defendant argued that evidence was illegally seized through his coerced consent, that incriminating statements he made after his arrest were the fruit of the illegal search and made under the influence of narcotics, and that § 161.610 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant while a fugitive from the State of California robbed a tavern at gunpoint. The police obtained a warrant for defendant's arrest based upon his fugitive status. While serving the warrant at defendant's residence, police officers gave defendant Miranda warnings and sought his consent to search the residence for the gun and money. After the officers informed defendant that they would obtain a warrant and tear the house apart to find the gun and the money, defendant showed the police where the money and the gun were hidden. Defendant then admitted to the robbery. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that defendant was not coerced and that no search occurred because defendant showed the officers where the evidence was hidden. Defendant's statements were admissible where they were voluntary despite his narcotic use. Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.610, which established mandatory minimum sentences, did not violate the separation of powers provisions of Or. Const. art. I, § 1, and did not deprive defendant of his right to a jury trial where he waived a jury and stipulated that he used a gun in the robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant.

State v. Kuhlmann


CA No. A27812


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


68 Ore. App. 746; 683 P.2d 552; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3568


September 20, 1983, Argued and submitted  
June 27, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted September 20, 1983


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied August 24, 1984. Petition for Review Allowed November 20, 1984 (298 Or 238).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Polk County. Donald R. Blensly, Judge. No. 30630.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court, Polk County (Oregon), which found him to be in contempt of an order for him to testify as a witness in his father's trial for murder after a grant of use and derivative use immunity under ORS 136.619.


OVERVIEW: Defendant refused to answer questions as a witness in his father's trial for murder, claiming his right against self-incrimination, despite an order under ORS 136.617 that he testify and a grant of use and derivative use immunity under ORS 136.619. The trial court found him in contempt and sentenced him to jail. Defendant argued on appeal, inter alia, that the immunity he received was inadequate under the Fifth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that because the legislature intended to provide immunity sufficiently extensive to overcome the Fifth Amendment right not to be a witness against oneself, it construed ORS 136.619 to prohibit the use of the immunized testimony or its fruits against the witness in any criminal proceeding or prosecution. The corut held, therefore, that the grant of immunity was sufficient to overcome the privilege not to answer. The court further held that the order directing defendant to testify was sufficiently specific to inform him of what was required. The court finally held that it was proper for an adult court to find defendant, a juvenile, in contempt for refusing to testify in an adult proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Belles


CA No. A29718


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


68 Ore. App. 910; 683 P.2d 1027; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3595


April 25, 1984, Argued and submitted  
June 27, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted April 25, 1984


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Philip T. Abraham, Judge. No. C83-03-31373.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Oregon appealed a pretrial order of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), that dismissed an indictment against defendant for theft. The cause was governed by the provisions of Or. Rev. Stat. § 135.705.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had reported that his property had been stolen, he filed an insurance claim thereon, and he then collected $ 1,000 from the insurance company. Subsequently, the company learned that defendant had disposed of the property himself. The State indicted defendant for theft. Defendant executed a civil compromise agreement with the company and a promissory note agreeing to re-pay the company in monthly installments. The costs of prosecution and court-appointed counsel in the theft case were $ 432. The trial court ordered defendant to pay attorney fees and costs totaling $ 200 in monthly installments and thereupon dismissed the indictment. The State appealed, arguing that the trial court should not have dismissed the indictment unless defendant had first paid the full sum of $ 432. In affirming the dismissal, the court noted that Or. Rev. Stat. § 135.705(1) recited that a court was to require the payment of costs and expenses incurred before it dismissed an indictment. If the trial court could not dismiss the indictment until defendant paid in full, dismissal could be substantially delayed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Soriano


CA Nos. A27206 (Control), A27207 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


68 Ore. App. 642; 684 P.2d 1220; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3384


July 22, 1983, Argued and submitted; May 2, 1984, Resubmitted In Banc  
June 13, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Argued and submitted July 22, 1983; resubmitted in banc May 2, 1984; Reconsideration Denied September 7, 1984
Reconsideration Denied September 7, 1984. Petition for Review Allowed November 20, 1984 (298 Or 238).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Klamath County. Donald A. W. Piper, Judge. No. 83-006CR.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Klamath County (Oregon), which found defendants guilty of contempt for refusing to testify before a grand jury without transactional immunity. The circuit court had granted defendants use and derivative use immunity under Or. Rev. Stat. § 136.617-136.619.


OVERVIEW: Defendants refused to testify before a grand jury investigating a possible burglary, asserting their right against self-incrimination under Or. Const. art. I, § 12, and continued to refuse after the circuit court granted them the use and derivative use immunity provided under Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 136.617-136.619. The circuit court, thus, found them in contempt. On appeal, the court reversed, and found that §§ 136.617-136.619 violated Or. Const. art. I, § 12. The court held that the right set forth in the Oregon Constitution was not co-extensive with that provided by U.S. Const. amend. V. The court held that before the state could force a witness to testify, the statutory immunity provided must totally supplant the constitutional right relinquished. Accordingly, the court held that only transactional immunity was constitutional in Oregon. The court found that the immunity afforded by Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 136.617-136.619 was insufficient to replace defendant's constitutional right, thus, was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court judgment convicting defendants of contempt for refusing to testify before a grand jury after being granted statutory use and derivative use immunity.

State v. Flores


CA No. A22413


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


68 Ore. App. 617; 685 P.2d 999; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3385


November 16, 1982, Submitted on remand; May 2, 1984, Resubmitted In Banc  
June 13, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted June 17, 1983


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied September 7, 1984. Petition for Review Denied October 30, 1984 (298 Or 151).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Edwin E. Allen, Judge. No. 10-81-05891; SC No. 28913.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an ex-convict, challenged his convictions for possession of a firearm and for possession of a controlled substance entered by the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon). After affirming the convictions, the court was again asked to review the matter as to search and seizure issues upon remand from the Oregon Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for running a stop sign. Before stopping him, the officer who was following him called for a cover unit because he saw defendant's head bobbing up and down in the car. The officer testified that defendant was very nervous during the stop and looked like he was trying to hide something in a plastic baggie. After defendant exited the car, the officer seized a plastic baggie containing marijuana from defendant's hand and a flowered cigarette purse and a leather change purse that he found in a brown paper bag on the front passenger seat of defendant's car. Another officer, who arrived as back-up, found a gun in a lidless container under some clothing on the back seat. The court held that the warrantless search required probable cause separate from the stop and that the trial court correctly refused to suppress the items found during the warrantless search. Specifically, the court held that, after finding the powder in the plastic bag in defendant's hand, the officers had probable cause to believe that there was more contraband in the car. The court further held that defendant's arrest for drug possession was a sufficient basis for the further search of the car.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.
