Robert Randall Co. v. Beaverton


CA No. A28386


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


68 Ore. App. 419; 682 P.2d 818; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3232


March 9, 1984, Argued and submitted  
May 23, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted March 9, 1984


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. Hollie Pihl, Judge. No. 82-1880C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, owners or property managers of apartments or apartment complexes, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Washington County (Oregon). The trial court found in favor of defendant city in plaintiffs' action to have an ordinance that set out the city's water rate structure declared arbitrary, unreasonable, and unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: The city's voters authorized a bond issue to build a water system for the city designed to meet the growth needs of the community and to remove it from dependence on another city for treated water. After the switchover to the new water system, the city council approved the ordinance, which established new rates and charges for water service. Multi-family units were charged the same base capacity charge as single family structures. Plaintiffs claimed that the ordinance discriminated against multi-family units because multi-family units used less water than single family units. The city claimed that the base capacity charge was designed to treat all residential users equally with regard to the fixed costs for the availability of the system. Upon review, the court found that its review of the city's ordinance was limited to the minimum security test because it related to local economics. The court observed that the ordinance accomplished equality among residential users for the fixed costs of the new water system. Treating the residential users equally with respect to fixed charges had a rational basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the city in plaintiffs' action to have an ordinance that set out the city's water rate structure declared arbitrary, unreasonable, and unconstitutional.

 

1134 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Collins


CA No. A27870


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


68 Ore. App. 101; 680 P.2d 713; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3128


October 24, 1983, Argued and submitted  
May 9, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted October 24, 1983


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 8, 1984. Petition for Review Denied July 3, 1984 (297 Or 458).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Klamath County. Ted Abram, Judge. No. 82-355C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Klamath County (Oregon) convicting him of criminal mistreatment in the first degree pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.205.


OVERVIEW: Defendant demurred to the indictment, asserting that the definition of a "dependent person" contained in the statute was so broad that a person could be indicted under § 163.205 for the assault of a clergyman or of a person receiving social security benefits. Consequently, defendant argued, the statute was unconstitutionally vague under both the state and the federal constitutions. On appeal, the court held that the right to challenge a criminal statute on vagueness grounds, however, was limited. Defendant did not argue that he was unable to determine from reading § 163.205 that his conduct of beating and choking a 10-month old child was prohibited. The court determined that defendant's conduct was unquestionably within § 163.205's prohibition, thus he could not challenge the constitutionality of the statute as applied to him on the ground of vagueness. The court also held that assuming that admission of testimony describing defendant's out-of-court admission to a police officer that he had committed a previous sexual assault on the child was error, it did not require reversal. Furthermore, the record indicated that the judge did not consider it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1135 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Atkeson v. Cupp


CA No. A28350


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


68 Ore. App. 196; 680 P.2d 722; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3136


February 27, 1984, Argued and submitted  
May 9, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted February 27, 1984


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 29, 1984. Petition for Review Denied August 8, 1984 (297 Or 546).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Val D. Sloper, Judge. No. 138,609.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), in three cases, dismissing their writs of habeas corpus upon the State's motion on the ground that petitioners' sole remedy was by post-conviction relief under Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 138.510 to 138.680.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners filed habeas corpus petitions alleging that certain irregularities in the selection of members and officers of the grand juries that indicted them rendered the indictments defective so that their convictions must be vacated. The trial court appointed the same attorney to represent all petitioners and then, on its own motion, consolidated the petitions into three cases. On the state's motion, it then dismissed all the petitions. On appeal, petitioners attacked the consolidation of the separate petitions into three cases. The court found consolidation was governed by Or. R. Civ. P. 53A, which permitted consolidation only on the motion of a party. Thus, the trial court did not have the authority to consolidate the cases. However, the court held that the trial court's error was harmless. The court also determined that a challenge to the lawfulness of the composition of the grand jury was a challenge to the proceedings on which the conviction was based; it was thus appropriately brought under post-conviction relief, which superseded habeas corpus. The court held that post-conviction relief was not an unconstitutional suspension of the writ of habeas corpus.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of petitioners' writs of habeas corpus.

 

1136 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dickenson


CA No. A29939


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


68 Ore. App. 283; 680 P.2d 1028; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3143


February 29, 1984, Argued and submitted  
May 9, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted February 29, 1984


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Harney County. Frank Yraguen, Judge. No. 83-05-1318-C.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court, Harney County (Oregon), which convicted defendant of first degree theft. Defendant specifically challenged that part of his sentence that ordered him to pay interest on the unpaid balance of the restitution ordered by the trial court, which was to commence on execution of the restitution order.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that a court's sentencing authority existed solely by statutory grants of power and that there was no statutory authority to impose interest as part of an order to pay restitution. The court held that the order to pay interest was proper only if interest would be recoverable as special damages in a civil action in conversion based on the same facts that gave rise to the case. Such interest represented the loss of the use of the money, and was proper from the time of the offense until judgment was entered. Interest after the entry of a final judgment or decree was an appendage to a judgment, not special damages authorized under Or. Rev. Stat. § 82.010(3); however, a restitution order was not a final judgment or decree subject to § 82.010(3). The court held that the interest on defendant's restitution order was not special damage but was to commence on execution of the order. In the absence of an agreement to pay, interest was required to be expressly authorized by statute; there was neither an agreement nor a statute authorizing the imposition of interest. Therefore, the interest ordered to commence on the execution of the restitution order was not authorized.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and remanded the case for resentencing.

 

1137 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. House


CA No. A25766


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


68 Ore. App. 360; 681 P.2d 173; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3389



May 9, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] On respondent's petition for reconsideration filed March 28, 1984. Former opinion filed February 8, 1984, 66 Or App 953, 676 P2d 892
Petition for Review Allowed July 31, 1984 (297 Or 546).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. Donald Ashmanskas, Judge. No. 82-0265. On respondent's reconsideration filed March 28, former opinion filed February 8, 1984 (66 Or App 953, 676 P2d 892).



DISPOSITION: Reconsideration granted; former opinion modified; former opinion affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent State filed a motion for reconsideration of the court's former judgment in which the court held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.062(1) was overbroad and on its face violated Or. Const. art. I, § 8.


OVERVIEW: In a former opinion, the court ruled that Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.062(1), an obscenity statute, was overbroad and on its face it violated Or. Const. art. I, § 8, and that defendant's demurrer to the indictment should have been sustained. The State filed a petition for reconsideration, arguing that the portions of the statute that prohibited "sadomasochistic abuse," "human masturbation" and "sexual intercourse" were severable. The court allowed the petition. The court held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.025(1)(c) was severable, that caselaw had not invalidated the entire disorderly conduct statute, and that Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.025(a) was valid. The court noted that although a statute could have been overbroad and on its face violative of Or. Const. art. I, § 8, its invalid parts could ordinarily be severed from its remaining parts unless the parts were inseparably related. The portions of Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.062(1) that prohibited any person from engaging in "sadomasochistic abuse," "human masturbation" or "sexual intercourse" in a live public show could be severed from the portion that dealt with "any touching" and, consistent with the legislative intent, remained in force.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion for reconsideration; modified the former opinion; and affirmed the former opinion as modified.

 

1138 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Barnhardt


CA No. A27083


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


67 Ore. App. 771; 680 P.2d 7; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3008


November 30, 1983, Argued and submitted  
April 18, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted November 30, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Tillamook County. Delbert Mayer, Judge. No. 20-233.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Tillamook County (Oregon), which convicted him, after a jury trial, of violating Or. Admin. R. 635-65-205(1), which prohibited the hunting of certain elk without the appropriate general elk rifle tags.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating hunting regulations and the trial court overruled his demurrer. On review, the court affirmed. On appeal, defendant claimed that Or. Admin. R. 635-65-205(1) was unconstitutionally vague. Defendant's assertion that the accusatory instrument was not definite and certain did not raise a constitutional claim of vagueness. That claim was raised for the first time on appeal, and the court declined to consider it. Defendant next claimed that the facts stated did not constitute an offense, under Or. Rev. Stat. § 135.630(4), because the offense charged infringed his constitutional right to bear arms. Nothing in the state or federal constitution prohibited the regulation of the use of a weapon. Defendant next claimed that the complaint failed to state an offense because no culpable mental state was alleged. Under Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.505, "offense" meant either a crime or violation. Thus, the citation stated facts sufficient to constitute an offense whether the offense was a strict liability misdemeanor or a violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.

 

1139 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Beebe


CA No. A29252


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


67 Ore. App. 738; 680 P.2d 11; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 3014


January 20, 1984, Argued and submitted  
April 18, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted January 20, 1984


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 15, 1984. Petition for Review Denied July 10, 1984 (297 Or 459).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Coos County. Robert E. Jones, Judge. MB No. 83-546.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the District Court of Coos County (Oregon), which sustained defendant's demurrer to a complaint charging racial intimidation in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.155(1). Defendant challenged the complaint under Or. Const. art. I, § 20, which guaranteed privileges and immunities, and the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with racial intimidation in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.155(1). Defendant filed a demurrer, arguing that it violated Or. Const. art. I, § 20 and the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV because it denied equal protection of the laws by granting greater protection to a victim who was assaulted because of his race, color, or national origin than to another person who was assaulted for some other reason. The trial court sustained the demurrer, and the state appealed. The court reversed and remanded the case for trial. Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.155 did not offer more protection to any class of victims. The enhancement of the penalty in Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.155 bore a rational relationship to the legitimate legislative purpose of preventing assaults on people based on their color or race, and thus it was constitutionally permissible to punish otherwise criminal conduct more severely when it was motivated by racial or ethnic hatred than by individual animosity. The court rejected defendant's argument that Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.155 violated his free speech rights under Or. Const. art. I, § 8, as the statute proscribed offensive conduct and not speech.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court sustaining defendant's demurrer to the state's complaint alleging that he committed the crime of racial intimidation.

State v. Hollywood


CA No. A27504


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


67 Ore. App. 546; 680 P.2d 655; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 2949


October 24, 1983, Argued and submitted  
April 11, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted October 24, 1983


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 14, 1984. Petition for Review Denied January 22, 1985 (298 Or 553).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. Jon B. Lund, Judge. Nos. 82-0347 & 82-0348.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the convictions for first degree rape, attempted rape, and first degree sexual abuse that the Circuit Court of Washington County (Oregon) adjudged against him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that evidentiary, procedural, and sentencing errors entitled him to relief. The prosecution prevailed. The four year old victim's statements were properly admitted against defendant, but not as excited utterances under Or. Evid. Code 803(2) due to the indeterminate delay that preceded them. Instead, the child's complaints were more appropriately admitted under the residual hearsay exception codified at Or. Evid. Code 803(24). Defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal was rightly denied because the evidence, viewed most favorably to the prosecution, was sufficient to permit any rational trier of fact to find defendant guilty of the several offenses charged. The trial court did not err in sentencing defendant to a mandatory minimum of seven years imprisonment. To do so was not unconstitutionally disproportionate to the gravity of defendant's offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

State v. Harrington


CA No. A28262


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


67 Ore. App. 608; 680 P.2d 666; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 2957


November 21, 1983, Argued and submitted  
April 11, 1984, Filed; Argued and Submitted November 21, 1983


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 29, 1984. Petition for Review Denied August 8, 1984 (297 Or 547).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Lane County. Bryan T. Hodges, Judge. No. B63-826.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the decision of the District Court, Lane County (Oregon), which sustained defendant's demurrer to a complaint charging racial intimidation.


OVERVIEW: The trial court sustained defendant's demurrer to a complaint charging racial intimidation and the state appealed. The intimidation statute enhanced the penalty for criminal mischief, Or. Rev. Stat. § 164.345, or harassment, Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.065, when such crimes were motivated by the race, color, religion, or national origin of the victim. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, holding that Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.065(1)(b) violated Or. Const. art. I, § 8. Legislation directed against obscene or abusive speech was not enacted until sometime after the adoption of the Oregon Constitution in 1859. The court therefore determined that obscene or abusive language spoken with intent to annoy or alarm was not an historical exception that was well established when the first American guarantees of freedom of expression were adopted and that the guarantees then or in 1859 demonstrably were not intended to reach.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision sustaining defendant's demurrer to the complaint that charged racial intimidation.

 

1142 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Frye v. Public Employees Retirement System


CA No. A26459


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


67 Ore. App. 617; 679 P.2d 875; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 2959


February 8, 1984, Argued and submitted  
April 11, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted February 8, 1984


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 25, 1984. Petition for Review Denied June 19, 1984 (297 Or 339).


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review from Public Employes Retirement System.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner former judge sought review of a final order of respondent Public Employes Retirement System (Oregon) (PERS), which denied her claim for the return of her contributions that she made to PERS. The former judge had voluntarily resigned to become a United States District Court judge. She made the contributions to the Judges' Retirement Fund, as was then required by ORS 1.310 to 1.390 (Oregon).


OVERVIEW: Under ORS 1.330 (Oregon), a judge who served for not less than six years or one full judicial term could be eligible for benefits equivalent to retirement pay in the event of physical or mental incapacity. The former judge was a state judge for less than 12 years or two full terms and was not incapacitated. The statutes specified no other circumstances under which payments could be made from the fund to a judge. However, ORS 1.340(4) (Oregon) provided that under specified circumstances pensions were payable from the fund to the surviving spouse of a judge who was not eligible for retirement pay at the time of death. The former judge contended that, because she was not entitled to retirement pay or other benefits from the fund, she was entitled to recover the contributions she made to it. She argued that the statutes should be construed to allow her recovery of the contributions and that, if they could not be so construed, they were unconstitutional. The court on appeal held that she had no statutory right to recover her contributions to the fund. Furthermore, the holding of the money was not an unconstitutional taking.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Norris v. Cupp


CA No. A26787


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


67 Ore. App. 393; 678 P.2d 756; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 2843


October 21, 1983, Argued and submitted  
March 21, 1984 Filed; Argued and submitted October 21, 1983


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied August 17, 1984. Petition for Review Denied September 18, 1984 (297 Or 824).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. John M. Copenhaver, Judge. No. 132,735.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed from Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief challenging the constitutionality of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.105, under which he received two consecutive terms of life imprisonment with minimum 20-year sentences for aggravated murder.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that the imposition of mandatory minimum sentences violated Or. Const. art. I, § 15, which required laws for the punishment of crime to be founded on the principles of reformation, and not of vindictive justice. The court observed, however, that in enacting penal statutes, the legislature was properly concerned with public safety and deterrence. Minimum sentences were not necessarily retaliatory but reflected the legislative concern for public safety and deterrence of crime.Because a person who murdered more than one person in a single criminal episode could legitimately be considered more dangerous to the public, the court concluded that Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.105 reasonably reflected the legislature's concern for public safety and deterrence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief.

 

1144 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Calderon


CA Nos. A25985, A25986, A25987 (Cases consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


67 Ore. App. 169; 678 P.2d 1245; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 2727


May 27, 1983, Argued and submitted  
March 7, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted May 27, 1983


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 13, 1984. Petition for Review Denied June 5, 1984 (297 Or 272).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Polk County. Harry Devlin, Judge. Nos. 29293, 29292 & 29294.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court, Polk County (Oregon) on two counts of manslaughter in the second degree and one count of third degree assault. On appeal, the issues included whether the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence of the alcohol content of his blood derived from blood samples taken on the night of an auto accident in which two people died and a third was injured.


OVERVIEW: On request of a deputy sheriff from the county where the accident occurred, the samples were taken by a medical technician at a hospital located in another county. On appeal, the court held that the deputy had probable cause to believe that defendant was driving under the influence of intoxicants and probable cause to believe that the blood samples would reveal evidence of alcohol consumption. The warrantless seizure of the samples was dictated by the practical necessity to seize the evidence before it dissipated. There was no merit to defendant's argument that a law enforcement officer from one county had no jurisdiction to make a warrantless seizure in another county. Under Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 133.525(2), 133.545(2), 133.575(1) any police officer could apply for and execute a search warrant in any jurisdiction within the state. It logically followed that any officer could conduct a search without a warrant in any jurisdiction within the state. Defendant's sentence of 10 years imprisonment with a three-year minimum term did not violate either Or. Const. art. I, § 16 or U.S. Const. amend. VIII.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1145 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Corvallis Lodge No. 1411 Loyal Order of Moose v. Oregon Liquor Control Com.


CA No. A26189


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


67 Ore. App. 15; 677 P.2d 76; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 2591


July 23, 1983, Argued and submitted  
February 22, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted July 25, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for determination of validity of rule of Oregon Liquor Control Commission.



DISPOSITION: Rule held invalid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Class B licensees sought a judicial determination of the validity of a rule promulgated by respondent Oregon Liquor Control Commission, Or. Admin. R. 845-08-045, which regulated the Class B licensees' service of liquor to nonmembers.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the OLCC's regulatory scheme, Class B licensees were allowed to serve alcohol to members and their guests, but not to members of the general public. As an exception to that rule, the OLCC promulgated Rule 845-08-045, which allowed the Class B licensees to host and to sell alcohol to nonmembers in connection with a function that no Class A licensee in the area was willing or able to accommodate. Under said rule, the Class B licensees were required to contact all Class A licensees within a 10 mile radius of its location and obtain their consent. The Class B licensees challenged the rule. The court held that the rule was invalid. The rule constituted an invalid delegation of governmental authority to private individuals because it failed to provide procedural safeguards to protect against the unaccountable exercise of government power. Given the competitive postures of the two classes, there was a substantial risk that the Class A licensees' decisions would have been colored by self-interest. Moreover, a Class B licensee was forced to confront potentially arbitrary and unresponsive exercise of governmental authority.


OUTCOME: The court held that the challenged rule was invalid.

Kalmiopsis Audubon Soc. v. Division of Lands


CA No. A26309


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


66 Ore. App. 810; 676 P.2d 885; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 2565


June 27, 1983, Argued and submitted  
February 8, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted June 27, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Judicial Review from Division of State Lands.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a non-profit corporation and a citizen, challenged an order of respondent Oregon's Division of State Lands, which renewed a permit to remove gravel from a gravel bar on the bank of a river. Petitioners sought review under the Administrative Procedure Act (APA), specifically Or. Rev. Stat. § 183.482, claiming that the action was inconsistent with Oregon's Statewide Planning Goals (Goals) listed under Or. Admin. R. ch. 660.


OVERVIEW: After a hearing, the Division found that granting a permit to remove gravel from the river bank to the applicant was not inconsistent with the Goals and was not inconsistent with the protection, conservation, and best use of the water and gravel resources and of the fishery and other biological resources. The Division claimed that the court did not have jurisdiction to consider the appeal under 1979 Or. Laws 772, §§ 4-6, as amended by 1981 Or. Laws 748, § 4(1). The court held that petitioners were entitled to appeal the decision under the APA, specifically Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 183.480 and 183.482, even though the action was a land use decision. However, the court held that the aspects of the decision in which the Division was required to apply the Goals under Or. Rev. Stat. § 197.015(10) was within the exclusive jurisdiction of the Land Use Board of Appeals. Additionally, the court held that petitioners did not demonstrate why the record did not support the finding that the removal of gravel from the river was not inconsistent with any use of the river and that the Division did not have to articulate what was the "best use" of the resource under Or. Rev. Stat. § 541.610.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, but declined to review any issues relating to the Goals.

 

1147 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. House


CA No. A25766


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


66 Ore. App. 953; 676 P.2d 892; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 2566


April 27, 1983, Argued and submited; December 1, 1983, Resubmitted In Banc  
February 8, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted April 27, 1983; resubmited in banc December 1, 1983


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Affirmed as Modified May 9, 1984 (68 Or App 360, 681 P2d 173). Petition for Review Allowed July 31, 1984 (297 Or 546).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. Donald C. Ashmanskas, Judge. No. 82-0265.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a male dancer, appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court, Washington County (Oregon) pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.062 for engaging in sexual conduct in a live public show. He was sentenced to pay a fine.


OVERVIEW: The indictment charged that defendant engaged in sexual conduct in a live public show in a bar, wearing only a "G-string," by touching his genitals, pubic area, and buttocks against female spectators and letting them touch him, in an act of apparent sexual stimulation or gratification. The court reversed his conviction, finding that the trial court should have sustained defendant's demurrer to the indictment because Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.062 was overbroad and therefore violated Or. Const. art. I, § 8. Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.062 prohibited expression that was protected by Or. Const. art. I, § 8, which prohibited the passage of any law restraining the free expression of opinion or restricting the right to speak, write, or print freely on any subject whatever. It was acceptable in stage performances for one performer to touch the buttocks, breasts, or genitals of another performer. The person touched might respond so that a reasonable person in the audience would perceive that the performer touched was sexually stimulated or gratified. Because Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.062 made such touching criminal, it was overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's conviction of defendant.

State v. Anderson


CA No. A26461


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


66 Ore. App. 855; 677 P.2d 39; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 2584


April 20, 1983, Argued and submitted  
February 8, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted April 20, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Multnomah County. Aaron Brown, Jr., Judge. No. M79250.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the District Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which convicted defendant of DUII.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a first-time offender. At his request, the trial court placed him in the DUII rehabilitation program then in operation, Or. Rev. Stat. § 484.385. The program required a fee to participate. Defendant was indigent and requested that the fee be waived. The trial court was unable to waive the fee but gave defendant one year to raise the fee. At the end of one-year period, defendant still had not raised the money. The trial court ultimately entered a judgment of conviction and imposed a fine. In reversing and remanding, the court held that denying defendant the opportunity of a rehabilitation program because of his indigency violated the Equal Protection Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The effect of § 484.385 was to discriminate against defendant in a way that was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

 

1149 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cantwell


CA No. A28712 (Cases consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


66 Ore. App. 848; 676 P.2d 353; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 2589


November 21, 1983, Argued and submitted  
February 8, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted November 21, 1983


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 16, 1984. Petition for Review Denied May 15, 1984 (297 Or 124).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Lane County. Laurie K. Smith, Judge. Nos. B64-751, B64-713.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Lane County (Oregon), which sustained defendants' demurrers to complaints charging them with disorderly conduct under Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.025(1)(a) on the ground that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad in its entirety.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with disorderly conduct under § 166.025(1)(a). The lower court sustained defendants' demurrers to the complaints charging them with disorderly conduct. The state challenged the lower court judgment as it held that § 166.025(1)(a) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The court reversed the lower court judgment and remanded for trial because it found that the words "fighting" and "violent, tumultuous, or threatening behavior" as used in § 166.025(1)(a) did not encompass constitutionally protected speech but rather physical acts of aggression. In prohibiting specific physical acts, § 166.025(1)(a) did not run afoul of Or. Const. art. 1, § 8. The court concluded that § 166.025(1)(a) made it unlawful only to use physical force or physical conduct that was immediately likely to produce the use of force and was intended to create a risk of public inconvenience, annoyance, or alarm and was not void for vagueness on its face.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court judgment that sustained defendants' demurrers on the disorderly conduct charges and remanded for trial.

 

1150 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cota


CA Nos. A23491, A23492 (Cases consolidated.)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


66 Ore. App. 650; 675 P.2d 1101; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 2482


August 30, 1982, Argued and submitted; September 9, 1983, Resubmitted In Banc  
January 25, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted August 30, 1982; resubmitted in banc September 9, 1983


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 9, 1984. Petition for Review Denied May 15, 1984 (297 Or 124).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. John C. Beatty, Jr., Judge (Judgment and Probation Order). James R. Ellis, Judge (Motion to Suppress). Nos. C81-01-30768, C81-01-30911.



DISPOSITION: CA A23492 is reversed and remanded for new trial; CA A23491 is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal of two cases, defendant appealed his convictions on three counts of possession of a controlled substance, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 475.992(4), and one count of delivery of a controlled substance, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 475.992(1). Two of the possession counts were based on evidence discovered when police officers were executing a warrant for defendant's arrest at his residence.


OVERVIEW: In respect to two of the possession counts, defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence discovered when police officers were executing a warrant for his arrest at his residence. Officers had arrived at defendant's residence to execute the warrant. Two officers walked up to the front door. The officers saw a small boy and a man. The man, defendant, answered the door and acknowledged his identity. An officer handed defendant a copy of the warrant of arrest. The officers entered the house without requesting defendant's consent. The officers asked if there was anyone else in the house to care for the boy. Defendant told the officers that no one else was in the house. The boy, however, led the officer to his father who was in the house. The officers then searched the rest of the house and found drugs and paraphernalia in an upstairs room. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress the evidence. The court reversed and remanded for a new trial. The court stated that once the boy's father was located, there was no "practical necessity" to search the rest of the house. Thus, the evidence should have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: In respect to the case involving two of the possession counts which were based on evidence discovered when police officers were executing a warrant for defendant's arrest at his residence, the court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded for a new trial. The court affirmed defendant's conviction in the other case.

 

1151 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Rocky B. Fisheries, Inc. v. North Bend Fabrication & Machine, Inc.


CA No. A25230


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


66 Ore. App. 625; 676 P.2d 319; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 2501; 1984 AMC 2594


July 8, 1983, Argued and submitted  
January 25, 1984, Filed;


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 9, 1984. Petition for Review Denied April 24, 1984 (297 Or 82).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Richard L. Barron, Judge. No. A8110-06552.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff shipowners appealed the orders of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which granted defendant shipfitter's motion for summary judgment and granted defendant individuals' motion to dismiss claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 that seizure of a vessel under Or. Rev. Stat. § 783.010 et seq. was unconstitutional as well as for conversion, noncompliance with provisional process, abuse of process, and interference with contract.


OVERVIEW: The shipfitter claimed a lien for supplies and services furnished for the construction of a vessel and brought an in rem proceeding under state law to seize the vessel and to enforce its lien. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that (1) Or. Rev. Stat. ch. 783 only applied to non-maritime liens, such as the present one, so that the state court did not invade the exclusive admiralty jurisdiction of the federal courts; (2) due process required notice and hearing except under exceptional circumstances, and a seizure statute must be narrowly drawn and construed; (3) the lien did not come into effect until seizure, so pre-seizure notice would give a shipowner a chance to remove the vessel and avoid the lien; (4) the bond and release provision was construed to offer a rapid post-seizure opportunity to challenge the seizure, which satisfied due process; (5) the seizure was valid so there was no conversion; (6) abuse of process required an ulterior motive for collateral gain and did not occur when lien claimants vied for priority; and (7) to prove interference with a contract, a claimant had to show not only interference but also a duty of non-interference or improper means.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that granted the individuals' motion to dismiss and the shipfitter's motion for summary judgment.

 

1152 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Whiting Corp.


CA No. A27452


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


66 Ore. App. 541; 674 P.2d 1194; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 2476; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P10,001


September 28, 1983, Argued and submitted  
January 18, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted September 28, 1983


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 16, 1984. Petition for Review Denied April 24, 1984 (297 Or 82).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Charles Crookham, Judge. No. A8210-06006.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff victim sought review of a judgment rendered by the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which held that his product liability action against defendant manufacture was time barred under Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.905(1) because it was not brought within eight years after the product was purchased.


OVERVIEW: The victim was an employer, who suffered injuries due to a defective condition in an overhead bridge crane. The victim sued the crane's manufacture, and the trial court dismissed the suit as being time barred under Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.905(1) because the suit was not brought within eight years from the date the crane was purchased. The victim appealed, arguing that the statute denied him access to the courts. The court held that § 30.905(1) served legitimate public purposes by preventing claims where evidence could be unreliable and unavailable due to lapse of time, by allowing persons to plan their affairs free from the burden of protracted and unknown potential liability, and to stabilize product liability insurance rates. The court stated that given these purposes, the statute did not unconstitutionally deny the victim access to the courts. The court also ruled that the statute did not deny the victim equal protection because it satisfied the rational basis test, since a statute of ultimate repose would have a stabilizing effect on the insurance situation. Finally, the court concluded that § 30.905(1) did not violate due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1153 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


CA No. A22787


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


66 Ore. App. 374; 675 P.2d 1060; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 2449


June 10, 1983, Argued and submitted  
January 11, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 11, 1984. Petition for Review Denied June 19, 1984 (297 Or 339).
Review denied by State v. Smith, 297 Ore. 339, 683 P.2d 1370, 1984 Ore. LEXIS 1545 (1984)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Smith v. Maass, 881 F.2d 1084, 1989 U.S. App. LEXIS 11776 (9th Cir. Or., 1989)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Philip T. Abraham, Judge. C No. 81-02-30858.



DISPOSITION: Judgment modified to delete the minimum sentence; affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which convicted defendant of attempted murder, first degree assault, and first degree robbery. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying defendant's pretrial motion requesting access to the county courthouse law library and in denying defendant's motion to suppress items seized during a search of a hotel room that defendant shared with his girlfriend.


OVERVIEW: Defendant also argued that the trial court erred in classifying defendant as a dangerous offender. On appeal, the court found no reversible error. First, defendant was not denied access to the law library because defendant's legal advisor, an attorney, was expressly authorized to supply defendant with materials from that library. Second, defendant's motion to suppress was properly denied because defendant's girlfriend, who rented the hotel room herself, gave oral and written consent sufficient to authorize the warrantless search. Third, defendant was properly classified as a dangerous offender under Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.725, and the psychiatric report required in making that determination under § 161.735(3) was not unconstitutional, because defendant perpetrated a violent attack on his victim, had a history of violent criminal behavior, and because precedent established that the fact that a penal statute was based on a prediction of future dangerousness did not render the statute violative of the Due Process Clause. Finally, the trial court erred in imposing a minimum mandatory sentence pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.610; thus, the judgment was modified by deleting that sentence.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the trial court by deleting the minimum mandatory sentence, and, as modified, affirmed the judgment.

 

1154 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Towerhill Condo. Ass'n v. Am. Condo. Homes, Inc.


CA No. A26610


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


66 Ore. App. 342; 675 P.2d 1051; 1984 Ore. App. LEXIS 2445


September 14, 1983, Argued and submitted  
January 4, 1984, Filed; Argued and submitted September 14, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Charles S. Crookham, Judge. No. A8204-02408.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff condominium association sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which granted defendant builders' motion to dismiss the association's complaint against them for breach of warranty and negligence, holding that the association lacked legal capacity to sue, was not the real part in interest, and failed to state facts sufficient to constitute a claim.


OVERVIEW: The builders' entered agreements for the sale of individual condominium units that contained express warranties concerning the general and limited common elements of the condominium complex. The association, as the representative of the condominium unit owners, brought an action against the builders alleging breach of warranty and seeking damages based upon the express warranties, and also alleging negligence in the construction of the common elements of the complex. The trial court granted the builders' motion to dismiss the complaint. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that: 1) the association, organized as a non-profit corporation, had the capacity to sue pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 61.061(2), and was the real party in interest; 2) the association had the authority to incur an obligation for defendants' legal fees if the builders prevailed in the litigation; 3) although the builders' contract might be indirectly impaired in an action by the association by modifying the remedy available to the builder, such modification would not impair the value of the contracts by destroying any meaningful remedy; therefore 4) federal or state constitutions were not violated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which dismissed the association's complaint against the builders for breach of warranty and negligence, and remanded the case to the trial court.

State v. Moyle


CA No. A28286


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


66 Ore. App. 274; 673 P.2d 1366; 1983 Ore. App. LEXIS 4054


September 20, 1983, Argued and submitted  
December 21, 1983, Filed; Argued and submitted September 20, 1983


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 9, 1984. Petition for Review Allowed June 5, 1984 (297 Or 272).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Multnomah County. Frank L. Bearden, Judge. DA No. 240844-8208.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the judgment of the District Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss harassment charges against him as being violative of his right to free speech.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of conveying a telephonic threat to inflict serious physical injury for threats that he made against two different victims. The trial court sustained defendant's demurrer to the charges finding that the statute violated Or. Const. Art. I, §8. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for trial finding that the threats made by defendant were not of the type intended to be protected by the constitution. The court found that the telephone harassment statute was not overbroad because the statute was only directed at instances in which the action threatened was itself wrongful. The court found that the statute was not vague because the language of the statute was clear and specific.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for trial.

 

1156 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Columbia County School Dist. v. Columbia County


CA No. A26424


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


66 Ore. App. 237; 674 P.2d 608; 1983 Ore. App. LEXIS 4048


August 5, 1983, Argued and submitted  
December 21, 1983, Filed; Argued and submitted August 5, 1983


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 10, 1984. Petition for Review Denied April 17, 1984 (296 Or 829).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Columbia County. Delbert B. Mayer, Judge. No. 27649.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions to determine defendant county's entitlement to costs and expenses pursuant to former ORS 275.275; affirmed in all other respects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a county, a county treasurer, and county commissioners, appealed a decision by the Circuit Court, Columbia County (Oregon), which rendered a judgment for plaintiffs, a state, school districts, a city, and a fire protection district, holding that plaintiffs were entitled to receive annually the accrued interest on mineral lease income received by defendants.


OVERVIEW: One school district filed a complaint for declaratory judgment and a petition for alternative writ of mandamus, seeking a declaration that it was entitled to a pro-rata share of interest earned on the mineral revenues for fiscal year 1980-81 and subsequent years. Th school district amended its complaint to include a petition for a writ of review. All other taxing districts in the county were named as opposite parties in the petition. The court concluded that the acts of the county commissioners were ministerial acts. Therefore, the trial court correctly concluded that declaratory relief was the proper remedy. A writ of review was not available to plaintiffs. The trial court correctly concluded that Or. Rev. Stat. § 34.030, which pertained to writs of review, did not apply. The court determined that Or. Rev. Stat. § 275.275 provided that the county should receive a minimum of 10 percent of the "total" proceeds as administrative costs. The interest earned on the principal received from the mineral leases was a component of the "total proceeds." Accordingly, the county was entitled to 10 percent of the principal and interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part the judgment of the trial court and remanded, with instructions, to determine the county's entitlement to costs and expenses. In all other respects, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1157 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


P v. Children's Services Div.


CA No. A27533


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


66 Ore. App. 66; 673 P.2d 864; 1983 Ore. App. LEXIS 4019


September 19, 1983, Argued and submitted  
December 7, 1983, Filed; Argued and submitted September 19, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Douglas County. Robert M. Stults, Judge. No. A82-5.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Children's Services Division (CSD) sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court, Douglas County (Oregon), which dismissed respondent adoptive parents petition to adopt a child on the ground that Or. Rev. Stat. § 109.096(2), which required notice be given to the father of the adoption proceedings, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The child was born to an unwed mother who stated in an affidavit that she met and had sexual relations with the father only once, that she had no further contact with him since, and that his whereabouts were unknown. She surrendered the child to CSD for adoption. CSD placed the child with the adoptive parents, who petitioned to adopt the child. CSD consented to the adoption and recommended to the trial court that the adoption be allowed. The adoptive parent's petition to adopt was dismissed following the trial court's denial of CSD's motion to dispense with notice of the adoption to the father pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 109.096(2). The court reversed the dismissal of the petition and remanded for further proceedings. The court held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 109.096(2), which did not require notice of the adoption proceedings be given to the father under the circumstances, satisfied the father's Fourteenth Amendment due process rights. The court stated that because the father had not come forward to initiate a parent-child relationship, his liberty interest was insufficient to justify the procedures necessary to apprise him of the adoption proceeding.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the adoptive parents petition was reversed, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1158 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lyon


CA No. A26214


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


65 Ore. App. 790; 672 P.2d 1358; 1983 Ore. App. LEXIS 3942


August 24, 1983, Argued and submitted  
November 30, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. Jon B. Lund, Judge. No. 82-0147.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Washington County (Oregon), which convicted him of murder in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.115. Defendant contended that § 163.115 contravened the due process provisions of both the United States and Oregon Constitutions by placing the burden on defendant of proving the affirmative defense of extreme emotional disturbance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant arrived at his ex-wife's house armed with a rifle and a pistol. After letting himself into the house, he went to his ex-wife's bedroom. He found her in bed with her boyfriend. The boyfriend fired at and wounded defendant. Defendant fired back and killed the victim. Defendant was transported to the hospital. He was visited several times by police while hospitalized, but was not charged until a week after his release. The indictment charged defendant with aggravated murder, murder, and burglary. At trial, he was convicted only of murder and he appealed. The court held that the affirmative defense of extreme emotional disturbance did not serve to negate any of the facts the State was required to prove in order to convict. The court held that the evidence supported the trial judge's findings that defendant was not in custody or deprived of his freedom of action in a significant way for purposes of mandating Miranda warnings. The court concluded that the challenged statements were given to the police in an investigatory and not a custodial setting. Miranda warnings were not required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants conviction for murder.

State v. Huffman


CA No. A24490


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


65 Ore. App. 594; 672 P.2d 1351; 1983 Ore. App. LEXIS 3916


April 27, 1983, Argued and submitted  
November 23, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Maurice K. Merten, Judge. No. 10-81-04620.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), which convicted him of perjury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of perjury in a municipal court trial regarding a traffic offense. After that trial, a witness came forward and stated that defendant had paid him to commit perjury. The prosecutor initiated grand jury proceedings and warned all defendant's witnesses of the possible consequences of perjury. Defendant asserted that the prosecutor's conduct required dismissal of the perjury charge because it violated the discovery rules and deprived him of compulsory process. The court rejected defendant's arguments. It was bound by the trial court's finding that the prosecutor's actions did not affect the witnesses' testimony. Without showing some effect on the testimony, the court concluded that defendant could not establish a violation of the Compulsory Process or Due Process Clauses. It also concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting a witness's testimony regarding a discussion with defendant in which defendant told him to "get rid of" the state's witness in the municipal court trial. The court found that the testimony was relevant, circumstantial evidence of a conspiracy to commit perjury alleged in the indictment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Kemp v. Workers' Compensation Dep't


CA No. A24274


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


65 Ore. App. 659; 672 P.2d 1343; 1983 Ore. App. LEXIS 3924


January 28, 1983, Argued and submitted  
November 23, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration of Denial of Attorney Fees Denied March 2, 1984. Petition for Review Denied March 20, 1984 (296 Or 638). Reconsideration Allowed. Former Opinion Adhered to as Modified March 7, 1984 (67 Or App 270, 677 P2d 725). Reconsideration Denied April 27, 1984. Petition for Review Denied May 22, 1984 (297 Or 227).


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review of Rules of Workers' Compensation Department. No. 5-1982.



DISPOSITION: OAR 436-69-201(2) and 436-69-401(1) and (2) held valid; OAR 436-69-301(3), 436-69-501 and 436-69-801(4) held invalid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a declaration from the court as to the validity of five rules established by respondent the Workers' Compensation Department, which included Or. Admin. R. 436-69-201(2), 436-69-401(1) and (2), 436-69-301(3), 436-69-501 and 436-69-801(4).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner filed an action against the department seeking a declaration as to the validity of five rules. After reviewing the rules, the court found that Or. Admin. R. 436-69-201(2) and 436-69-40191) and (2) were valid and that Or. Admin. R. 436-69-301(3), 436-69-501, and 436-69-801(4) were invalid. The court held Or. Admin. R. 436-69-201(2), which dealt with the frequency and extent of medical treatment was valid where the rule did not limit treatment but merely required that if the treatment exceeded the prescribed number of visits, the physician needed to submit a report justifying further treatment. The court found Or. Admin. R. 436-69-301(3), which allowed persons of well-recognized religions the right to refuse rehabilitative treatments was unconstitutional as violative of freedom of religion where the department failed to show the necessity for drawing the suspect distinction between beliefs. The court determined Admin. R. 436-69-501 was invalid because it in effect punished a claimant by refusing to pay duly incurred medical bills. The court concluded Or. Admin R. 436-69-801 invalidly provided an additional penalty when one had already been authorized by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court held that two of the rules challenged by petitioner which dealt with the subject of frequency and extent of medical treatment were valid. The court found that three of the rules challenged were invalid, including a rule that allowed persons of well-recognized religions the right to refuse treatments.

 

1161 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ramer


CA No. A25366


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


65 Ore. App. 480; 671 P.2d 723; 1983 Ore. App. LEXIS 3818


June 29, 1983, Argued and submitted  
November 9, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Washington County. Karl W. Freerksen, Jr., Judge. No. M 51602.



DISPOSITION: Conviction of carrying a concealed weapon reversed; conviction of possessing a stabbing weapon affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court, Washington County (Oregon) that convicted defendant of carrying a concealed weapon, a violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.240, and possessing a stabbing weapon, a violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.510.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of carrying a concealed weapon, a violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.240, and possessing a stabbing weapon, a violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.510. The weapon that gave rise to the charges was described at trial as a switchblade. Reversing defendant's conviction on the concealed weapon count, the court held that because a switchblade was a type of pocket knife and it was not illegal under Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.240 to carry a concealed pocket knife, it was not illegal under that statute to carry a concealed switchblade. The court found that because defendant framed his appeal in the alternative, the effect of arguing in the alternative was to admit that a challenge to the conviction on the possession count could only succeed if the appeal of the concealed weapon count failed. The court ruled that the appeal on the concealed weapon count did not fail, and thus affirmed defendant's conviction for possessing a stabbing weapon under Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.510.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for carrying a concealed weapon, but affirmed defendant's conviction for possessing a stabbing weapon affirmed.

 

1162 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Millspaugh v. Port of Portland


CA No. A26400


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


65 Ore. App. 389; 671 P.2d 743; 1983 Ore. App. LEXIS 3834


May 13, 1983, Argued and submitted  
November 9, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied January 6, 1984. Petition for Review Denied February 8, 1984 (296 Or 411).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Robert E. Jones, Judge. No. A8106-03273.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff longshoreman sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which granted the summary judgment motion of defendant port on a personal injury claim. The circuit court found that because the longshoreman's injury took place on the port's dock instead of on navigable waters of the United States, the port was immune from tort liability under Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.265(3)(a).


OVERVIEW: Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.265(3)(a) left the port immune from the longshoreman's claim because he had received worker's compensation benefits under the Longshoremen's and Harbor Workers' Compensation Act (LHWCA), 33 U.S.C.S. § 901 et seq. The circuit court reasoned that state law, rather than federal maritime law, applied to the claim because the longshoreman was on a ladder that was permanently affixed to the port's dock when he was injured. The court agreed, holding that: (1) because the ladder was not an appurtenance to the ship like a gangplank, the fact that the longshoreman was on the ladder instead of on the dock itself did not trigger maritime jurisdiction; (2) the fact that the injury was covered by the LHWCA did not mean that federal maritime law applied; (3) the longshoreman's claim that the port waived its immunity by procuring liability insurance failed because he provided no evidence of such insurance in his opposition to the port's summary judgment motion; and (4) Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.265(3)(a) did not violate constitutional guarantees of equal protection under Or. Const. art. I, § 20 or the 14th Amendment of the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1163 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Smith


CA No. A26447


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


65 Ore. App. 309; 671 P.2d 768; 1983 Ore. App. LEXIS 3850


May 31, 1983, Submitted on record and briefs  
November 9, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Jackson County. Loren L. Sawyer, Judge. No. 81-1281-NJ-2.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Costs to neither party.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee wife filed a divorce petition against appellant husband while the husband was incarcerated. The Jackson County Circuit Court (Oregon) entered a dissolution decree and the husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the husband was served with the wife's divorce complaint and he was transferred to a state penitentiary, he filed a responsive pleading. A default judgment had been entered against the husband, but he obtained relief from that judgment. The husband unsuccessfully attempted to reach a settlement with the wife, and a hearing was scheduled on her petition. The husband was still incarcerated and was unable to attend the hearing; the trial court denied the husband's motion for a continuance. The wife's divorce decree was entered. On appeal, the court found that the trial court had no duty to notify the husband of every action that it took; though incarcerated, the husband was able to communicate with the trial court and keep abreast of his affairs. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the husband's motion for a continuance. The divorce decree was based on all information provided; the trial court had no duty to gather information that the husband failed to provide. Finally, the husband failed to state a claim for violation of his constitutional rights based on the trial court's failure to transport him to the divorce hearing.


OUTCOME: The dissolution decree was affirmed.

 

1164 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Perkey v. Psychiatric Sec. Review Bd.


CA No. A26111


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


65 Ore. App. 259; 670 P.2d 1061; 1983 Ore. App. LEXIS 3773


May 9, 1983, Argued and submitted  
October 26, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Judicial Review from Psychiatric Security Review Board. No. 79-225.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a patient committed to a state hospital, challenged an order of respondent Psychiatric Security Review Board (Oregon), which continued its jurisdiction over him and continued his commitment. The patient alleged that the statute transferring jurisdiction over him from the circuit court to the Board was an unconstitutional ex post facto law and that the transfer of jurisdiction violated the separation of powers doctrine.


OVERVIEW: The patient was admitted to a state hospital at age nine. He was later accused of murdering a fellow patient. He was found not guilty by reason of insanity and was committed to the state hospital for life or until he became sane or was otherwise released. Under 1977 Or. Laws ch. 380, § 22 (Act), jurisdiction for such commitments of patients was transferred from the circuit court to the Psychiatric Security Review Board (PSRB). The patient challenged the PSRB's order that continued its jurisdiction over him and continued his commitment. The court affirmed, determining that the Act was not ex post facto as applied to the patient where he failed to show that the transfer of jurisdiction to the PSRB increased his penalty, imposed upon him a greater burden of proof, or otherwise deprived him of any due process rights. The Act did not violate the principal of separation of powers under Or. Const. art. III, § 1 because delegation of adjudicatory powers to administrative agencies was valid if judicial review was provided at some stage of the proceeding. Review of the PSRB's orders by the court was provided by ORS § 161.385(9)(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Kane v. Tri-County Metropolitan Transp. Dist.


CA No. A26359


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


65 Ore. App. 55; 670 P.2d 178; 1983 Ore. App. LEXIS 3671


June 3, 1983, Argued and submitted  
October 12, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 25, 1983. Petition for Review Denied February 8, 1984 (296 Or 411).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. Alan C. Bonebrake, Judge. No. 82-0073C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of an order of the Circuit Court, Washington County (Oregon), which granted the motion of defendant Tri-County Metropolitan Transportation District of Oregon, for summary judgment of the taxpayer's claim that Tri-County Metropolitan Transp. Dist., Or., Ordinance No. 92 (ordinance), which imposed an excise tax on an individual's net earnings from self-employment, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was self-employed. He filed an action for declaratory relief, alleging that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it imposed a tax on his net earnings from self-employment and on no other class of individuals or businesses. The district, a municipal corporation, was authorized to levy an income tax on the earnings of all individuals and business in the district, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. 267.370. The ordinance was enacted pursuant to that authority. The trial court ruled that the ordinance was constitutional and granted the district's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court held that Or. Const. art. IX, § 1, which provided that all taxes were to be levied uniformly, did not apply to the taxes imposed by the district, as it was a municipal corporation, and § 1 applied only to taxes that operated throughout the State. The court further held that a governmental authority was permitted to single out a subterritory for separate treatment so long as the classification rested on "genuine differences." The court concluded that the district's decision to tax only income derived from self-employment was based on genuine difference, thus, the ordinance was valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which granted the district's motion for summary judgment.

 

1166 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Bank of Oregon v. Independent News


CA No. A24067


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


65 Ore. App. 29; 670 P.2d 616; 1983 Ore. App. LEXIS 3672; 9 Media L. Rep. 2425


July 27, 1983, Argued and submitted  
October 12, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 25, 1983. Petition for Review Allowed February 8, 1984 (296 Or 411) See 298 Or 434, 693 P2d 35 (1985).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Richard L. Unis, Judge. No. A 7908-03679.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a bank and its president, brought a libel action against defendants, two reporters and their newspaper. After denying the bank's and the president's motion to amend their complaint, the Circuit Court of Multnomah County (Oregon) entered summary judgment for the reporters and the newspaper. The bank and the president appealed.


OVERVIEW: The newspaper published their reporters' article, which alleged that the bank and its president had had engaged in a series of wrongful acts to divert a customer's money and credit to another customer. The bank and its president brought a libel action contending that the newspaper and its reporters did not take adequate care to ascertain the truth or falsehood of the customer's charges before publishing them. The trial court entered summary judgment for the newspaper and its reporters, finding that the bank and its president, as private individuals, could not recover because they failed to allege gross negligence. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the bank and its president should have been allowed to amend their complaint to allege negligence, which was the proper level of culpability that a private individual had to prove against a "media defendant" to recover for libel. Thus, in order to recover, the bank and its president merely had to prove the common law elements of libel and that the newspaper and its reporters were at least negligent in failing to ascertain whether the defamatory publication was true or false. Therefore, summary judgment was precluded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's entry of summary judgment for the reporters and the newspaper in the defamation action brought by the bank and its president. Moreover, the trial court erred by denying the bank's and the president's motion to amend their complaint to allege negligence.

 

1167 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Malaer v. Flying Lion, Inc.


CA No. A24612


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


65 Ore. App. 154; 670 P.2d 214; 1983 Ore. App. LEXIS 3684


March 14, 1983, Argued and submitted  
October 12, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. Gregory E. Milnes, Judge. No. 42-726.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff farmer appealed the decision of the Circuit Court, Washington County (Oregon), which granted summary judgment to defendant pesticide operator (operator) in the farmer's action for damages to his orchard allegedly caused by aerial spraying of a pesticide.


OVERVIEW: The aerial pesticide sprayed by the operator on another property contaminated the farmer's orchard. An extension service agent assessed the farmer's damages. The operator's insurance adjuster inspected the damage, assured the farmer that the claim was legitimate, that he would take care of it and not to worry about it, and confirmed in writing that the claim was being processed. In the farmer's action for loss of profits, the trial court granted summary judgment to the operator because the farmer failed to report the loss to the state under Or. Rev. Stat. § 634.172(1). On appeal, the court reversed, finding questions of fact as to whether the operator was estopped from relying on failure to file the report in denying the farmer's claim. The court ruled that the farmer had not substantially complied with the statute because he made no report to the state or the operator and that informing the operator and extension agent was insufficient. The court concluded the adjuster's assurances, while not telling the farmer that recovery required a state report, raised questions as to whether the statements could have been interpreted as a promise to settle the claim and pay the damage.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order granting summary judgment to the operator and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1168 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Universal Ideas Corp. v. Linn County


CA No. A23408


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


64 Ore. App. 805; 669 P.2d 1165; 1983 Ore. App. LEXIS 3656


January 7, 1983, Argued and submitted  
October 5, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Linn County. James C. Goode, Judge. No. 80-0400.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judgment debtor challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Linn County (Oregon), in favor of appellee county. The judgment debtor was plaintiff in a contracts case which was resolved in favor of the judgment creditor. The judgment debtor alleged that the county clerk had negligently failed to mail notice of entry of judgment until after expiration of the appeals period, thereby precluding the judgment debtor from appealing.


OVERVIEW: The judgment debtor contended that notice of entry had not been mailed as required by former ORS 18.030, now ORCP 70B(1). The debtor presented its attorney's affidavit stating that had the clerk mailed notice, an appeal would have been filed, judgment would have been reversed, and the debtor had sustained damages as a result. The trial court concluded that the clerk was negligent, was not immune, that the debtor was not contributorily negligent, but that the debtor was collaterally estopped from contending that the issues in the prior litigation would have been resolved differently. On appeal, the court held that the trial court had improperly applied the doctrine of collateral estoppel. The court compared the case to one of legal malpractice, where as an element of recovery, the debtor was required to prove that had the clerk complied with the statute, the outcome would have been favorable. The first issue for the trial court was to determine from the record, as though a direct appeal, whether the debtor would have prevailed on appeal. If that were resolved in the its favor, then retrial of the original case should be had to determine whether the debtor would have prevailed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1169 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Accident Prevention Div. v. Hoffman Constr. Co.


No. A26322


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


64 Ore. App. 73; 667 P.2d 543; 1983 Ore. App. LEXIS 3262


May 11, 1983, Argued and submitted  
August 3, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Judicial Review from Workers' Compensation Board. No. SH-81-420.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Accident Prevention Division (Oregon) sought review of an order of the Workers' Compensation Board (Oregon), which held that it was improper to issue a citation to an employer for a "repeat violation" of an occupational safety standard while the citation for the prior violation was being contested by the employer and had not yet been upheld by a final order.


OVERVIEW: The Accident Prevention Division issued a citation to an employer after inspecting its worksite. The employer contested the citation and, after another inspection of the same worksite, the employer received another citation. Following a hearing, a referee concluded that the repeat violation citation was improper. On appeal, the court noted that referee's decision effectively invalidated Or. Admin. R. 436-46-160(3), which authorized the issuance of repeat violation citations. The court determined that the basic policy of providing employers with incentives to comply with the safety requirements of the Oregon Safe Employment Act, ORS 654.001 to 654.295 (Oregon), was intrinsic to the statutory scheme of enforcement of the Act, that the rule promoted that policy by discouraging employers from avoiding the incentive provided by the enhanced penalties for repeat violations by contesting the prior citation, and that the rule was consistent with both the language and the policy of the Act. The court further determined that the employer was given an adequate opportunity for a hearing and, thus, there was no violation of due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Board's order and remanded the case.
